# Cain Marko — UATU INTELLIGENCE DOSSIER

*Full-existence intelligence briefing. Independent, evidence-based assessment — the benevolent inverse of total surveillance.*


## Executive Brief (BLUF)

# EXECUTIVE BRIEF (BLUF) — SUBJECT: CAIN MARKO

**Classification:** Comprehensive longitudinal subject file, Section 0 of N. Bottom-line-up-front summary for handlers, analysts, and any responder likely to encounter the subject in the field, the bar, or the wreckage.

---

## 0.1 — One-Paragraph Bottom Line

The subject is a chronically traumatized man, arrested in development at the approximate age of his worst paternal beatings, who by cosmic accident was given the body the beaten boy fantasizes about and has never lived a day since outside that armor. Everything about him — the towering frame, the crimson plating, the domed helmet, the sixty-year vendetta against a stepbrother who has repeatedly forgiven him, the bar fights, the drinking, the rare and almost embarrassed acts of tenderness toward children and underdogs, the compulsive reclamation of the Cyttorak gem every time it is taken — is downstream of a single organizing imperative: *never be the smaller body in the room again.* He is not a master criminal. He is not a strategist. He is not, in the clinical sense, a psychopath. He is a child in a mountain of muscle, and the mountain is the defense.

---

## 0.2 — Who The Subject Is At The Deepest Level

Underneath the operator surface — the hulking silhouette, the shaved skull under the helmet, the brutish heavy-browed face, the crimson-and-brown plating — sits a remarkably simple and remarkably damaged structure. Strip away sixty years of property damage, the headlines, the team-ups with Black Tom Cassidy, the brief and humiliating tenures on the side of the angels, and what remains is recognizably the same person across every era: an angry, frightened, comparatively unloved stepson, who learned in early childhood that (a) larger bodies hurt smaller bodies, (b) the man hurting him preferred the smaller, gentler boy standing next to him, and (c) no adult was coming. The Juggernaut identity is the architectural solution to those three facts. The body solves (a). The vendetta against Charles solves (b) by inverting the power gradient. The refusal to trust authority, the long silences, the bar-stool isolation, solve (c) by preempting the disappointment.

At the deepest level, the subject is a **defense mechanism wearing a man**. The somatization is unusually literal — most patients with this structure carry it psychically; he carries it as eight feet of mystical mass and a helmet that physically blocks the one route by which someone might reach the interior. He is the cleanest case in the available record of a psyche that has succeeded in making itself unreachable, and is therefore also the cleanest case of a psyche that cannot be helped without first being penetrated against its will — which is precisely the experience he has organized his entire adult life to prevent.

---

## 0.3 — The Through-Line Of His Entire Existence

A single sentence covers it: **he keeps trying to stop being the smaller body, and he keeps failing, and he keeps reaching for the gem.**

Expanded, the through-line traces a recurring four-beat cycle visible across every decade of the file:

1. **Loss or humiliation.** Something contests the unstoppability — a Sentinel that outclasses him (Nimrod), an entity that tears the helmet off (Onslaught), a writer who strips the gem (Bunn run, Sins of Sinister), a stepbrother whose telepathy or moral standing makes him feel small. The original wound is reactivated.
2. **Withdrawal and quiet.** He goes to ground. Construction work. A bar. A safehouse with Tom. A sober interval. Real, sometimes lengthy, never structurally stable.
3. **Provocation.** Either an old grievance surfaces (Xavier, in any form) or the powerlessness itself becomes unbearable. He reaches for the power again — the gem, the hammer, the deal, the fight.
4. **Destruction, then contrition or numbness.** A city, a building, a relationship. Afterward, sometimes a flicker of grief; more often, the bar.

He has never broken this cycle. He has interrupted it — the Sammy Paré period, the Bunn-run sobriety, the X-Men membership — but the interruptions are interludes, not exits. The through-line is not malevolence. The through-line is a man who cannot live as himself and cannot live as the armor, oscillating between them forever.

---

## 0.4 — The Core Wound And Its Maintenance

**The wound.** Kurt Marko, atomic researcher, second husband to Sharon Xavier, beat his biological son Cain and privately favored his stepson Charles. The wound is not the beatings alone — beatings are common in the case literature and produce a wide range of outcomes. The wound is the **combination**: physical violence delivered by the only available father figure, paired with the visible, daily evidence that the same man was capable of tenderness, was simply withholding it, and was bestowing it on the smaller boy in the next room. This converts straightforward abuse trauma into something more corrosive — a comparison wound, a worthiness wound — and it is the comparison, not the violence, that has never healed.

A secondary deposit was laid down in adolescence and young adulthood: the laboratory fire in which Kurt died (and which Cain, in some tellings, did nothing to stop) gave the subject his first taste of the relief of *not rescuing*, and gave him a piece of unprocessed guilt that he now carries as flat affect. The Korean War desertion added a third layer — the experience of being, under combat stress, exactly the coward his father told him he was. The Cyttorak gem, found in flight from that shame, was grasped without hesitation precisely because it offered to invert every previous data point at once.

**Maintenance — the active conditions that keep the wound from healing.**

- *The helmet.* Functional — it blocks telepathy. Symbolic — it ensures no one can reach the interior child. As long as it is on, the wound is preserved intact because nothing can get to it to metabolize it.
- *The body.* Pain feedback is degraded by sixty years of being hit by Thor and the Hulk without injury. The body no longer teaches caution, and it no longer teaches grief. The subject cannot feel his way to his own wound because the somatic channel is anesthetized.
- *The alcohol.* Whatever pharmacology applies to a body of his density, the *behavior* is reliable: drink to dull affect, drink alone after loss, drink socially with Tom. Alcohol forecloses the introspective window that would otherwise open in down-cycles.
- *The vendetta.* Charles Xavier is the wound's externalization. As long as there is a living surrogate for Kurt to attack, the subject does not have to face that the actual perpetrator is dead and out of reach. The vendetta is grief-avoidance dressed as hatred.
- *The cyclical depowering and repowering.* Every loss of the gem reactivates the original helplessness; every reclamation re-armors against it. The cycle itself is the wound's life-support system.
- *The refusal of sincere offers.* Xavier has, repeatedly and across decades, offered reconciliation in good faith. Each refusal preserves the structure. Acceptance would require the subject to live without the organizing grievance, and he does not know who he is without it.

The wound is, in this sense, **self-maintaining** — every defense the subject deploys to manage it has the side effect of keeping it fresh.

---

## 0.5 — Operational Summary

**Threat profile.** Catastrophic on the physical axis; modest on the strategic axis. The subject is a weapon, not a planner. Maximum recorded output: city-leveling (Las Vegas, Fear Itself, under Kuurth amplification). Baseline output: structural demolition, mass-casualty risk in any sustained engagement, near-immunity to conventional kinetic and energy weapons, momentum that cannot be stopped by physical means once initiated. He does not stop. He runs out of targets.

**Engagement modes — three, mutually exclusive in any first encounter, determined within roughly thirty seconds:**

1. **Surrogate-target mode** (triggered by: authority claims, moral condescension, mention of or proximity to Charles Xavier, telepathic contact attempts, mockery touching size or worth). Outcome: immediate verbal escalation, near-vertical climb to physical violence, no plateau, no self-de-escalation.
2. **Peer/companion mode** (triggered by: Black Tom, recognized fellow ex-cons, bartenders he has known a long time, anyone who treats him as a man and not as a phenomenon). Outcome: loyalty, banter, willingness to defer, capacity for grief, surprisingly good company.
3. **Protector mode** (triggered by: visible bullying of a smaller party, children in obvious distress, mutant kids who remind him of Sammy Paré). Outcome: identification, intervention on the underdog's behalf, willingness to sustain damage to prevent harm to the protected party.

**Pressure points — exploit only with full awareness of the escalation cost.**

- *Telepathic intrusion:* the most effective tactical lever; also the most dangerous, because successful intrusion produces apocalyptic retaliation if it fails to incapacitate.
- *Depowering / size reduction:* tactically decisive in the short term; produces the most psychologically destabilized version of the subject in the medium term — a frightened, sober, dangerous man without his armor is in some ways more volatile than the armored version.
- *Comparison to Charles:* never use as a deliberate provocation; the escalation outpaces the value.
- *Threats to chosen kin:* removes prosocial anchors; subject becomes more dangerous, not less. Avoid.

**Approach vectors — for any operator attempting de-escalation, recruitment, or sustained contact:**

- Low-demand, non-evaluative kindness from a party that wants nothing is the only lever with a positive track record. It has produced every documented period of reform. It cannot be faked — the subject reads insincerity quickly and routes it to surrogate-target mode.
- Honest work, physical labor, the company of a small number of trusted equals, distance from the stepbrother, abstinence from alcohol — these are the conditions under which the subject has been stable. None of them are conditions the subject can sustain unaided.
- The helmet must be respected as non-negotiable in any negotiation. Asking him to remove it is asking him to open the wound; he will not do it, and the request itself is taken as hostile.

**Probability assessment — durable reform.** Low, on present evidence. Not zero. The subject has demonstrated the capacity for every prerequisite — attachment (Tom), protection (Sammy), grief, shame, sober work, voluntary alignment with prosocial cause. He has never assembled the prerequisites simultaneously for long enough to set. The intervention that has not yet been tried, across sixty years of file, is one that addresses the wound directly rather than its symptoms — and the subject has structured his body, his armor, and his social world specifically to prevent that intervention.

**Bottom line.** Treat as: a Category-1 physical threat with a Category-3 strategic profile and a Category-1 psychological vulnerability under the helmet. Approach as: a man, not a phenomenon. Never as the boy he was, and never as the stepbrother of anyone. Address him as Cain — never as Marko, which is the father's name and the original wound's surname — and expect, on a good day, to be surprised by who answers.


## Chronology I — Origin & Childhood

# CHRONOLOGY I — ORIGIN & CHILDHOOD

*Subject: MARKO, Cain. File segment: pre-pubertal through late adolescence, ending at conscription. Sources: X-Men #12 (Lee/Kirby, March 1965, foundational); Uncanny X-Men #'s touching the Marko household across the Claremont era; X-Men Unlimited #12 (1996, Nicieza, "A Cain Is Able" expanded backstory); Chuck Austen, Uncanny X-Men #410–443 (2002–2004, retrospective monologues by the subject during his X-Men tenure, particularly the Sammy Paré arc); Cullen Bunn, Juggernaut (2020) #1–5 (subject's own narration in AA-style first person, the cleanest primary self-report on file); recurring flashbacks across Excalibur, X-Men Forever, and the various Onslaught tie-ins.*

---

## 1.1 BIRTH AND PROVENANCE

The subject is recorded as born **Cain Marko**, in upstate New York, to **Dr. Kurt Marko** (atomic researcher, US government contractor, later director of the **Alamogordo** nuclear test facility in New Mexico) and a mother who is **almost entirely absent from the documentary record.** No name is preserved across the canon; no photograph survives in any flashback panel; the subject in adult life never invokes her in dialogue except by implication ("my old man," never "my parents"). Whether she died in childbirth, abandoned the household, or was driven out by Kurt is unestablished — and the *absence of the question* in the subject's adult speech is itself a data point. He does not wonder about her aloud. The maternal slot is unfilled and apparently un-mourned, which in clinical practice usually indicates a loss so early or so chronically denied that the grief work was never initiated.

Kurt Marko remarried — to **Sharon Xavier**, widow of **Dr. Brian Xavier** (also a nuclear physicist, Kurt's colleague and, per longstanding implication first laid in X-Men #12 and made explicit in later retcons, possibly murdered by Kurt to acquire both his wife and his estate). Sharon brought to the marriage a son, **Charles Francis Xavier**, several years younger than Cain, frail, brilliant, latently telepathic. The marriage relocated the household to the **Xavier mansion in Westchester County**, the same building that becomes, in adult chronology, the Xavier School. The geographical detail is operationally important: the subject grew up in the house his stepbrother would later inherit, in the rooms that would later become classrooms, on the grounds where as an adult he would surface from a tunnel dug from Asia for the express purpose of breaking down the front door.

Date of birth is not pinned in canon. By Korean War conscription (1950–1953) the subject is an adolescent/young adult of draft age; working backward this places birth in the **late 1920s to mid-1930s** in original publication continuity, sliding-timescale-adjusted in later runs. For UATU purposes the precise year is less material than the developmental sequence: **Kurt's first marriage and Cain's birth predate the Xavier remarriage by enough years that Cain was an established only child** — accustomed to the entire (hostile) attention of his father — before Charles entered the home. The arrival of Charles is therefore not merely the introduction of a sibling but the **displacement of the subject from his only known position**, even if that position was a battered one.

## 1.2 KURT MARKO — PERPETRATOR PROFILE

Every available datum on Kurt Marko is consistent with a **chronically abusive, narcissistically injured, occupationally high-status man**. He was a credentialed scientist, professionally respected, in the photograph the subject has been shown holding across multiple flashbacks (X-Men Unlimited #12 establishes the framed-photo motif) standing in a lab coat with a clipboard. The respectability is part of the file: Kurt's violence was domestic and invisible, the violence of a man whose external world treated him as competent and whose internal world apparently could not tolerate witnesses to that competence's limits.

The recurring behavioral pattern, established in flashback across nearly every Cain-centric arc:

- **Physical beatings of Cain**, frequent enough to be a routine of the household rather than a series of incidents. The subject has described, in adult monologue (Austen run, Uncanny #421 area), being struck "for breathing wrong" — a phrase that, whether literal or compressed memory, communicates the **arbitrary-trigger character** of the abuse. There was no rule set. The child could not modify behavior to avoid the violence. This is the developmental substrate for adult-life learned helplessness about provocation: the subject does not believe, at a deep level, that any modification of his conduct ever prevents pain.
- **Verbal denigration**, particularly comparative. Cain was told he was stupid, weak, a disappointment, *unlike Charles.* The explicit invidious comparison is the most psychologically toxic feature of the household and is referenced by the subject more often in adulthood than the physical beatings themselves.
- **Differential treatment of Charles**, ranging from open affection to (in some tellings) protection from Kurt's own violence — a household in which Cain was visibly beaten in front of a stepbrother who was visibly not. The subject witnessed his abuser's *capacity for tenderness*, deployed elsewhere, and could not access it.
- **Possible escalation toward Charles** in the period immediately preceding Kurt's death — implied in X-Men #12 and elaborated later: at some point Kurt began to turn on Charles as well, which is when the laboratory-fire incident occurs.

Significantly, no canon depicts Kurt striking Cain in Charles's presence and Charles intervening. The two boys' experience of the abuse is **siloed**: Cain absorbs it, Charles is shielded from it (or, by virtue of nascent telepathy, *closes himself off from it*, which the subject in adulthood would experience as the same thing). The lifelong grievance against Charles is built on this silo. Charles, in the subject's organizing memory, did not see and did not stop it.

## 1.3 SHARON XAVIER-MARKO

The stepmother is nearly as absent from the record as the biological mother. She is rendered, in the available flashbacks, as **alcoholic, dissociated, and ineffective** — a woman who had married a violent man for reasons the panels do not investigate and who appears in the kitchen, in the parlor, holding a glass, not intervening. The subject does not record being beaten by her. He does not record being comforted by her either.

The behavioral inheritance is double-edged: **the subject's own adult alcohol use** (documented from the Claremont bar-fight panels forward through the Bunn run's explicit AA framing) maps onto a household in which the adult coping signature he watched was the bottle. He drinks in the same posture his stepmother drank in — alone, in a chair, in silence, working toward affect-blunt. The female-coded adult he watched was not a protector and not an aggressor; she was a sedated bystander, and that template — *the adult who is in the room and does nothing* — is one of two adult templates he had. The other was Kurt.

## 1.4 CHARLES — THE STEPBROTHER AS PROXIMATE WOUND

Charles Xavier enters the household as a younger, smaller, sickly boy with a dead father and a fragile mother. From the subject's vantage at the time of arrival — already a battered older child, already accustomed to the household's hostile baseline — Charles is **the visible evidence that gentleness was possible in this house and had simply been withheld from him.** Every kindness Kurt extended to Charles was, to Cain's developing psyche, a kindness *taken from* Cain.

The early bullying is documented in flashback as **physical and verbal, sustained over years, with private cruelty alternating with public denial**. The subject pushed Charles down stairs, took his belongings, threatened him in private and presented neutrally in front of adults. The pattern is textbook: it is the behavior of a child who has learned that aggression toward an even smaller target is the only available discharge for an affect the larger world prohibits him from directing upward.

Critically — and this is the data point that most cleanly distinguishes the subject from a pure antisocial profile — **Charles's developing telepathy made the bullying ineffective in the usual way.** Charles could feel Cain's misery. The subject became aware, gradually then suddenly, that his stepbrother *knew* he was hurting and *knew why*, and was witnessing the interior of him without permission. The childhood discovery of Charles's telepathy is, in the adult file, **the origin of the subject's entire architecture around mental privacy** — the helmet, the rage at being "read," the refusal to be psychologically known. The wound is not "Charles reads minds." The wound is "Charles read mine while I was beating him for being read."

This is the developmental moment that locks the relationship into permanent unresolvability. The subject cannot reconcile with Charles because reconciliation would require being seen, and being seen is precisely what he organized his entire adult identity to prevent.

## 1.5 THE LABORATORY FIRE

In adolescence, an explosion at Kurt Marko's laboratory facility. Kurt is mortally injured. In the canonical telling (X-Men #12, reinforced by Unlimited #12), Kurt with his dying breath **asks Cain to look after Charles**, and in some readings reveals or implies the truth of Brian Xavier's death. The subject's response, depending on telling, ranges from **passive non-rescue** (he does not pull his father from the fire) to **active refusal** (he watches Kurt die and does not attempt aid).

The behavioral data is what matters: the subject was offered, at the deathbed, the one act that could have re-narrated his entire childhood — *I saved the man who hurt me; I am better than him.* He did not take it. He let the man die and walked out. This is not the moral failure it is sometimes read as in-universe; it is, developmentally, the most coherent act available to him. A child who has been beaten without rules does not develop the rescue reflex. He develops the witnessing reflex. He watches the harm finish.

But the deathbed instruction — *look after Charles* — was internalized in inverted form. The subject did not protect Charles. He instead, for the rest of his life, treats Charles as the locus of grievance, as if the dying instruction had transmitted *Charles is the one who took everything from you* rather than *Charles is your responsibility now.* The misreading is consistent with disorganized attachment: the last word of the abuser becomes the operating instruction, but interpreted through the lens of the abuse, not the lens of its content.

## 1.6 ADOLESCENCE — POST-FIRE, PRE-KOREA

The years between Kurt's death and conscription are the sparsest in the documentary record. What is preserved:

- The household, with Kurt removed, became a **two-stepbrother arrangement under Sharon's distant supervision**, in the same Westchester mansion. The asymmetry of resources and affection persisted: Charles was the brilliant student, on the academic track that would lead to Oxford; the subject was understood within the household as the troubled older boy.
- **Bullying of Charles continued**, possibly intensified, now without even the structuring presence of Kurt's violence as a containing context. The wound had no longer a fresh source; the displacement onto Charles became more clearly self-sustaining.
- The subject's **physical size** developed rapidly. By late adolescence he was large, strong, locally formidable — the body that would, even pre-Cyttorak, support combat conscription. The body-as-defense pattern begins here, *before* the gem: the subject was already organizing himself around being too big to hit. The Cyttorak transformation later would not invent this pattern; it would only complete it.
- **Academic failure** is implied across the record. The subject does not, in adult life, deploy the vocabulary or reference frame of an educated man. He is not stupid — the Claremont-era heist sequences with Black Tom demonstrate situational intelligence — but the *educational* track that was available in the household was the one Charles took, and the subject appears to have refused or been denied it. This is the period in which the cognitive style described in the working psychological profile — concrete, tactical, anti-reflective — sets as the permanent configuration.
- **First substance use** is plausible in this window, modeled on Sharon. No specific canonical scene, but the adult drinking pattern is too established and too stereotyped to have begun in adulthood.
- **No documented adolescent friendships, no documented adolescent romances.** The subject enters the Korean War conscription without any peer attachment on the record. The interpersonal ledger as of age ~18 is: one dead-and-hated father, one absent-and-sedated stepmother, one resented stepbrother, no peers. This is a near-total relational vacuum, and it is the configuration he carried into military service.

## 1.7 EARLIEST STABLE BEHAVIORAL SIGNATURES — INDEX

By the close of the childhood window, the file already shows the following patterns that will persist, unmodified, across the next sixty years of adult chronology:

1. **Displacement of pain downward.** Hit by Kurt, hits Charles. The vector is set.
2. **Non-rescue.** Watches harm conclude. Does not intervene. The deathbed fire is the type-specimen.
3. **Body as defense.** Pre-power physical development is already organized around becoming too large to be struck. The Cyttorak transformation will be experienced, when it arrives, as the *completion* of a project the subject had already begun, which is why he reaches for the gem without hesitation.
4. **Mental privacy as non-negotiable.** Charles's telepathy taught him, before any helmet existed, that being read is the deepest possible violation. The helmet is the second draft of a defense the boy was already building.
5. **Comparison-intolerance.** The Kurt-favors-Charles dynamic establishes that any framing positioning another person as the "better" one will produce immediate destabilization. This will be the lifelong trigger.
6. **Bystander-template alcoholism.** Sharon's chair and glass are the adult posture he will inherit when alone.
7. **Operationalized grievance, retrospective grief.** Anger is the available real-time affect; sadness arrives, if at all, years late and chemically mediated.
8. **Loyalty unavailable, but not impossible.** No childhood friendships exist on record — but the *absence* of a childhood best friend, combined with the later intensity of the Black Tom bond, suggests the capacity was never used, not that it was missing. The Tom relationship in adulthood functions as a *first* peer bond, with the developmental weight a first bond carries.

The childhood file closes with the subject as an adolescent of considerable size, no education to speak of, no peer relationships, a recently dead abusive father whose dying instruction he has misread, a stepmother he has effectively written off, and a stepbrother he hates with a heat disproportionate to anything Charles has done — because Charles is the only available stand-in for a hatred that has nowhere else to go. He is, in this configuration, drafted into the Korean War.

Everything that happens in the cave at Cyttorak happens to a person already fully assembled. The gem does not create the Juggernaut. The childhood does. The gem only gives him the body to match.


## Chronology II — Formation & Emergence

# CHRONOLOGY II — FORMATION & EMERGENCE

*Subject: MARKO, Cain Robert. File continues from Chronology I (Natal & Childhood). Period under review: approx. ages 13 through 22 — i.e., the consolidation of adolescent personality structure under the Marko household, the military induction, the Korean theater, the discovery event at the Temple of Cyttorak, and the post-emergence months culminating in the first hostile transit to North America.*

---

## I. THE LATE MARKO HOUSEHOLD (approx. ages 13–17)

### A. Domestic geometry after Kurt

Following Kurt Marko's death in the laboratory fire (Chronology I, §VII), the household at the Westchester estate contracted to three: Sharon Xavier-Marko in advancing alcoholism; the stepson, Charles, accelerating both academically and telepathically; and the subject, then in the early-to-mid adolescent range, physically already conspicuous — taller than his year-mates by a head, broader through the shoulders, with the heavy supraorbital ridge and squared jaw that would later become the operator-canon profile. School photographs of the period (extrapolated from the estate's later cataloguing) would show him in the back row of every class group, arms folded, gaze askance from the lens — the posture of a body that has learned it photographs as a threat and has stopped trying to soften it.

The functional pattern of the household after Kurt's death was that **no adult was supervising**. Sharon's drinking removed her as an authority before noon most days. Charles, by virtue of intellect and (covert, still-suppressed) telepathy, navigated the house by route-avoidance — knowing without being told which floor the subject was on, and choosing the other one. The subject in turn experienced this avoidance not as the kindness it partly was but as a continuation of the favoritism: *the smaller boy still gets to choose where I am not.*

### B. The first private rituals

This is the period in which several lifelong behavioral signatures consolidate. A total-surveillance file would catalogue:

- **The "circuit walk."** The subject habitually patrolled the perimeter of the Marko property at dusk — a roughly forty-minute loop along the treeline, kicking deadfall, breaking branches against his thigh. This is the earliest somatic version of what later becomes the Juggernaut's forward-motion-as-self-regulation pattern: ambulation under load, low and rhythmic, to discharge an affect he could not name.
- **The shed.** A disused outbuilding near the old greenhouse was converted, without permission, into his own space — a heavy bag improvised from a feed sack and burlap, a bench, a cache of pilfered cigarettes and (by age fifteen) bottles taken in small increments from Sharon's supply such that she would not notice. This is the prototype of every later hideout, every shared apartment with Black Tom: a male-coded enclosure with the door barred from inside, alcohol available, a target to hit.
- **The cellar visit.** Approximately once a fortnight in the months after Kurt's death, the subject would descend to the basement of the main house and stand in the boiler room — the closest interior space to the geometry of Kurt's old laboratory. He did not vandalize it. He did not cry, on any occasion that would later be reconstructable. He stood. This is the earliest form of his **grievance maintenance ritual**: returning to the site of the wound at regular intervals to confirm that it is still there. The adult version of this is the recurrent unprovoked surfacing in Westchester to attack the school; the structure is identical.

### C. Schooling

The subject's academic record in this period is poor but not failing — the file should not record him as unintelligent. He read at grade level, performed adequately in mathematics, and demonstrated, in shop and mechanical drawing, an unusual three-dimensional spatial intuition (later evident in the precision of his demolition trajectories: he does not break things at random; he hits load-bearing members). He failed deportment, repeatedly. The standard incident pattern was: a smaller boy makes a remark; the subject does not engage; a second remark; the subject does not engage; a third; the subject puts the boy through something — a locker, a railing, on one recorded occasion the glass of an interior door. He never struck first. He never struck at the second. He struck at the third, and he struck once.

This is the earliest expression of what the Personality synthesis identifies as the **fairness streak within his own warped code**: a need to be provoked enough to license what he was already going to do. It is also the first reliable evidence that the violence is not impulsive in the clinical sense — it is regulated by an internal threshold, just one set far too low and discharged with disproportionate force.

He was suspended four times in the documented period and expelled once, late in the sequence, after the door-glass incident. He did not return to formal schooling.

### D. The relationship with Charles, terminal-adolescent phase

Three patterns crystallize:

1. **The dining-table silence.** Meals in the Marko house, after Kurt's death and before Sharon's full collapse, were eaten in near-total silence broken only by the subject's chewing, which he performed loudly and with mouth-open contempt as a small daily aggression. Charles ate quickly and excused himself. The subject sometimes remained at table after Charles left, drinking a second glass of milk standing up, watching the door.
2. **The room-line.** The subject established, with no verbal negotiation, that certain rooms (the front parlor, the upper landing, the library after 8 p.m.) were *his* in the evenings, and Charles's during the day. Charles complied. The subject did not interpret compliance as concession; he interpreted it as confirmation of a natural order finally being acknowledged.
3. **The single recorded act of protection.** This is anomalous and important. On one occasion, the subject intervened when a delivery man spoke roughly to Charles at the back door — the subject came around the corner of the house, said nothing, and stood until the man left. He did not look at Charles afterward and did not acknowledge what he had done. This is the earliest data point for the **protector mode** that will later attach to Sammy Paré and others: it is reflexive, non-verbal, and immediately disavowed. It indicates that the wound was never an absence of bond with Charles; it was the corruption of one.

### E. Sharon's death

Sharon Xavier-Marko died in this period (canonically of complications related to her drinking, exacerbated, in the more psychologically detailed retellings, by grief and isolation). The subject's response is not recorded in any flashback as overtly grief-stricken. He attended the funeral. He did not speak. He did not stand near Charles at the graveside. He left the estate within weeks of the funeral and was, for a span of months, off the available record entirely — a period the file should mark as **the first disappearance**, the prototype of every later vanishing between rampages.

When he resurfaced he had enlisted.

---

## II. MILITARY INDUCTION AND PRE-DEPLOYMENT (approx. ages 18–19)

### A. The choice to enlist

The decision was not patriotic. The available evidence — extrapolated from later barroom self-disclosures and from the Bunn-era reflections during his depowered construction-job period — frames the enlistment as a triangulated escape: from the estate, from Charles, from the absence of a structuring authority now that both Kurt and Sharon were gone. The Army offered a **larger man to be hit by**, which is the only configuration in which the subject knew how to function. It also offered a sanctioned outlet for the kind of physicality that civilian life had been punishing him for.

A surveillance file would note the irony that **Charles enlisted too**, in a parallel and slightly later cycle, with the explicit (telepathically informed) intent of watching over his stepbrother. The subject never learned this in any form he accepted. Told it later — and he was told it, more than once, by Charles and by intermediaries — he reframed it as further evidence of Charles's intolerable moral positioning: *even my war was about him.*

### B. Basic training profile

In basic, the subject excelled at exactly what one would predict and failed at exactly what one would predict:

- **Excelled at:** load-bearing marches, obstacle courses, hand-to-hand, marksmanship at close-to-medium range, any task involving the application of raw force to a discrete object.
- **Failed at:** map exercises requiring sustained attention to a second-order representation, any drill requiring him to subordinate his judgment to a peer of equivalent rank, and — critically — the **inspection regime**. He could not tolerate having his person evaluated by a smaller man in a position of authority. Multiple disciplinary actions in the training period stem from his response to NCO inspections: he would stand at attention, jaw set, eyes fixed not on the inspecting officer but slightly above the inspecting officer's head, and refuse to verbally respond to corrections. This is **avoidance of the comparison-frame** — the same defense that later structures his refusals of Xavier's outreach.

He completed basic. The unit he was sent to in Korea, in the Lee/Thomas-original framing modernized in subsequent retellings, was an infantry posting in a sector under heavy and irregular fire.

### C. The deployment with Charles

The deliberately bonded posting — Charles in the same unit, by Charles's engineering — is one of the most psychologically loaded facts in the dossier. The subject's behavior in the unit, during the pre-incident weeks, is reconstructable as follows:

- He acknowledged Charles's presence with the minimum nod required by shared uniform.
- He did not bunk near him; he did not share rations; he did not include him in the small unit-internal circles that form in any deployed infantry company.
- He did, however, **track Charles's location** at all times. Multiple anecdotes from the period (surfaced in later flashbacks) have the subject knowing where Charles was without being told and turning his head in that direction at unexplained intervals. This is the surveillance-target relationship in its earliest form: the wound-figure must be monitored, not approached.
- He drank, in the field, what he could acquire — bartered, scavenged, or won at cards. He played cards well. He won often. He did not always collect.

The unit took casualties. The subject saw bodies — both enemy and his own — and demonstrated, even at this age, the **anhedonic somatic feedback** that will later be amplified by Cyttorak: he did not flinch, did not vomit, did not visibly process. He helped move the dead when ordered. He did not volunteer.

---

## III. THE INCIDENT — DESERTION AND DISCOVERY

### A. The break

The precipitating engagement (the firefight that produced the desertion) is variously described across canon. The consistent elements: the unit was overrun or about to be; the subject was separated from immediate command; Charles was elsewhere in the line; an order to hold or to fall back was unclear or never reached him; and the subject, alone with his own decision for perhaps the first time in his adult life under genuine mortal threat, **ran**.

This is the second great shame-event of his life, after the abandonment of Kurt in the laboratory fire. It rhymes with the first in form: *in a moment requiring action toward another person's preservation, he chose his own removal.* He did not run back to friendly lines. He ran laterally, away from both the engagement and the unit, into terrain.

He would carry this for the rest of his life. He would never speak it accurately. The bravado of the Juggernaut identity — *unstoppable, advancing, unable to be turned* — is in significant part a reaction-formation against the documented fact that in the one moment of his life that asked him to stand, he ran.

### B. The cave

The terrain into which he fled contained, by the canon's chosen geography, the **Temple of Cyttorak** — an extradimensional site of worship to one of the Octessence, embedded in or accessible from a cave system the subject entered while seeking concealment. The progression as a surveillance file would reconstruct it:

1. **Entry under threat.** He went in because he was being shot at, or believed he was; the cave was cover. He had no spiritual or acquisitive intent.
2. **Descent.** The cave system descended further than natural geology would account for. He kept going. He has been asked, later, why he did not stop and wait; he has never had a real answer. The plausible reconstruction is that **forward motion was already his only regulation strategy** and that the deeper he went the more the panic of the firefight discharged itself in the simple metabolic work of walking.
3. **The chamber.** He came into a worked chamber, plainly not natural — masonry, carvings, a great central object. The ruby. The inscription.
4. **The inscription.** *"Whosoever touches this gem shall possess the power of the Crimson Bands of Cyttorak. Henceforth, you who read these words, shall become forever more a human juggernaut."* The subject read at grade level. He read it. He understood it. The behavioral data point is that **he did not hesitate**. He had been running from a man with a rifle; he was offered, in the dark, the promise of never having to run again. He took it.

### C. The transformation

What happened to his body in that chamber is unrecorded from any third-party perspective. The reconstruction available is somatic and visual:

- His mass increased — not gradually over weeks, but in the chamber, in minutes. Bone density, muscle cross-section, height, all augmented past human range.
- His skin coarsened. The features heavied. The face that emerged was recognizably his but exaggerated along the lines his adolescence had already drawn: the brow heavier, the jaw squarer, the neck thickened into the shoulders.
- His clothing did not survive. The crimson-and-brown plating that becomes iconic is, in the older canon, partly mystically conferred and partly later-acquired; in the operator-canon profile, the **domed crimson helmet** in particular is associated with a later acquisition and ritualization, not the initial transformation. In the chamber itself, what emerged was the body — naked, enormous, and his.
- The cave collapsed during or immediately after the transformation. He was sealed in.

### D. The interment

He was underground for a long time. The exact span is canonically vague; the behavioral relevant fact is that **it was long enough for his stepbrother to believe him dead and grieve him**, and long enough for the subject himself to develop the underground-traversal habit that would later define his approach vectors. He did not panic. He could not be hurt. He could not starve in any normal timeframe. He walked.

What he thought about during this interment is not recoverable. What can be inferred from the man who emerged: **he did not use the time to reconsider.** He did not arrive at the surface with a plan for wealth, for conquest, for any of the things a person with that new body could have built. He arrived with one destination. Westchester. Charles.

This is the cleanest evidence in the whole formation period that the Juggernaut identity, from its first instant, was **organized around the wound rather than around the power**. The gem gave him the body. He gave the body its purpose, and the purpose was old.

---

## IV. THE LONG TRANSIT (approx. age 20–22)

### A. The route

The subject traveled from the Korean peninsula to Westchester County, New York, largely by subterranean route — through cave systems, rivers, under-sea trenches in the canon's looser geology — and partly above ground in regions where his appearance could be moved through without immediate military response. This transit took, depending on the telling, a substantial period of months to years. A surveillance file should note that **the transit itself was his apprenticeship in the Juggernaut identity**. He learned, over those months:

- That walls would yield to him before he yielded to them, and to stop turning his head before impact.
- That hunger had become advisory rather than commanding.
- That sleep, when he allowed it, was a discretionary act.
- That human beings, on encountering him, responded with one of three patterns — flight, freeze, or attack — and that the third was rare and never effective. He learned to *expect* the first two and was destabilized by their absence (a fact later exploited by anyone, including Charles, who declined to flee).
- That the body could be hit by things that would kill a man and remain unmoved. This degraded, over the transit period, whatever residual pain-mediated caution his nervous system still possessed. By the time he surfaced in North America, the body no longer taught him anything. The mind was, from then on, the only possible regulator — and the mind had not been trained for the job.

### B. The first violences

The transit produced incidents. None are catalogued with precision in primary canon, but the structural pattern can be reconstructed: villages avoided where possible; obstacles (walls, vehicles, livestock fences) destroyed without ceremony; encountered persons either fled or, in a few cases, attempted to engage and were swatted aside with force that, in his new body, he did not yet calibrate. He killed, during this transit, almost certainly more people than the canon explicitly records, and not from cruelty — from miscalibration. He had a new body and no governor. He was, somatically, an infant in a tank.

The psychological residue of this period is the **baseline indifference to bystander casualty** that characterizes his adult presentation. He did not develop it; he had it before he ever announced himself. Westchester would be the announcement.

### C. The acquisition of the public identity

Somewhere in the late transit — and this is a useful index point — the **costume** consolidated. The crimson-and-brown armored plating, the eventual domed helmet, the public name. The canon distributes the acquisitions across different phases; the operator-canon mandates the look as foundational. The behavioral reading: he chose a presentation that **announced what he was before he arrived**. He did not want to be mistaken for a man who could be reasoned with. He wanted, at the door of the school, to be recognized as inevitability.

The helmet in particular — and the file should be emphatic about this — was a tactical choice that *became* a psychological necessity. He did not initially know it blocked telepathy. He came to suspect it. Charles confirmed it the first time he tried to reach inside the subject's mind and could not. From that moment, the helmet was non-negotiable. **The interior child could not be reached.** Every later loss of the helmet in canon — by Onslaught, by Xavier's tactical strikes, by his own moments of inadvisable removal — produces the same response: catastrophic exposure, identity collapse, a man inside the armor smaller than the armor implies.

---

## V. THE FIRST DEFINING CHOICE AND ITS FALLOUT

### A. The arrival

The subject surfaced in Westchester. He did not approach the school by road. He came up through the ground at or near the property line and **walked**. His arrival on the lawn of the Xavier estate-cum-school is the first event in his career as a public figure. The X-Men, in their first iteration, were the obstacle. They were not the target. **The target was upstairs in the wheelchair he had not yet seen.**

Everything that follows in his canonical career — the decades of recurrence, the dozens of arcs — is a variation on what he did that day. He came back to hurt his brother. He used a body bought with shame to discharge a grievance bought with childhood. He did not ask whether the brother wished to be reconciled. He did not test whether the door would have opened to him in another form. He had organized the new self entirely around the old wound, and he arrived ready to deliver it.

### B. The fallout — what was foreclosed

A surveillance file's function in this section is to mark what the subject **chose against** in this defining act, because the unchosen options remained, faintly, all his life:

- **Not chosen: anonymity.** With his power and his underground habit, he could have lived undetected on any continent. He chose the most public possible re-entry — at the door of the one person whose recognition mattered to him.
- **Not chosen: reconciliation.** Charles believed him dead and would, on any reading of Charles's later behavior, have received him with relief. The subject did not test this. He could not afford the answer to be yes; a yes would unmake the structure he had built.
- **Not chosen: a project.** The body he had could have built — institutions, fortunes, empires. He built none. He hit a school. The poverty of his ambition relative to his power is one of the diagnostic facts of the file: **he is not a man with a plan; he is a man with a wound, executing it.**
- **Not chosen: solitude.** He could have remained in the underground transit indefinitely, alone, unhurt. He did not. He needed the brother to be present for the action to mean anything. This is the most damning evidence that the Juggernaut, from its first hour above ground, was **a relational gesture, not an autonomous identity** — addressed always to Charles, and constituted by Charles's witness.

### C. The fallout — what was set in motion

From this first arrival emerge, in seed form, every later pattern:

1. **The recurrence cycle.** Defeat → withdrawal → reactivation → return to the same door. The subject never, in his subsequent career, attacks Xavier *once*. He attacks always with the implicit promise of returning.
2. **The X-Men as scaffolding.** The roster of mutants between him and Charles becomes, over decades, the matrix through which all his other relationships are mediated — including, eventually, Black Tom (introduced as a partner *outside* the Xavier orbit, the only major bond the subject forms without Charles in the frame).
3. **The helmet doctrine.** Charles having reached inside him telepathically, even briefly, in the first encounters, the helmet becomes inviolable. The interior is sealed. The subject lives, from this point on, inside an armor whose primary function is to prevent the only person who ever knew the boy from finding him again.
4. **The bifurcated self.** Public identity: the Juggernaut, advancing, unstoppable. Private identity: a man who deserted his unit, abandoned his stepfather to a fire, and was never as loved as the smaller boy. The two will, for the rest of the dossier, never integrate. Every later module — the Tom partnership, the Sammy Paré episode, the Worthy regression, the Bunn-era reform, the perpetual oscillation — is a referendum on whether the two selves can be held in the same hand. They cannot.

---

## VI. CLOSING NOTE ON THE FORMATION PERIOD

The window from the late Marko household through the first arrival at Westchester is, in dossier terms, the **load-bearing decade** of the subject's life. Everything earlier (Chronology I) supplies the wound; everything later (Chronologies III onward) supplies the variations. Between them sits this period, in which a beaten adolescent with no adult ego consolidation acquires, by cosmic accident, an indestructible body, and uses it for the only purpose his interior life is organized around: the punishment of a smaller, more-loved brother for a crime committed by a dead man.

Operator note for downstream modules: when this subject appears on any horizon, the file's standing recommendation is to identify **which of his three interpersonal modes** the contact has tripped — surrogate-target, peer/companion, or protector — within the first thirty seconds, because the rest of the interaction will be determined by it. The formation period is the reason the modes exist and the reason they are so rigidly separated. He did not learn to blend them. He was never given the time.

*— End Chronology II. File continues at Chronology III: The Recurrence Decades.*


## Chronology III — The Defining Middle Period

# CHRONOLOGY III — THE DEFINING MIDDLE PERIOD

*Subject: MARKO, CAIN R. — File continues. This section covers the operational middle of the subject's recorded life: the long stretch from the post-Korea reemergence through the Onslaught extraction event and into the years of attempted reform, terminating before the late-period Cyttorak-cycling era. This is the bulk of the longitudinal record. Patterns first observed in childhood and at the Temple of Cyttorak now ossify, are tested, partially break, and reset.*

---

## 1. THE WESTCHESTER MARCH AND THE FIRST DECADE OF X-MEN ENGAGEMENTS

### 1.1 The subterranean transit (post-Korea, pre-X-Men #12)

The single most diagnostically valuable behavior of the subject's young adulthood is what he did *immediately* after acquiring the gem. He did not surface in Seoul. He did not surface in Tokyo, Honolulu, San Francisco, Anchorage, or any of the dozen ports between the cave and the eastern United States where a newly invulnerable man could have established himself in comfort. He walked. Underground, through rock, for a period the canon treats as years, in a straight functional line toward his stepbrother. There are no recorded detours. No documented attempt to contact his mother's estate, the U.S. Army (which would have logged him as a deserter), any surviving relative of Kurt Marko, or any acquaintance from his pre-conscription life. The world was now penetrable as water and he used the new ability for one purpose: to find the smaller boy and hit him.

This is not the behavior of a man who has gained power. It is the behavior of a man who has gained *permission*. The gem did not give him the wish; it gave him the alibi. The wish was decades old.

Tactical note: the transit also tells us something about his cognitive horizon. He did not stop to plan. He did not assemble resources. He did not recruit. He moved forward in a straight line for an enormous duration without revising the objective. Forward motion as cognitive habit, already established before the first surface emergence.

### 1.2 First strike on the Xavier Institute (X-Men #12–13)

The opening engagement establishes the operational template that will recur for forty years.

- **Approach behavior.** Telegraphed, contemptuous, frontal. He announces himself. He does not infiltrate. He breaches the wall rather than the door. Subsequent file entries will record the same preference — when given the choice between any two routes, the subject selects the one that destroys more wall.
- **Target discrimination.** The X-Men are not the target; they are the friction. He addresses Xavier directly, repeatedly, by name and by the diminutive *Charles* even mid-combat. Bystander attacks are reactive rather than initiated.
- **Verbal pattern.** Monologue-heavy. He recites the family history aloud, to an audience of strangers, while fighting. The grievance has to be witnessed; private revenge is insufficient. This need-for-audience persists in every later engagement and is one of the file's more useful behavioral fingerprints.
- **Termination mode.** The fight ends when Xavier's then-new student (the team's telepathically inexperienced Jean Grey contribution, augmented by Xavier) removes the helmet and reaches the interior mind. The subject is neutralized not by force — none of the assembled mutants could match him physically at this stage — but by intrusion into the small body inside the armor. This is the first recorded confirmation of the helmet's true function and the first time the subject experiences, as an adult Juggernaut, the original wound being touched. He does not recover from this lesson; he integrates it. Every subsequent appearance treats the helmet as non-negotiable.

### 1.3 The recurrence pattern (X-Men #13 through the early Roy Thomas / Neal Adams runs)

Across the next several years of file entries the engagements repeat with minor variation:

- The subject is contained — buried, dimensionally displaced, sealed in a structure, on one occasion sent to a "crimson" pocket dimension by Doctor Strange — and then, after a latency of months to years, he returns. The latency is not idleness. It is travel. He is, in each case, walking back.
- The cost of containment is always paid by Xavier or his proxies and the subject knows it. His re-emergence carries the implicit message: *you cannot keep me away from you.* This is, in attachment terms, pursuit behavior. The most parsimonious read is that the subject's hostility toward Xavier is, structurally, a perversion of approach — he cannot tolerate contact, cannot tolerate absence, and resolves the contradiction by approaching violently.

### 1.4 Standalone engagements outside the Xavier orbit

In this same first decade the subject is briefly contracted, manipulated, or coincidentally adjacent to several non-Xavier conflicts (Hulk encounters; minor New York criminal entanglements). The pattern across these is instructive precisely because it differs from the Xavier engagements:

- No monologuing.
- No wall-preference.
- No audience-seeking.
- Faster disengagement when the fight stops being productive.

In other words: when Charles is not on the field, the subject becomes a markedly more rational combatant. The Xavier engagements are not how he fights. They are how he grieves.

---

## 2. THE BLACK TOM CASSIDY ERA — THE LONGEST RELATIONSHIP OF HIS LIFE

### 2.1 Pairing and initial dynamic (X-Men #101–103 and the broader Claremont run, late 1970s)

The Black Tom partnership is the single most important relational data set in the file. It begins as an opportunistic pairing — a contract, mercenary work, a heist — and it does not end. Across the subsequent two decades they share addresses, share funds, share down-time, and treat each other's well-being as a default operational priority. This is not a thieves' alliance of the kind the subject forms with, for example, the various criminal handlers who try to leverage him; this is a domestic partnership in everything but legal designation.

What Tom provides, structurally:

- **No comparison.** Tom is not smaller in the wounding way (he is a powered metahuman in his own right), not morally elevated, not a Xavier. He does not represent the surrogate-target category.
- **Acceptance of hierarchy without contest.** Tom takes the planner role; the subject takes the breach role. Neither tries to dominate the other's lane. The subject, who has never tolerated authority, tolerates Tom's tactical lead because Tom does not frame it as authority.
- **Low emotional demand.** Tom does not ask the subject to narrate his motives, name his feelings, or revisit his history. He does not therapize. The subject, who shuts down under any such demand, blooms in its absence.
- **Shared verbal register.** The bar-talk, the banter, the willingness to be ribbed: with Tom, the subject is observably *lighter*. File reviewers should note this. It is the closest thing in the record to baseline temperament uncontaminated by trauma signature.

### 2.2 Specific micro-pattern observations from the Tom years

- **Drinking pattern shifts.** With Tom, alcohol intake is social, paced, conversational. Alone, in the same period, intake is heavier and more silent. The substance is the same; the function is different. Tom is a partial substitute for the bottle.
- **Sleep and quarters.** Apartments shared by the two across the period are consistently small, working-class, urban — not the lairs of a man with delusions of empire. The subject's housing choices, when not coerced by circumstance, are domestic. He likes a couch, a television, a fridge. The Juggernaut shell collapses inside the apartment door.
- **Grief response.** Each of the several occasions on which Tom is apparently killed (Muir Island, X-Tinction Agenda adjacencies, the various Claremont/post-Claremont attrition events) produces from the subject not merely rage but observable derangement — the only situations in the file other than the small-body wound itself in which his behavior becomes incoherent rather than escalatory. He has been recorded sitting with a body. He has been recorded refusing food. The depressive register, normally unavailable in real time, becomes available here.
- **Defense of Tom against external comment.** The subject does not tolerate mockery of Tom by third parties. In several recorded altercations the trigger for disproportionate violence is a sneer at Tom, not a sneer at himself. This is, in clinical terms, displaced self-defense — but it also demonstrates that he experiences Tom's dignity as continuous with his own.

### 2.3 Operational note

For the entirety of the Tom period the subject's crime portfolio is *acquisitive* rather than retaliatory — bank jobs, art theft, contract muscle, geographic mobility. This is the only span in his life where Juggernaut activity is economically rational rather than psychodynamically driven. The correlation is too clean to ignore: when the chosen-kin attachment is active, the small-body wound recedes from operational priority, and behavior normalizes toward ordinary criminality. When the attachment is severed or threatened, the Xavier-shaped wound resurfaces and the behavior re-pathologizes.

This is the strongest argument in the file against any constitutional reading of the subject's hostility. The hostility is contingent. It has a switch.

---

## 3. THE NIMROD ENCOUNTER (UNCANNY X-MEN #194, 1985)

A single-issue event but a high-value behavioral data point. Confronted with a future Sentinel that genuinely matched and exceeded his durability, the subject's response was, in sequence:

1. Initial disbelief — repeated forward charges into a target that did not yield.
2. Visible confusion — the body had not previously failed to resolve a situation.
3. Frank fear, expressed verbally.
4. Appeal to teamwork — specifically, an appeal to X-Men present on the field, including his stepbrother's students, framed in pragmatic rather than ideological terms.
5. Tactical withdrawal.

The diagnostic content is that steps 3 and 4 happened at all. Under sufficient threat the antisocial presentation thins out and an underlying social organism becomes visible. He will accept help. He will admit fear. He will name a peer relationship in real time. The bravado is, as previously assessed, brittle, and the Nimrod encounter is the cleanest single-event demonstration in the canon.

A secondary observation: after the encounter the subject did not seek revenge on Nimrod, did not pursue the Sentinel program, and did not incorporate the experience into his standing grievance set. Fear-events, unlike shame-events, are filed and forgotten. Only humiliation accumulates.

---

## 4. THE MUIR ISLAND / INFERNO / ACTS OF VENGEANCE PERIPHERY (late 1980s)

Across the late Claremont period the subject appears repeatedly in the Muir Island orbit — sometimes as Tom's plus-one, sometimes as a contracted asset, sometimes as collateral. Notable from these appearances:

- **Sustained tolerance of Moira MacTaggert.** A telepath-adjacent, morally serious, X-aligned scientist who would, on the Xavier template, trigger the surrogate-target response — and largely does not, because she does not condescend and does not invite comparison. The subject is observably wary around her, occasionally hostile, but does not escalate. He recognizes the type without firing the reflex. This refines our model: the trigger is not "Xavier-aligned authority" in general, but specifically the comparative-favor dynamic of a sibling figure with the moral high ground.
- **Acts of Vengeance recruitment.** Like many street-level Marvel villains he was approached during the cross-villain reshuffle and slotted into various targeted operations. Documented behavior: bored compliance, low investment, no ideological alignment with any of the principals. He is not a joiner. He is a contractor with a partner, and the partnership is the only durable loyalty.

---

## 5. THE EXILES INTERLUDE AND ASSORTED COSMIC DETOURS

A category of events worth flagging only briefly: the subject is, periodically across this middle period, displaced into dimensions, futures, alternate Earths, or temporal pockets (by Strange, by Cyttorak's whims, by the various crossover engines of the era). These episodes share a common signature: he behaves, in the alternate context, *exactly as he behaves at home*. He does not reinvent. He does not seize the opportunity for a fresh identity. Stripped of his original grievance set and offered new ones, he simply waits to return.

This is consistent with the previously noted cognitive style: present-focused, non-narrative. He does not imagine himself differently because he does not imagine himself at all. He is what is happening to him.

---

## 6. THE ONSLAUGHT EXTRACTION EVENT (1996) — THE CENTRAL TRAUMA OF THE MIDDLE PERIOD

This is the file's single most important event after the Cyttorak transformation itself.

### 6.1 The event

Onslaught — a psionic entity born of repressed material from Xavier's own mind, with additional Magneto substrate — sought the dormant Cyttorak essence inside the subject. He did not negotiate for it. He tore the helmet off, reached in, and extracted the power directly, leaving a man-sized residue of Cain Marko in a collapsed posture on the ground.

Every component of this event is a literalization of the subject's worst structural fears, in sequence:

1. **A psionic entity born of Xavier's mind.** The stepbrother, with the boundaries off, finally reaching all the way in.
2. **Helmet removal by force.** The non-negotiable shield, removed without his consent.
3. **Extraction through the head.** The route of intrusion is exactly the route the helmet existed to block.
4. **Reduction to small-body state.** The defended-against outcome, achieved instantly.
5. **Public witness.** He is left visible in this state, in front of combatants on both sides.

There is no other event in the file that combines so many of the subject's specific vulnerabilities into a single sequence. It is structurally the original beating, replayed at scale, with Xavier's mind as the proximal instrument.

### 6.2 Behavior immediately after

He does not seek revenge on Onslaught in any tactical sense. He withdraws. He goes silent. He is, in subsequent appearances within the same crossover, peripheral — a man recovering from a wound he cannot describe, in the presence of people he cannot bring himself to ask for help.

This is significant. The reflexive response — retaliation, displacement, escalation — does not fire. The injury was *too direct.* When the wound is touched at its actual location, the defensive architecture cannot route around it; it goes offline. The subject becomes briefly inert.

### 6.3 Sequelae across the late 1990s

For roughly the rest of the decade the file records a man functioning at reduced amplitude. The power eventually returns (Cyttorak does not surrender his avatar so easily), but the subject's confidence in the shell is permanently downgraded. He drinks more. He fights less, and less decisively. The Tom partnership reasserts itself as the primary stabilizer. There is no period in the file with a higher density of self-isolating behavior outside of the late-period depowerings.

The Onslaught event is, in the longitudinal record, the proof-of-concept for what depowering means to the subject. Every subsequent loss of the gem reactivates this template.

---

## 7. THE X-MEN TENURE (UNCANNY X-MEN, AUSTEN ERA, 2002–2004)

### 7.1 Recruitment and the offered chair

Xavier extends an invitation. The subject accepts. The decision itself is the data point: at no prior moment in the file would acceptance have been possible. Three contributing conditions:

- Onslaught had punctured the omnipotence narrative. The shell no longer felt sufficient.
- Tom was, in this stretch, unavailable as a daily anchor.
- The invitation was, by the subject's standards, low-demand. Xavier did not ask for apology, conversion, or narrative.

The acceptance is not reform. It is exhaustion that resembles reform.

### 7.2 Daily-life observations from the mansion period

This is, for the file, an unprecedented documentation density. For roughly two years the subject lived in a residential community of people whose business was observation. Patterns observable:

- **Spatial behavior.** He chose rooms at the edges of the residential wing, on the ground floor, with external egress. Avoided the upper floors. Avoided the basement War Room except when summoned. The placement is consistent with a man who needs to be able to leave without seeing anyone first.
- **Refectory behavior.** Took meals at off-peak hours when feasible. When forced into the group meal, sat at the end of the table with his back to a wall. Ate quickly. Did not initiate conversation but responded if directly addressed by students; was markedly less responsive to staff.
- **Training-area behavior.** Used the gym in the early morning, alone. Did not enter the Danger Room without explicit operational reason. The reluctance to enter simulated combat unprovoked is consistent with the broader observation that he does not, when undriven, seek violence; he metabolizes existing violence.
- **Verbal register with the team.** Blunt, transactional, occasionally dryly humorous in a way other team members appeared not to expect. The blunt-and-dry register is the subject's most relaxed mode and its presence on team operations indicates that the X-Men tenure produced genuine, if shallow, social comfort.
- **Refusal of telepathic contact.** Helmet worn at all times in mixed company including all team training. The non-negotiability of the helmet was respected by Xavier without comment, which is itself a tactical concession of considerable weight — and one that the subject almost certainly noted.

### 7.3 The Sammy Paré bond

A young mutant, bullied for his appearance and his powers, attaches himself to the subject. The subject does not deflect the attachment. He permits it, then reciprocates it, then defends it.

This is the protector-mode relational template in its purest documented form. The components map exactly:

- Sammy is smaller.
- Sammy is hit by larger things.
- Sammy is not loved by his father.

The subject, in adopting a paternal stance toward Sammy, is performing the **symbolic undoing** previously assessed: he is being to Sammy the man Kurt Marko was not to him. The bond is not strategic, not exploitative, not narratively self-aggrandizing. It is private, low-volume, and consistent. He walks the boy to and from places. He sits with him in public spaces in a way that makes clear to onlookers that interference will be costly. He listens — and *listening* is, in the file, almost an unprecedented behavior.

### 7.4 Sammy's murder and the collapse

Sammy is killed (a Church of Humanity-aligned attack, the era's anti-mutant violence). The subject's response is, in sequence:

1. Stillness — a documented period of non-response that worried the team.
2. Departure from the mansion without notification.
3. A retaliatory engagement conducted with markedly less of the usual monologuing — quiet, fast, lethal-adjacent violence.
4. Return, partial.
5. Gradual drift back to old patterns.

The destabilization is total but the regression is gradual. He does not, in the immediate aftermath, attack Charles. The bond with Sammy was attached to Charles by proximity, and grief is not yet routed through the surrogate-target circuitry. That routing reasserts itself slowly across the following months.

The Sammy arc is the file's strongest single piece of evidence that the subject is capable of non-exploitative attachment, capable of grief, capable of behaving in the parental role he was never given. It is also the file's strongest evidence that he cannot hold those capacities under stress without external scaffolding. The mansion provided the scaffolding. When the mansion's promises proved insufficient — when a child under his protection was killed inside the X-aligned world — the scaffolding lost its credibility, and the older architecture reasserted.

### 7.5 The arc's terminal pattern

The subject does not formally leave the X-Men so much as he stops being one. The transition is gradual, attended by drinking, by a return to old contacts, and ultimately by a reactivation of the Tom partnership when Tom returns to circulation. He carries Sammy as a private grievance for years afterward. He does not name the boy often. When he does, it is not in monologue. It is short, terminal, and the conversation is over.

---

## 8. THE INTER-RUN INTERSTICES — DRINKING, DRIFTING, AND THE FIRST DEPOWERING PRESSURES

Across the years bracketing the X-Men tenure (the late 1990s through the late 2000s) the file records a man cycling between three operational states:

- **With Tom.** Functional crime; pub life; manageable affect; rare contact with the Xavier orbit.
- **Alone, powered.** Mercenary contracts; bar fights; periodic disproportionate violence triggered by ambient provocation; alcohol intake elevated.
- **Alone, depowered or partially depowered.** (Cyttorak's investment fluctuates throughout this period as the entity tests its avatar.) In these stretches the subject's anxiety baseline rises sharply. Sleep degrades. He becomes more careful in motion, then more reckless verbally, as if compensating for the body with the voice. He picks fights he could have avoided. He loses some.

The recurrence of the depowering pressure across this middle period is what prepares the ground for the late-period reform arcs. The body is no longer reliably his. The shell that the boy built is becoming a leaky shelter. The behavioral consequence is that the subject begins, intermittently, to look for other shelters — chosen kin, work, occasional sobriety — without ever yet committing to any of them.

---

## 9. THE FEAR ITSELF AMPLIFICATION (2011)

The middle period closes, for the purposes of this section, with the Asgardian hammer event. Offered a weapon designated for a "Worthy" — a hammer named Kuurth, Breaker of Stone — the subject was elevated to a destructive scale beyond even the Cyttorak baseline.

The diagnostic content is what he did with it.

He went to Las Vegas.

He did not march on Westchester. He did not target Xavier. He did not pursue any standing grievance. He did not assemble a faction. He did not pursue wealth, territory, or any acquisitive end. He went to a city of bright lights and broke it.

This is the most important behavioral observation of the late middle period. **Given unlimited power with no contingency, the subject's default operating mode is destruction without object.** The grievance against Charles is, it turns out, *containing*. It gives the rage a vector. Without the vector — when the power is sufficient that no vector is required — the rage discharges as undirected demolition. The Vegas rampage is the rage in its underlying form: a child's tantrum at planetary scale, in a place chosen because it was loud and it was bright and someone else built it.

It is worth noting what he did *not* do during the amplification, again:

- He did not kill systematically.
- He did not target the children's areas of the city preferentially or avoid them with any documented consistency; the casualties were architectural rather than selected.
- He did not speak much. The monologuing reflex, normally inseparable from Xavier-adjacent violence, was absent. There was no audience worth the speech, because the speech was for one audience and that audience was not present.

After the hammer was removed, the subject reverted with observable shame — not articulated, but visible in the post-event withdrawal, the absence of bragging, the refusal to discuss what he had done even with T


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# CHRONOLOGY IV — RECENT HISTORY & CURRENT STATE

*Covering roughly the last decade of recorded activity: the post-Fear Itself contrition, the 2018 *Damnation* interlude, the 2020 Bunn solo run and its construction-site aftermath, the *Sins of Sinister*-adjacent power churn, and the present-tense disposition of the subject as of the most recent confirmed sightings.*

---

## 1. THE POST-WORTHY DECADE — DRIFT, RETRENCHMENT, SHRINKAGE

The most reliable hinge in the recent file is **Las Vegas**. The subject's tenure as Kuurth, Breaker of Stone (Fear Itself, 2011) ended with a city in ruins and — critically — with the subject himself present, in his own skin, when the smoke cleared. He saw what the unbraked version of his power did to a civilian skyline. The behavioral data from the immediate post-Worthy years (loose appearances across *Amazing X-Men*, *Thunderbolts*, the various *Avengers vs. X-Men* tie-in pages) reads as a man **fundamentally rattled by his own ceiling**. Public appearances become less frequent. Heists with Black Tom dry up almost completely — Tom's own arc carries him toward the X-Men adjacency, and the long pair-bond is, for the first sustained period since the late 1970s, *operationally idle*.

This is the era in which the subject begins **shrinking his own footprint**. He stops contesting territory. He stops surfacing in major super-criminal lineups. The Hood's organized-crime cartel, which absorbed most C- and B-tier muscle in this period, never reliably retains him — every recorded recruitment attempt ends within a single arc. The pattern is not reform; it is **withdrawal**. Crucial distinction: he is not seeking the good, he is conserving the bad. A man who has hit his maximum, did not like the view, and has been quietly trying to spend less time near the lever ever since.

Domestically, the subject in this period is documented in low-rent motels along the I-15 and I-40 corridors, in single-room residences in the older parts of Bayonne, NJ (a quietly persistent geographic anchor across decades — proximity to docks, proximity to Catholic infrastructure he does not use but recognizes, proximity to a class of bar he can drink in without being asked questions), and in periodic stints at Tom's various rural Irish-American safehouses in upstate New York and the New Jersey Pine Barrens. Sleep cycle is irregular but trending toward genuine somatic exhaustion — a man whose body is finally registering that something is wrong, even if it cannot be hurt in the usual sense.

## 2. *DAMNATION* (2018) — THE LAS VEGAS RETURN

In the *Doctor Strange: Damnation* event, Las Vegas is resurrected by Mephisto as a hell-city, and a strike team is assembled to retake it. The subject is pulled into the orbit of the rebuilt city — the city *he leveled*. The data point is small but psychologically heavy: he chooses to be there. There is no operational reason he must be. He is in the geography of his own worst act, walking it on foot, and the file notes that for the first time in the public record he is seen praying — not in any liturgical sense, but the unmistakable behavior of a large man standing alone on a sidewalk where a building used to be, with his hands at his sides and his head down. He does not speak about it afterward. He does not need to.

The 2018 interval establishes the **return-to-the-site-of-harm** behavior that the 2020 Bunn series picks up and formalizes.

## 3. THE BUNN *JUGGERNAUT* RUN (2020) — THE CONSTRUCTION JOB

This is the most important recent-era document in the file and the section to which every subsequent inference must be tethered.

**Depowering.** Cyttorak strips the subject substantially (not entirely — residuals remain; he is still abnormally durable, still abnormally strong by human standards, but the towering scale and the unstoppability are gone, and crucially the helmet is gone). The deity's stated grievance is that the subject was insufficiently destructive. Read clinically: the cosmic patron of his somatic defense has fired him for *being too restrained*. This is, by any measure, a humiliating and clarifying communication.

**The job.** He takes work with a New York demolition-and-construction outfit.
