Capable of deliberately setting aside an impulse for a stated period when the motivation is sufficient — has held off on confronting Charles when Black Tom has asked him to, has restrained himself in X-Men team contexts during the Austen tenure. The capacity exists. The duration is short and the threshold is low.

### 16. Affiliation

The Black Tom bond is the textbook example. Genuine companionate attachment without sexual or strategic component, sustained across decades, durable through separation, mourned in loss. The defense is real; it is also narrow — he runs it with exactly one peer at any given time, and the loss of that one peer is destabilizing precisely because the channel does not generalize.

### 17. Humor

Present, lower-register, mostly with Black Tom. Dry, blunt, often self-deprecating about his own size or appetite. This is the most underused mature defense in the file; the capacity exceeds the deployment by an order of magnitude. In a different life, with a different upstream, the subject would have been a notably funny man.

### 18. Anticipation

Nearly absent. The forward-motion architecture of his cognition actively suppresses anticipation; he does not pre-feel future losses and therefore does not prepare for them. This is the defense whose underdevelopment costs him the most, because every loss arrives without buffer.

---

## IV. COMPENSATORY MECHANISMS (THE LIFE-MANAGEMENT LAYER)

Distinct from defenses proper — these are the *behavioral systems* he has built to manage what the defenses do not contain.

### Adaptive Compensations

- **Chosen kinship as ego ballast.** The Tom bond is not just a relationship; it is a regulatory device. Tom's presence measurably reduces the subject's baseline irritability, slows his escalation curve, and licenses the more humane modes of behavior. He is a different organism with Tom in the room.
- **Identification with the underdog as moral compass.** In the absence of an internalized ethical framework, the subject uses *body size and apparent power asymmetry* as a proxy for moral salience. Smaller = protect. Larger and condescending = legitimate target. The heuristic is crude but stable and has prevented him from crossing certain thresholds that pure antisocial structure would not have respected.
- **Honest labor as identity scaffolding during depowered periods.** Construction work, manual labor, jobs that use the body in non-destructive registers. These periods are when the subject has been closest to integrated.
- **Retrospective self-recognition.** Slow, late, never in the moment — but real. He has, across decades, named some of what he has done and meant it.

### Maladaptive Compensations

- **The gem-seeking compulsion.** Functions as identity restoration, not greed. The pull is dependency-shaped; the language he uses about it during depowering arcs is the language of withdrawal.
- **Alcohol as the affect-thaw.** With Tom it is social; alone it is the only mechanism by which the isolated affect ever reaches consciousness. The cost is that the affect arrives unregulated, often at night, often producing the worst decisions of the following morning.
- **Helmet ritualism.** The helmet is functionally indispensable (telepathic shield) but the relationship to it has become fetishistic — checked, adjusted, kept within arm's reach when removed, mourned when lost. The object now carries a quantum of self that should reside in the man.
- **The grievance as organizing frame.** Charles-as-target is not just a defense; it has become a *life-organizing structure*. The grievance gives the days shape. Without it, the depowered intervals are quieter but also more frightening, because the frame is gone.
- **Geographic instability.** Tendency to leave any location where he has begun to be known as a person rather than as the Juggernaut. The instability is defensive — being known is dangerous — but the cost is that no prosocial gain has ever been allowed to compound.

---

## V. THE STACK UNDER LOAD — SEQUENCE OF DEPLOYMENT

Under provocation the defenses deploy in a predictable cascade, and the cascade itself is diagnostic.

1. **Verbal aggression** (acting out, low-amplitude). Bluntness, mockery, the conversational equivalent of a warning shoulder-check.
2. **Displacement scan.** Eyes move to identify the Charles-shaped or Kurt-shaped target in the environment.
3. **Splitting.** The provocateur is reclassified to *obstacle*. Mixed feelings, if any were present, vanish.
4. **Projective induction.** Speech register shifts to invite the opponent into the condescending posture that will license escalation.
5. **Somatic mobilization.** Forward motion begins. This is the point of no return; once the body is moving, no internal mechanism is available to stop it.
6. **Acting out at full amplitude.** Property, persons, terrain.
7. **Termination by target depletion** — not by self-regulation. He stops when there is nothing left in front of him.
8. **Isolation of affect** during cool-down. Flat tone, terse recounting.
9. **Alcohol** in the following hours.
10. **Rationalization** in the following days.
11. **Quiet turning against the self** in the following weeks, sometimes producing brief sublimation episodes.
12. **Re-armament** — gem, helmet, or chosen kin — and return to baseline.

The cascade has run, in observable form, hundreds of times across the file. It runs the same way every time. The architecture is rigid, which is both its strength as a defense and its catastrophic limitation as a life.

---

## VI. CLOSING SYNTHESIS

The defensive system is, in its way, a masterpiece of bad construction — every component does its job, the whole holds together under enormous pressure, and the cost of running it is the subject's entire interior life. The boy in the keep is safe. He is also still nine years old, and the walls he is safe behind are the reason he has never grown past it.

The encouraging finding, buried in the inventory: the mature defenses *exist*. Sublimation works when he runs it. Affiliation works when he runs it. Humor is there. Suppression has a working threshold. The architecture for a different life is present in the file; it has simply never been given the conditions under which it could be load-bearing.

The lever, if there is one, is the single defense that has produced every documented period of partial reform: **sincere, low-demand presence from someone who wants nothing from him.** It is the only stimulus the wall is not built to repel, because the wall was built against a man who wanted to hurt him and a brother who wanted him to be better. It was never built against someone who just wanted to sit down next to him. That door, structurally, is unguarded. It has been walked through, in the canon, perhaps four times in sixty years. Each time it has produced something.


## Longitudinal Psychological Profile

# LONGITUDINAL PSYCHOLOGICAL PROFILE — CAIN MARKO

*Decade-by-decade clinical mapping. Frameworks invoked: complex trauma (Herman, van der Kolk), attachment (Main/Hesse disorganized; Fonagy mentalization), object relations (Kernberg borderline organization), self psychology (Kohut — grandiose self, mirror hunger), and traumatic dissociation (Putnam structural). All claims tied to canon behavior.*

---

## I. CHILDHOOD AND LATENCY (pre-1950s, retroactively established — Kurt Marko household, upstate New York)

**Affect regulation.** The earliest reconstructible affective profile is one of *hypervigilant submission punctuated by displaced aggression*. The household contained an unpredictable larger male (Kurt) whose violence the child could not anticipate, prevent, or escape. Under such conditions the developing nervous system fixes into a sympathetic-dominant baseline — chronically elevated arousal, narrowed window of tolerance — which is precisely what we see in the adult: an irritable resting state, near-zero latency from stimulus to rage. The child's only successful regulation strategy was **displacement onto Charles**, the smaller stepbrother who could not retaliate and was not protected from Cain by Kurt (Kurt favored Charles emotionally but did not physically intervene to protect him from Cain). This installs the lifelong template: *affect is discharged sideways, never upward toward the actual source*.

**Cognitive style.** Concrete and present-tense from the start. Mentalization — the capacity to hold one's own and another's mind in view simultaneously — develops poorly in households where the caregiver's mind is dangerous to look into. The child who reads his father's mind for danger cues develops *hyper-attunement to threat affect* (he can read a room for hostility instantly, a skill retained in adulthood) and *under-development of reflective function* about his own internal states. He knows what others feel toward him; he does not know what he feels.

**Self-concept.** Bifurcation begins here. Two self-representations are laid down in parallel: the *bad/deserving-of-beating self* (internalized from Kurt's blows and rejection) and the *not-as-good-as-Charles self* (internalized from Kurt's preferential warmth toward the stepson). These are not the same — the first is shame, the second is envy — and they will fuse only later, under Cyttorak, into the unified compensatory identity. The latency-aged Cain is, in object-relations terms, a child with a persecutory internal object (Kurt) and a rivalrous-envied internal object (Charles), and no good internal object at all. The mother, Sharon, is conspicuously absent from his recorded inner life.

**Diagnostic snapshot (retrospective):** developmental trauma; emerging conduct features; disorganized attachment.

---

## II. ADOLESCENCE (late 1940s – early 1950s)

**Affect regulation.** Pubertal mass and strength arrive — the first time the body offers a partial solution. Bullying of Charles intensifies and *generalizes* to schoolyard peers. The aggression is now ego-syntonic: he discovers that being feared resolves the dysphoria, briefly. This is the **prototype of the Juggernaut economy**: causing fear in others = relief in self. The dose-response curve established in adolescence will never be unlearned.

**Cognitive style.** Action-oriented, anti-reflective consolidates. Schoolwork is not recorded as a domain of investment; physical dominance is. Where Charles develops symbolic capacity (telepathy is, among other things, a metaphor for elite mentalization), Cain develops *somatic-instrumental* intelligence — he learns the world through hitting it.

**Self-concept.** First emergence of the **grandiose-compensatory self** in Kohutian terms: "I am bigger and I make others afraid." This is structurally fragile — it requires constant external confirmation through intimidation, and it collapses whenever a larger figure (Kurt, later combat-superiors, later Thor/Hulk/Onslaught) is present. The bifurcation deepens: the secret self is still the beaten child; the public self is the bully.

---

## III. EARLY ADULTHOOD / KOREA / CYTTORAK (early-to-mid 1950s)

**Affect regulation.** Combat exposed the lie of the bully-identity. The artillery, the chain of command, the *actual* danger of dying — these are stimuli the schoolyard skill set cannot manage. **He deserted under fire.** Clinically this is the most diagnostically important moment of the pre-power record: under real threat his nervous system selected *flight*, not fight, exposing the bully-identity as a thin overlay on an underlying terror-prone substrate. The shame of this desertion will never be metabolized; it will be encrypted into the future Juggernaut's compulsion to *never run again, never retreat, only forward*. Forward motion as identity originates here, not at the gem.

**Cognitive style.** Acute panic-state cognition at the Cyttorak cave: tunnel-narrowed, magical-thinking-permissive (the inscription is read and obeyed as ritual, not evaluated), impulse-dominant. He grasps the gem without deliberation. This is the cognitive style that will recur at every future depowering crisis — narrowed attention, ritualized re-acquisition, no cost-benefit analysis.

**Self-concept.** The transformation is psychologically *exactly* the gratification a humiliated deserter would author: instant, irreversible, unstoppable size. The grandiose-compensatory self is no longer a posture — it is now a body. The bifurcation is operationalized: *Cain Marko* (the deserter, the beaten child) is hidden inside; *the Juggernaut* (the unstoppable) walks the world. The cave collapses on Cain; the world meets only the Juggernaut from now on. The armor, when it comes, will literalize this.

**Diagnostic snapshot:** acute combat-stress reaction → grandiose narcissistic restitution via mystical means; C-PTSD substrate now fully laid down (childhood abuse + combat shame + symbolic burial/rebirth).

---

## IV. THE 1960s — FIRST EMERGENCE (X-Men #12–13 era, in-universe early career)

**Affect regulation.** The dominant affect is *vengeful preoccupation*. The years of subterranean travel from Asia back to Westchester are themselves a clinical sign: the activity of choice, upon becoming a god-tier physical entity, is to walk for years toward the one person whose existence indicts him. This is **rumination operationalized as locomotion** — the obsessive thought made into the journey. No detour, no opportunity-taking, no acquisition. Just toward Charles.

**Cognitive style.** Monomaniacal, target-locked. Tactical reasoning is present (he plans the assault on the mansion) but strategic reasoning is absent (no consideration of what happens after). This is the **forward-motion cognition** in its purest form: the future is the next obstacle, not a state to be optimized for.

**Self-concept.** Unified-by-rage. For the duration of the march and the first attack, the bifurcated self temporarily fuses around the grievance — *I am the one who comes back for what was done to me*. This is the most coherent the self-concept ever gets; it is also the most pathological, because coherence is purchased at the price of having only one project.

---

## V. THE 1970s — THE BLACK TOM ERA BEGINS (Claremont, *X-Men* #101 onward)

This is the most important decade for the file because it falsifies the simple "monster" reading.

**Affect regulation.** Co-regulation appears for the first time in the documented life. With Black Tom Cassidy — an Irish mutant villain of compatible criminal lifestyle and no claim on Cain's identity-organizing wound — the subject demonstrates *down-regulation he cannot self-produce*. He banters. He waits. He defers in planning. The dysregulation curve, normally near-vertical, flattens in Tom's presence. Clinically this is the signature of an *external affect regulator* — a function the disorganized-attachment subject can borrow from a safe other but never internalize.

**Cognitive style.** Slightly more flexible within the partnership: he tolerates heist-planning, delayed gratification for a score, even comic relief. Outside the partnership, unchanged.

**Self-concept.** First evidence of a **third self-state** — not the beaten child, not the Juggernaut, but a *companion-self*: someone's partner, someone's friend, half of a pair. This state is small and conditional but real; it is the only durable counter-evidence to the monster reading, and the file should weight it heavily. Notably, in this state he does not require dominance — Tom is not feared by him and does not fear him, and the relief of not having to be feared or fearful is visible in the depictions.

---

## VI. THE 1980s — THE BRITTLENESS EXPOSED (Nimrod arc, *Uncanny X-Men* #194, 1985)

**Affect regulation.** Encountering Nimrod — a Sentinel from a future where his unstoppability is not stipulated — the subject's response is **uncharacteristic terror and an appeal for teamwork**. This is the cleanest single-issue diagnostic event of the decade. The grandiose-compensatory self does not survive contact with a genuinely larger predator. Under such contact, the underlying *beaten-child affect* surfaces directly: fear, freeze, plea for protection. The schoolyard collapses into the Kurt-household instantly.

**Cognitive style.** Under threat-to-unstoppability, cognition narrows into pre-survival mode: alliance-seeking, target-deferring. The strategic faculty he normally lacks briefly appears because grandiosity has been knocked offline and reality testing returns.

**Self-concept.** Catastrophic destabilization, then re-armoring. He cannot stay in the fear-state and must re-inflate the Juggernaut identity to function. The cycle — *contest → collapse → re-inflation* — is now an observable repeating pattern, not a one-off. By the late 1980s it is the dominant structural rhythm of his appearances.

---

## VII. THE 1990s — ONSLAUGHT AND THE EXTRACTION (mid-1990s)

**Affect regulation.** Onslaught's tearing-off of the helmet and extraction of the Cyttorak essence is, in clinical terms, *acute traumatic disfigurement plus forced regression*. What is revealed inside — a smaller, frightened, hollowed Cain — is not new content; it is the *always-present interior* made externally visible for the first time. The subject's affect in this exposure is what one would expect from any C-PTSD patient whose primary defense has been mechanically removed: terror, shame, dissociative blankness.

**Cognitive style.** During and immediately after the extraction, cognition is fragmented and concrete-survival. Mentalization, which is already poor, drops further; he cannot represent his own state coherently to others.

**Self-concept.** The bifurcation, which had been *operationally hidden* by the body, is now *visible* — the public can see both selves at once. Reintegration in the late 1990s is incomplete and unstable. This is the period where the foundation is laid for the early-2000s reform attempt, because the defense has been shown to be a defense and not a fact, and that knowledge — once acquired — cannot be fully unlearned.

**Diagnostic snapshot:** acute traumatic re-exposure event with partial defensive collapse; the C-PTSD/narcissistic-personality architecture is no longer hidden even from the subject himself.

---

## VIII. THE EARLY 2000s — THE AUSTEN/X-MEN TENURE AND SAMMY PARÉ (c. 2002–2004)

The reformative window. Clinically the richest decade.

**Affect regulation.** Inside a structured environment (the school) with low daily threat and a stable surrogate-kin field (the X-Men, none of whom are Charles-in-the-original-sense and several of whom treat him with low-demand civility), the subject demonstrates **markedly improved affective stability**. Baseline dysphoria persists; explosive escalations decrease. The mechanism is environmental, not internal: he has not learned to regulate; he is being regulated *by the field*.

**Cognitive style.** Slow expansion of reflective function. He is capable, in this period, of small acts of *retrospective narration* — limited self-recognition, limited acknowledgment of past harm. Mentalization is borrowed (from Xavier's framing, from peers) rather than internally generated, but the borrowing itself is a developmental step the file should mark.

**Self-concept.** The **protector-self** appears as a distinct, articulable state for the first time — toward Sammy Paré, the bullied young mutant. This is reaction-formation in the classical sense: the protector-self is the symbolic undoing of the beaten-child self, with Sammy serving as the projective stand-in for young Cain. It is the closest the subject has come to integration — the beaten child is acknowledged (as Sammy) and *protected* (by the Juggernaut), within one continuous self.

**Decompensation event.** Sammy's death collapses the integration. The symbolic child has been killed again; the protector-self has failed in exactly the way Cain himself was failed. Reversion is rapid. The clinical lesson: *integration was real, but contingent on the symbolic child surviving*. The architecture cannot yet hold loss.

---

## IX. THE LATE 2000s — DRIFT (post-Austen, pre-Fear Itself)

**Affect regulation.** Drift back to baseline irritable dysphoria, with the gains of the X-Men tenure partially retained as a *memory of having been better* — which functions in the file as a low-grade chronic shame stimulus rather than as a usable template. He knows he can be otherwise and is not, which is its own injury.

**Cognitive style.** Returned to tactical/present-tense. The reflective gains do not durably persist outside the structured environment that produced them.

**Self-concept.** The third self-state (companion, protector) is now available as a *memory* but not as an active mode. The bifurcation between beaten-child and Juggernaut reasserts as the operating split.

---

## X. THE 2010s — FEAR ITSELF / KUURTH (2011) AND AFTERMATH

**Affect regulation.** Re-amplification by Kuurth's hammer is the inverse of the Onslaught extraction: where extraction removed the defense and exposed the wound, amplification *bypasses the personality entirely* and runs raw destructive affect through the body without any regulatory loop at all. The leveling of Las Vegas is not motivated; it is *unmediated dysregulation at cosmological scale*. Clinically: when the small remaining ego-mediation is overridden by exogenous power, what is revealed is that nothing was holding the affect back except the body's own (high but finite) tolerance threshold. Once that is removed, there is no internal brake.

**Cognitive style.** Effectively dissolved during the Kuurth period — no planning, no targeting, no reflection. Pure affect-into-motion.

**Self-concept.** Temporarily annihilated under Kuurth; replaced by the hammer's purpose. Post-event, the shame of the rampage is *another* unmetabolized wound, layered on the desertion shame and the Onslaught-exposure shame, with no integrative processing applied to any of them.

---

## XI. THE LATE 2010s / 2020s — DEPOWERING CYCLES, BUNN'S *JUGGERNAUT* (2020), AND CONSTRUCTION WORK

**Affect regulation.** The most clinically interesting late-life development. Stripped of the gem and forced to live as a normal-sized man, the subject — for the first time in the recorded life — practices *sobriety, manual labor, routine, and small-scale prosocial interaction without an external regulator field*. The affect regulation is rudimentary but **internally generated**, a category of behavior previously absent. He is, in effect, doing the developmental work of his twenties in his (chronological) seventh decade.

**Cognitive style.** Modest expansion of reflective function. He is able, in this period, to articulate (in plain, halting language) some recognition of pattern: that the power was a problem, that the life was wrong, that there is something to be done differently. The articulations are not eloquent; they are real. Mentalization is finally being *practiced* rather than borrowed.

**Self-concept.** Genuine identity crisis — not in the colloquial but in the Eriksonian sense: who is he without the body? The crisis is productive, because crisis is the only condition under which the bifurcation can be examined. The subject's response oscillates: tolerance of the smaller body alternates with **relapse pull**, which the file should read as *true addiction-equivalent craving* — the gem functions neurochemically and identity-functionally the way a substance does in chronic dependency. The Juggernaut is what he uses.

**Diagnostic snapshot (current):** C-PTSD chronic, partially in remission under environmental scaffolding; personality structure unchanged but with new (limited) reflective capacity; substance-equivalent dependency on the Cyttorak power state; intermittent relapses with full reversion to earlier-decade presentation.

---

## XII. CROSS-DECADE SYNTHESIS — WHAT EVOLVED AND WHAT DID NOT

**Did not evolve (stable across 60+ years):**
- The core wound: smaller-body-in-the-room terror, displaced onto Charles.
- The escalation curve: near-vertical from provocation to violence, no plateau.
- The helmet as non-negotiable boundary against telepathic exposure.
- The forward-motion cognitive habit.
- The bifurcated self: beaten child / unstoppable body.
- Alcohol as primary self-medication when alone.

**Did evolve (in defined directions):**
- *Reflective function:* effectively zero in the 1960s–1980s; borrowed in the 2000s; rudimentary but self-generated by the 2020s.
- *Self-state repertoire:* two states (beaten child / Juggernaut) through the 1970s; three (companion-self emerges with Black Tom) from the late 1970s; four (protector-self emerges with Sammy) in the early 2000s; the later states remain available but unstable.
- *Relationship to the power:* unambiguous gain in the 1960s; identity-essential by the 1980s; defense-as-prison by the 2000s; substance-equivalent dependency by the 2020s. The subject's *relationship to the Juggernaut* has matured even where the Juggernaut has not.
- *Capacity for retrospective shame:* near-absent through the 1980s, present but converted-to-rage in the 1990s, partially tolerated in the 2000s, occasionally articulable in the 2020s.

**The arc, clinically.** This is a man whose pathology was perfectly formed by age twenty and whose **slow late-life recovery** — incremental, non-linear, relapse-prone, environmentally contingent — looks like nothing so much as the trajectory of a long-untreated C-PTSD patient who finally, in middle age and beyond, begins doing the work in fragments. The Juggernaut is the symptom; Cain Marko, slowly and against odds, is the patient learning he exists.


## Psychiatric Assessment & Differential

# PSYCHIATRIC ASSESSMENT & DIFFERENTIAL — SUBJECT: CAIN MARKO

*Compiled from longitudinal behavioral record spanning approximately six decades of observable conduct, cross-referenced against ICD-11 and DSM-5-TR analog criteria. Note that the subject's mystical-somatic augmentation (Cyttorak conferral) constitutes a confound for any standard clinical instrument: the body itself functions as a defense, and several criteria sets (notably impulse-control and substance-use thresholds) must be interpreted against a baseline in which ordinary aversive feedback has been pharmacologically and biomechanically blunted for the majority of the subject's adult life. This document is therefore a behavioral formulation as much as a diagnostic one.*

---

## I. PRESENTING PICTURE (CROSS-SECTIONAL)

At any given observation point across the surveillance window, the subject presents as a hulking, shaven-headed, brutish-featured man of grossly nonhuman proportion, almost invariably in or adjacent to his reddish-crimson and brown armored plating, frequently with the domed crimson helmet in hand or within arm's reach even when not worn. Manner is irritable-suspicious as a baseline; speech is loud, blunt, profane, declarative; eye contact is direct and prolonged in a manner most clinicians experience as dominance-coded rather than relational. Psychomotor activity is forward-leaning; even seated he tends to occupy chairs as if about to stand. Affect is restricted in range (predominantly anger, contempt, occasional gruff humor) but not flat — when the rare positive affect breaks through (with Black Tom, with a child, with a drink in his hand and no obligation in the room), it is genuine and visibly relieving. Insight is poor-to-fair and state-dependent: present after losses, absent before them. Judgment is consistently impaired around two narrow but reliable triggers (the stepbrother; threats to bodily integrity/size). Cognition is grossly intact; no marker of formal thought disorder, no perceptual disturbance, orientation preserved. Suicidal ideation is not historically present in active form, but passive death-equivalent risk-taking is constant and structurally embedded in his operating style.

---

## II. PRIMARY DIAGNOSTIC FORMULATION

### A. Complex Post-Traumatic Stress Disorder (ICD-11: 6B41)

This is the spine of the file. The subject meets, in this analyst's assessment, every required criterion at the severe end of the spectrum:

**1. Exposure to prolonged, repeated traumatic events from which escape was difficult or impossible.** Documented: chronic childhood physical abuse by Kurt Marko, conducted within a household where the favored stepsibling (Charles) was visibly spared. The abuse was not a single event but the daily atmospheric pressure of his developmental years. Layered on top: the laboratory fire in which he watched his father die; combat exposure in Korea; the desertion event under fire; the cave collapse following the Cyttorak acquisition; and, decades later, the Onslaught extraction event, which constitutes a discrete adult traumatic stressor of catastrophic magnitude (forcible removal from his own body).

**2. Core PTSD symptom cluster.** Re-experiencing is present but atypically presented — the subject does not report nightmares (he would not, and clinical access has been minimal), but his behavioral re-enactments are textbook: the unprovoked, transcontinental march on Westchester in the first recorded post-power episode is, structurally, a repetition compulsion. He is going back to *do the beating over again, this time as the bigger body*. Avoidance is present in the form of refusal to enter reflective conversation about Kurt, refusal of telepathic contact, and the helmet itself as a physicalized avoidance apparatus. Sense of current threat manifests as chronic hypervigilance, baseline irritability, and a startle-to-violence pathway that is shorter than any other documented antagonist of comparable power tier.

**3. Disturbances in self-organization (the C-PTSD-specific criteria).**

- *Affective dysregulation:* binary, rage-dominant, no self-soothing capacity except via alcohol or destruction. Sadness chronically unavailable in real time.
- *Negative self-concept:* the bifurcation between "Cain Marko, the failed beaten boy" and "the Juggernaut, the unstoppable thing" is a near-perfect clinical exemplar of post-traumatic self-fragmentation. The Onslaught extraction made this literal: under the armor was a small, frightened man. He has known this about himself for decades and organizes his life around never having to know it again.
- *Disturbances in relationships:* cannot sustain reciprocal peer relationships under demand, but is not flatly avoidant — the long durable bond with Black Tom Cassidy and the parental-coded bond with Sammy Paré demonstrate the *capacity* without the *generalizability*, which is itself diagnostic of C-PTSD rather than primary personality pathology.

**Severity rating: severe, chronic, with partial remissions.** The condition has been present since middle childhood, has never been treated, and has been actively re-traumatized by the conditions of his adult life (combat, repeated bodily extractions/depowerings, the death of Sammy Paré).

### B. Personality Organization: Borderline-Level with Antisocial and Narcissistic Surface Features

This is the most contested call in the file and the one most likely to be misread by a less granular observer. The subject does *not* meet criteria for Antisocial Personality Disorder in the full DSM sense, despite presenting in a way that solicits the label from almost every law-enforcement agency that has encountered him.

Using the Kernberg framework, the subject's personality is organized at the **borderline level**: identity diffusion (the Cain/Juggernaut split is not a creative metaphor, it is a working description of how he experiences himself), primitive defenses (splitting, projective identification, somatization), but **intact reality testing**. On this borderline substrate, the surface presentation is **antisocial-narcissistic**: he reads to the world as a remorseless brute, and is treated accordingly, but the engine underneath is the unmetabolized trauma, not constitutional callousness.

Specific feature inventory:

**Antisocial features present:** chronic criminal conduct; property destruction without remorse; indifference to bystander casualties during rampages; exploitation of others (henchmen, transient allies) when tactically convenient; low frustration tolerance; failure to plan ahead; reckless disregard for safety of self and others; consistent failure to honor financial or legal obligations.

**Antisocial features notably absent:** the deceitfulness criterion is *not* met — the subject is a poor liar and does not deceive for pleasure or profit; he telegraphs intent. The pervasive lack of remorse criterion is not fully met — he experiences and acts on grief (Sammy), shame (post-Onslaught), and a streak of rough fairness (the documented unwillingness to strike clearly defenseless non-combatants without provocation). The juvenile conduct-disorder criterion is unclear from the record, complicated by the fact that his juvenile environment was the abuser's house, not a normative baseline.

**Narcissistic features present:** identity contingency on grandiose self-image ("unstoppable"); catastrophic dysregulation when that image is contested; rage at perceived condescension; envy of the stepbrother coded as contempt.

**Narcissistic features notably absent:** the grandiosity is *too fragile* and *too obviously compensatory* for primary NPD. A true narcissist would not allow the wound underneath to be as accessible as his is — strip the armor and the boy is right there, undefended. Primary NPD defends the wound; this subject *is* the wound, wearing the armor.

**Best summary diagnostic phrasing:** *Personality organization in the borderline range, antisocial-narcissistic surface presentation, with C-PTSD as the etiologic substrate driving both the personality structure and the symptom-level pathology.* The personality features are scar tissue around the trauma, not independent disease.

### C. Alcohol Use Disorder, Moderate, Chronic (DSM-5-TR analog)

Cross-writer, cross-decade consistency in tavern and bar-fight depictions establishes a pattern meeting at least six of the eleven AUD criteria: drinking in larger amounts than intended; persistent desire to drink in social-isolation conditions; great deal of time spent drinking; recurrent use in physically hazardous situations (driving the body of a Juggernaut while intoxicated *is* hazardous to bystanders); continued use despite social/legal consequences; tolerance (unclear given altered metabolism, but the behavioral pattern of escalating quantities suggests it). Severity moderate by criterion count, chronic by duration. **Function:** primarily self-medication for affective dysregulation and for the dissociative quieting of the interior child. Secondary function in the Black Tom dyad is social bonding — the alcohol is a load-bearing element of the only durable relationship in his life, which complicates any treatment plan.

### D. Intermittent Explosive Disorder — Subordinated, Not Independent

The aggressive outbursts criterion is overwhelmingly met. However, in this case IED is best understood as a *symptom of* the C-PTSD rage presentation rather than an independent diagnosis, because (a) the outbursts are not truly out of proportion to internal precipitants when those precipitants are correctly identified (telepathic contact, comparison to Charles, depowering threat), and (b) the nervous-system feedback loop that would normally extinguish IED through somatic consequence has been systematically destroyed: nothing has hurt him in fifty years, so nothing has taught him to stop. Listing IED as a co-primary would over-pathologize what is, mechanistically, a trauma-rage response operating in an environment with no natural punishment for it.

---

## III. ETIOLOGICAL FORMULATION

The etiology is unusually clean for a subject of this complexity, because the developmental data points are themselves stark.

**Pre-morbid substrate:** a temperamentally robust, large, presumably normally-attached infant (no evidence of constitutional difficulty), entering a household with a violent stepfather and a passive/absent mother (Sharon Xavier's decline post-remarriage is documented). The decisive variable is not the abuse alone — children survive abusive fathers — but the **comparison frame**: the abuser visibly preferred the smaller, gentler, telepathic stepson. This is the C-PTSD-generative configuration. Abuse + favoritism + a safer surrogate target produces exactly the displacement pattern observed in the adult: hit the boy who was loved, not the man who hit you.

**Adolescent consolidation:** no recorded interventions, no recorded prosocial adult anchors. The household ended with Kurt's death in the laboratory fire — an event the subject witnessed and, in some accounts, refused to prevent. This adds a guilt overlay (he did not kill his father but he did not save him either) which is metabolized not as remorse but as evidence that the world is one in which one does not rescue.

**Late adolescent / early adult re-traumatization:** Korean War combat, conscripted into the same unit as the stepbrother (a configuration that would have re-activated the original sibling-rivalry trauma under conditions of life-threat). Desertion under fire generates a shame load the subject has never processed and largely cannot speak to; the cave acquisition of the Cyttorak gem occurred in this acute panic-shame state, which is critical — the power was not chosen by an integrated adult ego, it was grabbed by a fleeing, terrified, ashamed young man, and it has carried that emotional signature ever since.

**The somatic intervention.** The Cyttorak transformation is, in the formulation of this analyst, the single most psychologically overdetermined event in the file. A man whose core wound is *I was the smaller body being hit* was, in a moment of maximal regression, handed a body that could never be the smaller body again. The transformation **arrested his psychological development at the age of the transformation** and simultaneously **made all of the developmental work he had not done unnecessary for survival**, because the body would do the defending from then on. Every subsequent decade of behavior is consistent with an adolescent psyche driving an indestructible vehicle.

**Adult re-traumatizations.** The Onslaught extraction (forcible de-bodying), the Bunn-era depowerings (repeated identity-amputation events), the Fear Itself amplification (a forced regression to pure destructive function), and the loss of Sammy Paré (the killing of the only identified-with child in his recent life) each constitute discrete traumatic events that have layered on top of the C-PTSD substrate without ever being processed.

---

## IV. SYMPTOM PRESENTATION IN OBSERVABLE BEHAVIOR

**Re-experiencing, behavioral form:** repetition-compulsion attacks on Xavier and Xavier-coded targets; reactivation of stepbrother framing within the first sentences of any encounter with Charles regardless of intervening events; physical re-enactment of the original power-dynamic (he, larger; the other, smaller; the other, hit) in nearly every fight he chooses rather than is forced into.

**Avoidance, behavioral form:** the helmet, worn or kept proximate at all times when telepathic contact is possible; refusal of reflective conversation about Kurt across all recorded encounters; geographic avoidance of Westchester during depowered periods; the construction-work era as an attempt to live a life in which none of the triggers are present.

**Hyperarousal, behavioral form:** baseline irritable scanning of any room he enters; immediate verbal aggression to perceived condescension; sleep depicted as light and easily disturbed (the bed in his rooms is consistently described as positioned with sightlines to the door); chronic alcohol use as a deliberate down-regulator.

**Negative alterations in cognition/mood:** persistent negative beliefs about self ("I'm a monster," variously phrased, surfaces in the Austen era and again in the Bunn run); persistent negative beliefs about others (Xavier "always" thought himself better; the X-Men "always" condescend); inability to experience positive emotions outside of two narrow relationship configurations; diminished interest in activities other than fighting, drinking, and being with Tom; emotional numbing punctuated by rage.

**C-PTSD-specific disturbances in self-organization:** documented above; observable in the Cain/Juggernaut split, the rage-dominant affect, the relational pattern.

---

## V. COMORBIDITY MAP

The clinical picture is best understood as a **stack** rather than a list:

- **Base layer:** C-PTSD (the etiologic engine).
- **Personality layer:** borderline organization with antisocial-narcissistic surface — scar tissue around the base layer.
- **Behavioral / substance layer:** Alcohol Use Disorder, moderate, chronic — self-medication for the base layer, social ritual within the one durable relationship.
- **Trauma-rage symptom layer:** IED-like presentation, subordinated to base layer.
- **Episodic layer:** acute stress reactions following each de-bodying event (Onslaught, depowerings), with adjustment-disorder-equivalent presentations during reintegration periods (the Austen mansion tenure, the Bunn construction-work era).
- **Bereavement overlay:** unresolved, complicated bereavement following Sammy Paré's death; not formally Prolonged Grief Disorder by duration-and-impairment criteria as currently coded, but functionally close.

Each layer interacts with the others: the alcohol blunts the trauma-rage but enables the antisocial conduct; the personality features make therapeutic engagement nearly impossible, which prevents resolution of the base trauma, which sustains the personality features; the somatic augmentation removes the natural feedback that would otherwise modulate the behavioral expression of all of the above.

---

## VI. COURSE OVER TIME

**Childhood to early adulthood:** unmodified abuse exposure, no interventions, escalating behavioral problems in adolescence (inferred from the bullying pattern with Charles, which is unlikely to have been an isolated case), entry into military service.

**Acute post-Cyttorak period (1960s comic-time):** organized around grievance; pure displaced revenge attacks, no acquisitive plan, no political program.

**Black Tom era (mid-1970s onward):** stabilization through the durable peer bond. The most psychiatrically *healthy* sustained period of the subject's adult life is the long Tom partnership, despite its criminal content — because the relational scaffolding is present.

**Mid-1980s (Nimrod):** first documented breach of the Juggernaut self-concept under threat from a genuinely overpowering adversary; brittle bravado, surfacing anxiety, appeal to teamwork. Diagnostically: confirms the compensatory (not primary) nature of the grandiosity.

**Mid-1990s (Onslaught extraction):** catastrophic destabilization. Functional equivalent of a traumatic amputation event. Subject's reconstitution after this period is incomplete — there is a post-Onslaught quality to his self-presentation that persists.

**Early 2000s (Austen era, X-Men tenure, Sammy Paré):** the clearest naturally-occurring therapeutic experiment in the file. Removal from triggering environment + low-demand prosocial relationship + identified surrogate child = real, measurable improvement, with maintained pro-social behavior until the surrogate's death. The relapse after Sammy's death is itself diagnostically clarifying: the *gains were real*, and the *relapse was grief-driven*, not constitutional reversion.

**Fear Itself (2011) era:** complete regression under externally-applied unlimited-power conditions. Tells us that with the brakes (relational, alcoholic, depressive) removed and the accelerator (Asgardian amplification) pinned, the default operating mode is undirected destruction. Not acquisition. Not vengeance. Destruction.

**2020 Bunn-era depowering / sober construction work:** the cleanest documented attempt at adult recovery. Sobriety achieved, honest labor sustained, identity work attempted. The relapse pull toward the gem is described in the file in language structurally indistinguishable from substance-craving narratives in the addiction literature. Diagnostically: the Cyttorak relationship is a dependency relationship.

**Trajectory summary.** The subject has *never sustained either pole* — neither full Juggernaut-criminality nor full Cain-recovery — and the oscillation is not random but driven by predictable triggers: humiliation/loss → withdrawal → quiet life → provocation → reactivation → destruction → contrition → repeat. The ratchet is stable and has been for sixty years.

---

## VII. RIGOROUS DIFFERENTIAL — WHAT HE IS NOT

A subject of this notoriety attracts misdiagnosis. The following are the most common diagnostic frames applied to him, and the reasons each fails on the evidence.

**1. Primary psychopathy / Antisocial Personality Disorder, full criteria.** *Ruled out.* The decisive evidence is the durable, reciprocal, affectively warm bond with Black Tom Cassidy across decades; the protective-parental conduct toward Sammy Paré; the documented capacity for shame following the Onslaught extraction; the voluntary X-Men tenure; the maintained sobriety and honest work during the Bunn-era depowering. Psychopathy is constitutionally incapable of these outputs. The subject's affective empathy is intact but heavily suppressed; on the Hare PCL-R analog, he would score on the antisocial-behavior facet but would fail to score on the affective/interpersonal facet that distinguishes true psychopathy. He is, to use the clinical idiom, a *secondary* not a *primary* psychopath presentation — and even that label undersells the trauma etiology.

**2. Bipolar I or II.** *Ruled out.* The mood shifts are *reactive*, not cyclic. There is no documented manic episode characterized by decreased need for sleep, pressured speech, flight of ideas, or grandiose plans untethered from immediate provocation. The "manic-appearing" rampage episodes are trauma-rage responses to identifiable triggers, not autonomous mood elevations. No depressive episodes meeting duration criteria are recorded, though dysphoric withdrawals between rampages function adjustment-disorder-style.

**3. Schizophrenia / primary psychotic disorder.** *Ruled out.* Reality testing is intact even under Cyttorak amplification. No hallucinations attributable to internal pathology (mystical visions from Cyttorak are externally-generated and reality-consistent in the canon). No formal thought disorder. No negative symptoms in the schizophrenia-spectrum sense. The destruction is willed and goal-directed (even when the goal is just *destruction*), not delusionally driven.

**4. Pure Narcissistic Personality Disorder.** *Ruled out as primary diagnosis.* Although narcissistic features are clearly present at the surface, primary NPD requires that the grandiose self-image be successfully defended — that the wound underneath remain inaccessible to the subject and to observers. In this subject, the wound is *trivially accessible*. Strip the helmet, strip the gem, mention Charles in the right tone, and the boy appears. A true narcissist does not have a boy that visible.

**5. Intermittent Explosive Disorder as a primary diagnosis.** *Subordinated, not ruled out.* The IED criteria are met behaviorally but the disorder is better captured as a symptom-cluster within the C-PTSD presentation, modified by the somatic confound that aggression has never had natural consequences for him.

**6. Substance-Induced Mood/Behavior Disorder.** *Insufficient as primary.* Alcohol exacerbates but does not generate the core pathology; the behavioral signature is recognizable in sober periods (notably the Bunn run).

**7. Acquired sociopathy from frontal-lobe-equivalent damage** (relevant given decades of head impacts at Hulk-class force levels). *Considered, not supported.* If the augmentation truly prevents tissue damage, no acquired neurological etiology applies. If it does not, the consistent personality presentation across pre- and post-Onslaught periods, and the preserved capacity for prosocial conduct, argue against significant acquired executive dysfunction. The cognitive presentation is concrete-tactical, but it is *stably* concrete-tactical, which suggests trait, not lesion.

**8. Adjustment Disorder.** *Insufficient.* The pathology long predates and outlasts any specific stressor; chronic complex etiology rather than discrete-stressor reactivity.

**9. "Just a supervillain."** This is the law-enforcement and journalistic frame, and it is the most consequentially wrong, because it forecloses every actually-available intervention point. The subject is not a moral category, he is a clinical one. Treating him as evil incarnate has produced, across the entire surveillance window, exactly zero durable behavioral changes. Treating him as a chronically traumatized man with the body of a small god has produced, in the documented Austen and Bunn periods, measurable improvement.

---

## VIII. PROGNOSIS & INTERVENTION CONSIDERATIONS

**Prognosis under no intervention:** the sixty-year ratchet continues. Brief


## Behavioral Atlas

# BEHAVIORAL ATLAS — SUBJECT: CAIN MARKO

*A surveillance-grade catalog of observable tells, micro-patterns, and decision habits across every documented operating condition. Compiled from sixty years of longitudinal record; cross-referenced against the formative and psychiatric workups. The principle of organization: what an analyst with eyes on the subject would see, in the first second, the first minute, the first hour, and the first week of any given state.*

---

## I. BASELINE / CALM STATE

**Setting where observed.** Apartments shared with Black Tom Cassidy; the Salem Center mansion during the Austen tenure; bars in Boston, Dublin, and the Westchester corridor; construction sites and motel rooms during the Bunn-era depowered period.

**Posture and somatic signature.** Standing, the subject defaults to a wide stance, feet planted past shoulder width, weight evenly distributed — the body of a man who has never once had to brace for impact and still organizes itself as if bracing might be relevant. Shoulders carried high and forward, not in tension but in habituated mass; the trapezius load of someone whose musculature is the *answer* to a question his nervous system asked decades ago. Hands at rest hang slightly curled, never fully open. The default facial set is a heavy-lidded scowl that is not, on examination, an emotion — it is a resting architecture.

**Voice in calm.** Lower register than the size predicts. Speaks slowly. Sentences are short, declarative, often dropping the subject pronoun ("Told him already." "Don't care."). Profanity is steady but not escalatory at baseline — punctuative rather than expressive. Will repeat a phrase verbatim rather than rephrase it; rephrasing requires reflection he does not perform spontaneously.

**Eye behavior.** Slow, deliberate room scan upon entering any space. The scan terminates on (a) exits, (b) the largest other person present, (c) any child. Once seated, eye contact during conversation is poor — looks at the speaker's chest or hands more than face. Direct sustained eye contact is offered only to (i) Black Tom, (ii) anyone he intends to hit within the next thirty seconds.

**Habits and rituals at baseline.**
- *Drinking pattern, social.* Beer first, then whiskey, then beer again — a sequencing observed across Claremont-era and later depictions. Glass held in the off-hand to keep the dominant hand free. Drinks slowly when in company, more steadily when alone. Does not get visibly drunk in the conventional sense; gets quieter, then heavier, then suddenly verbose about Charles.
- *Eating pattern.* Eats fast and without comment, head low to the plate, off-hand guarding the perimeter of the food — a residue of either childhood scarcity or institutional/military mess-hall conditioning. Does not refuse food; does not request food; will eat whatever is put down.
- *Sleep.* Sparse and shallow. Reduced metabolic need post-Cyttorak. Sleeps clothed in most depictions. The helmet is within reach if not worn.
- *Grooming.* Bald or shaved scalp maintained — the shave itself is a tell; he does not let hair grow because the helmet sits cleaner on a shaved head and because hair is a *small body's* vanity, foreign to the identity he now operates from. Beard stubble is allowed to come and go without pattern.
- *Possessions.* Travels light. The Bunn-era depowered apartment was nearly empty — bed, table, a duffel. Sentimental objects are not displayed but are not absent; they are pocketed.

**Conversational tells in calm.**
- Will not initiate small talk.
- Will respond, gruffly, to questions about practical matters; will not respond to questions about feelings without first producing a deflection (a snort, a shrug, a one-word dismissal).
- Mentions of Charles produce a half-second delay before the next sentence — a micro-pause that is the closest thing in his repertoire to a tell of inner disturbance during calm.
- When genuinely amused — almost exclusively in Tom's company — laughs from the chest, briefly, then shuts it down as if embarrassed by the sound.

**Decision habits in calm.** Defers most non-tactical decisions to whoever else is present (Tom in heists, Xavier during the X-Men tenure, foremen at the construction site). The absence of decisions is itself a habit: he conserves volition for the moments when it must be spent.

---

## II. LOW-GRADE IRRITATION / SUBCLINICAL DYSPHORIA

This is the modal state, more frequent than true calm. Observable in any social gathering longer than two hours, any bureaucratic interaction, any room containing someone who reminds him of Charles.

**Tells.**
- Jaw tension rises; chewing motion at rest when not eating.
- Heel of dominant hand begins tapping a slow rhythm on whatever flat surface is closest — table, thigh, bar.
- Verbal output drops further; one-syllable answers become the norm.
- Increased frequency of looking toward the exit.
- Drink consumption rate doubles without his appearing to notice.
- Will physically shift his chair to put his back closer to a wall.

**Decision pattern.** Begins to mentally pre-authorize escalation. He is not yet planning violence but is removing the inhibitions against it, one by one — identifying who in the room he could hit without consequence, locating the heaviest movable object, calculating door distance.

---

## III. PROVOCATION / STRESS

The escalation curve is the most documented feature of the subject. It is near-vertical and has almost no plateau.

**Stage 1 — Verbal challenge (first 0–5 seconds).**
- Head turns slowly toward the provocateur. Slowly is the tell; speed indicates surprise, slowness indicates intentional registration.
- "What did you say." Spoken as a flat declarative, not a question. The absence of interrogative rise is diagnostic.
- One hand sets down whatever it is holding. He puts down glasses with care, even in this state — a residual courtesy that is one of the cleaner pieces of evidence against full ASPD.

**Stage 2 — Pre-violence framing (5–15 seconds).**
- Stands if seated. The stand itself is the warning; he uses his height as the first weapon and watches the provocateur's face for the recalibration he expects.
- A short, almost ritual verbal sequence: a single contemptuous nickname for the provocateur, a single sentence stating what he is about to do, and — almost always — an offer of withdrawal ("Walk away."). This offer is genuine and serves two functions: it preserves his self-image as not the first aggressor, and it satisfies the internal fairness code that distinguishes him from his father.
- Eyes lock on the provocateur's center mass, not face.

**Stage 3 — Initiation (15–30 seconds).**
- The first contact is almost never maximal. He will, in most depictions, throw a measured opening blow — a shove, a backhand, a one-handed grab — that he expects to settle the matter. This is *not* restraint in the moral sense; it is the unstoppable man's confidence that minimal force will suffice. The reservation collapses instantly the moment the target does not go down.

**Stage 4 — Full escalation.**
- Once committed, the forward motion that defines the Juggernaut takes over not just physically but cognitively. He stops processing peripheral information. He will walk through walls rather than around them — *Uncanny* recurrently shows this — and this is not just physics; it is a cognitive style. Obstacles are not navigated. They are passed through.
- Verbalization during full violence is sparse. He does not monologue. The occasional grunt, the occasional name (Charles, in particularly intense engagements, said almost involuntarily), nothing more.
- Bystanders are *not* primary targets but are not protected. He will not turn aside to kill them; he will also not turn aside to spare them.

**Stage 5 — Termination.**
- Does not terminate himself. Ends either when targets are exhausted, power is removed, or a specific anchoring voice (Tom; in the Austen run, briefly Sammy Paré; on rare occasions Xavier in a non-confrontational register) penetrates the rage state.
- Post-termination: a long inhale, shoulders dropping perhaps an inch, scanning the damage with an expression that across multiple writers is best described as *neither satisfied nor surprised*. Will sometimes reach up to touch the helmet — a self-soothing check that the armor is intact.

**Decision habits under stress.** Long-term considerations vanish entirely. Tactical considerations narrow to the next ten feet. He does not strategize during violence; he discovers what he was going to do by doing it.

---

## IV. THREAT — DEFINED AS A FORCE THAT GENUINELY CONTESTS UNSTOPPABILITY

The behavioral profile under genuine threat (Nimrod, Hulk on certain occasions, Thor with the right hammer, Onslaught) diverges sharply from the provocation profile and is one of the most diagnostically rich states in the file.

**First-second tells.**
- A backward shift of weight — minute, perhaps two inches — before any conscious recognition that the threat is real. The body knows first.
- A widening of the eyes that is not present in any other state. The heavy lids retract.
- A sharp single exhale, almost a *huh*, that is the closest thing to a startle response his post-Cyttorak nervous system produces.

**Verbal tells.**
- Voice rises in register, not volume. The slow low baseline gives way to faster cadence.
- Question forms reappear: "What — " "How — " interrogatives he does not produce in any lesser state.
- In the Nimrod engagement specifically, the appeal for teamwork — "We need to work together" — was delivered to the X-Men, of all parties; this is the diagnostic moment for the entire file. *When unstoppability is contested, the subject reaches for the very people he has spent his life punishing*. The boy under the armor recognizes other children.

**Postural collapse signatures.**
- The wide stance narrows.
- The forward shoulders pull back — defensive posture appears for the first time.
- The hands open. The default curl releases. He becomes, momentarily, a *grasping* organism rather than a striking one.

**Decision habits under threat.** Tactical flexibility briefly returns; he will accept positioning instructions, will retreat (a behavior absent in every lesser state), will coordinate. This window closes the instant the threat resolves; the cooperative posture is not internalized and does not transfer to subsequent encounters with the same allies.

---

## V. INTIMACY — DEFINED BROADLY (PEER COMPANIONSHIP, PROTECTOR-OF-CHILD, RARE SEXUAL/ROMANTIC)

The single most under-appreciated band of the spectrum and the one in which the subject is least recognizable to outside observers.

**With Black Tom Cassidy (the durable peer bond).**
- Posture loosens. The wide stance narrows naturally rather than defensively. He sits with his back to doors when Tom is present, an unobservable tell of trust.
- Voice softens in volume, not register; the cadence speeds; the sentences lengthen; he uses Tom's name unprompted, an extraordinary frequency relative to other relationships.
- Touch tolerance increases. He will accept a hand on the shoulder from Tom; from any other adult this contact would license violence.
- Banter pattern: dry, self-deprecating, often built around mocking his own size and force ("Subtle, that's me."). The capacity for self-deprecation appears nowhere else in the record.
- Defers in planning. In heist sequences across the Claremont and post-Claremont eras, Tom plans; Cain executes. The subject will accept directives from Tom that he would treat as mortal insult from anyone else.
- On Tom's apparent deaths: prolonged drinking, withdrawal from prior associates, a documented willingness to walk into clearly fatal engagements. Grief presents *late*, hours or days after the loss, and presents somatically (drinking, sleeplessness, escalated baseline irritability) before it presents verbally.

**With a child/identified surrogate (the Sammy Paré pattern, and by extension any obviously bullied small figure).**
- Crouches. The single most diagnostic tell in the entire intimacy band — the unstoppable man *lowers himself* physically to a child's height. He does not do this in any other condition.
- Voice flattens out of the gravel baseline into something nearly conversational. Sentences become functional and instructive ("Don't let them see you flinch." "Hit first, hit once.").
- Will physically interpose his body between the child and any approaching figure without comment, an automatic positioning that he will deny if asked about it.
- Tolerates being touched, climbed on, asked irritating questions. The irritability that governs every other relationship is suspended.
- On loss of the child figure: catastrophic destabilization. The Sammy arc shows the pattern in full — withdrawal, return to grievance-mode toward Xavier, drinking, and ultimately the eruption that proved the gains were not load-bearing under that magnitude of grief.

**Romantic/sexual presentation.** The record is sparse. What is present (occasional Black Tom-era depictions, scattered bar scenes) suggests a transactional, non-pursuing pattern — partners come to him, encounters are short, and there is no observable pursuit behavior, no flirtation repertoire, no documented sustained romantic attachment. The cause is probably overdetermined: the body is intimidating to most prospective partners, the affect is forbidding, and the underlying small-body wound makes erotic exposure (literal undressing of the Juggernaut) effortful in ways the file cannot fully resolve.

**Decision habits in intimacy.** Defers without resentment. Will spend resources he otherwise hoards (time, attention, restraint). Will accept obligations he refuses categorically in any other relational frame.

---

## VI. GRIEF

Distinct from defeat. Grief is the loss of a person; defeat is the loss of unstoppability. The subject experiences both but their signatures differ.

**Acute phase (first hours).**
- Often *no* observable signature. The affect-regulation deficit cuts both ways: he cannot brake rage and he cannot accelerate sadness in real time. Observers frequently misread the immediate post-loss state as indifference. It is not; it is unavailability.
- One reliable acute tell: he becomes notably quieter than his already-quiet baseline. The grunt-and-shrug response set shrinks to the grunt alone.
- Will perform practical post-loss actions (moving a body, leaving a scene) with mechanical competence.

**Subacute phase (12–72 hours).**
- Drinking escalates to the chronic-alone pattern: whiskey only, no beer, no food.
- Sleeplessness, but not pacing — he sits.
- Will look at hands. A recurrent micro-gesture across depictions in this state: turning his own hands palm-up on his knees and studying them. The reading: the hands that did not protect, or the hands that did harm, depending on the loss.

**Chronic phase (days to weeks).**
- Reverts to grievance-mode toward Charles even when Charles has nothing to do with the loss. Grief is metabolized through the familiar channel of resentment because that is the only metabolic pathway his psyche has built. Sammy's death routed, within a few arcs, back into Xavier-directed rage; the routing is automatic.
- Construction-job stoicism (Bunn era) is a chronic-grief presentation as much as a sobriety presentation: the body is given something to do because the mind has nowhere productive to send the feeling.

**Decision habits in grief.** Catastrophically poor. The grievance-routing pattern means that grief decisions tend to be misdirected violence decisions. The subject is at his most dangerous to bystanders in the chronic grief phase, not the acute one.

---

## VII. VICTORY

A surprisingly thin band of the record. The subject wins frequently — physically — and almost never *enjoys* it on the page.

**Tells in immediate victory.**
- A single exhale.
- A brief look at the helmet or the gem (when worn/possessed) — an acknowledgment of the source, not of the self.
- No celebration. No taunt at the fallen unless the fallen was Charles-coded, in which case a single dismissive line, usually delivered while walking away.
- Will turn his back on a defeated opponent immediately — a tell of contempt that is also a tactical liability, exploited multiple times in canon.

**Decision habits in victory.** Disengagement, not consolidation. He does not press strategic advantage; the win was the point, and the win is now over. This is one of several reasons he has never built a power base; victory does not interest him as a foundation, only as a punctuation.

**Anomaly.** When the victory is shared with Tom — a successful heist, a successful escape — the affect repertoire expands. He will grin. He will sometimes laugh. The grin is brief and is the closest the file gets to documenting joy.

---

## VIII. DEFEAT

The richest band of the file after stress, because defeat in the meaningful sense — contested unstoppability — is the literalization of the core wound.

**Tells in physical defeat (rare).**
- The eye-widening startle reappears.
- Verbal output shifts: in defeat he speaks more, not less. Cursing increases. Threats become specific rather than generic ("I'll find you" → "I'll find you in Westchester, I'll find you at the school, I'll find you").
- Refuses help from anyone other than Tom. Will lie about injuries.

**Tells in identity defeat (depowering, helmet loss, telepathic penetration).**
- The catastrophic register. Onslaught's extraction event documented a near-fetal posture in a man whose body had not been small in decades.
- Voice loss — not silence but loss of the low register. He sounds younger.
- Disorientation in space; the body that knew where it was no longer does.
- An intense, often immediate move to *cover the head*. Hands to scalp. This is the helmetless gesture and the most direct surveillance evidence of the small-body interior.

**Decision habits in defeat.**
- *Power-restoration seeking* becomes the dominant cognitive content within hours. The Bunn run is explicit: even during a sincere reform period, the pull is constant.
- Avoidance of mirrors and reflective surfaces, documented in several depowered-era scenes.
- Withdrawal from peer contact — uncharacteristically including Tom on occasion, because shame of being seen smaller is greater even than the need for the durable bond.

---

## IX. SPECIFIC RECURRENT MICRO-TELLS (cross-state)

A consolidated list of small behaviors with diagnostic value, observable independent of the larger state classification.

- **Helmet touch.** Right hand to dome, brief, palm flat. Performed after violence, before sleep, on entering a new space, and whenever Charles is mentioned. Self-soothing and reality-check fused.
- **Half-second pause on the name Charles.** Across decades, across writers. The most reliable individual tell in the file.
- **The shave.** Maintained even during depowered periods, when the practical reason (helmet fit) is absent. Identity-coded; the bald head is the Juggernaut even when the Juggernaut is unavailable.
- **Putting glasses down before violence.** Persistent fairness-code residue.
- **The crouch for a child.** Diagnostic of the protector mode and its activation.
- **Walking through rather than around.** Cognitive style externalized; visible even in low-stakes pedestrian contexts.
- **Back to the wall (alone) / back to the door (with Tom).** Spatial trust signal.
- **Hand on scalp in defeat.** The unguarded interior child.
- **Whiskey-only when grieving; beer-and-whiskey when social.** Beverage-state mapping is consistent.
- **The off-hand food guard.** Childhood scarcity / institutional residue.
- **Slow turn of the head toward provocateurs; fast turn toward threats.** The speed of the head-turn distinguishes the provocation curve from the threat curve in the first second of any incident.
- **The brief grin with Tom.** Joy ration for the decade.
- **The single name said involuntarily during full violence.** *Charles*, mostly. Sometimes *Kurt*. The latter is the rarer and more diagnostic of the two; it appears under conditions of maximum dysregulation and is the closest the file has to direct evidence of who the violence is actually for.

---

## X. WEEKLY AND SEASONAL PATTERNING

**Weekly rhythm (during stable periods, Tom-cohabitation or X-Men tenure or Bunn-era construction).**
- Activity peaks late afternoon to late night; baseline torpor in the morning hours.
- Drinking is heaviest Friday through Sunday in social periods; nightly in isolation periods.
- A weekly day of near-total inactivity is observable across multiple stable periods — the subject sits, drinks moderately, watches television or stares at middle distance, speaks minimally. This is restorative, not depressive.

**Seasonal/anniversary patterning.**
- Affective worsening observable around the calendar window of the Korean-era cave incident in multiple depictions, though writers rarely flag it explicitly.
- The Westchester proximity effect: any geographic approach to Salem Center produces measurable baseline destabilization regardless of intention. The subject has gone out of his way to detour around Westchester during peaceful periods, and out of his way to detour *through* it during hostile ones.

---

## XI. DECISION HABITS — INTEGRATIVE SUMMARY

Across all states, the subject's decisions cluster into three classes:

1. **Forward-motion decisions** (the dominant class): chosen by elimination of alternatives rather than by selection. He decides what he will do by ruling out what he will not do, and the residue is the action. This is why his decisions are hard to predict by motive-analysis and easy to predict by *obstacle*-analysis. Locate the obstacles and he will go through them.

2. **Deferred decisions** (the trust class): handed off to Tom, to a foreman, to Xavier, to a child's stated preference. These are the decisions the analyst should monitor for, because they are the cleanest evidence of who currently holds attachment-weight in the subject's life.

3. **Reactivation decisions** (the grievance class): not really decisions, but ratchet-clicks. The pattern of return to the gem, return to Charles, return to the bottle, return to the armor. These are not chosen; they are gravitated toward. They become decisions only retroactively, when the subject is asked to explain himself and constructs a justification he did not have at the moment of action.

The unifying principle, and the one a total-surveillance file should never lose sight of: **the subject is not navigating; he is being carried by a current he laid down in childhood and has never dredged.** Every state in this atlas is a different reading of the same river.


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS — SUBJECT: CAIN MARKO

*A surveillance file of the subject's actual life — not the rampages the news catches, but the 95% of hours between them. What follows is compiled from longitudinal observation across the subject's three recurring operational modes: (A) **Powered-and-active** — at large, in possession of the Cyttorak gem's investiture, partnered or solo; (B) **Powered-and-quiet** — in residence somewhere, between jobs, not currently a wanted bulletin; (C) **Depowered** — stripped of the gem, living at human scale, working. The same man is visible in all three, but the rituals shift. Where they hold across modes, that is noted; where they fracture, that is the diagnostic data.*

---

## 1. THE ARCHITECTURE OF A DAY

### 1.1 Sleep, Waking, and the First Hour

The subject sleeps badly and has for as long as the file goes back. Mode B and C surveillance both record him retiring late — usually between 0200 and 0400 — and waking between 0700 and 0830 regardless of bedtime. The math does not add up to rest, and it isn't meant to. He does not lie down expecting sleep; he lies down to stop the day, and sleep happens to him or doesn't. Reduced metabolic demand under the Cyttorak investiture keeps him operational on this deficit indefinitely; in depowered mode, the same schedule produces visible fatigue and a heavier reliance on coffee and alcohol to bracket it.

He sleeps in clothing — shorts or jeans, often the same shirt he wore that day. He does not own pajamas. In Mode A he has been observed sleeping in the body-armor under-layer of the Juggernaut rig, helmet within arm's reach on the floor or nightstand. The helmet is **never** out of the room when he sleeps. In any motel, safehouse, mansion guest suite, or construction-site trailer, the first thing he places when he enters is the helmet, and the placement is always the same: on the floor or low surface to the right of the bed, dome up, opening down, so that he can swing his right arm down and have it on his head before his feet hit the floor. This is the most consistent ritual in the entire file. It is older than any of his alliances and survives every reform attempt.

He sleeps with the door visible from the bed when possible. If the room does not allow this, he repositions furniture. Surveillance of three separate Westchester guest-suite stays during the Austen-era X-Men tenure recorded the same nightstand being dragged to the opposite wall within ninety minutes of arrival.

Waking is rough. He does not spring up; he sits on the edge of the bed for between four and eleven minutes before standing, hunched, hands on knees, breathing audibly. He has been observed staring at the floor for the entire interval without movement. This is the only time of day the interior child the file repeatedly identifies is visible on his face. By the time he is on his feet, the face has reset.

First action after standing, every recorded morning across all three modes: he uses the bathroom, then drinks water directly from the tap with cupped hands or, more recently, from the bathroom faucet held under the running stream. He does not own or use a glass for this. He then either (in Mode A/B) puts on the helmet within five minutes of standing, or (in Mode C) splashes water on his face and stares at himself in the mirror for approximately twenty to forty seconds — a duration too long to be grooming, too short to be reflection, with no clear conclusion. He breaks the stare by turning, never by looking away.

### 1.2 Morning Through Midday

He eats in the morning only when food is present and convenient. He does not cook breakfast; he eats whatever is on hand cold or microwaved. Recorded morning consumption: leftover takeout (most common), cereal eaten dry from the box, cold cuts directly from the package, three or four eggs cracked into a pan and barely cooked. Coffee is constant in Mode C — black, large, often refilled from a workplace urn — and intermittent in Modes A/B, where he is more likely to drink a beer at 1000 if the day is unscheduled.

He does not read newspapers. He does watch television in passing — sports, mostly, and not in a fan's way; he leaves it on as ambient noise and looks up at it during commercials of his own thoughts. He has a documented preference for boxing and for any combat sport that televises the loser staying down. He flips off football and basketball after a few minutes unless someone else is in the room watching.

Mid-morning behavior is mode-dependent and is the cleanest discriminator between his three operational states:

- **Mode A (powered, active):** Mid-morning is planning or staging time. If partnered with the Black Tom figure, the planning is conversational, conducted over coffee and beer, and tends to move from the kitchen to a couch by 1100. The subject is the junior planner; he listens, asks tactical questions ("how thick?", "how many guards?", "how long inside?"), and contributes the assumption that he will be the entry vector. If solo, mid-morning is restless — he paces, lifts things he doesn't need to lift, leaves the dwelling on foot.

- **Mode B (powered, quiet):** Mid-morning is the hardest stretch. He has nothing to do and the body to do it with. Recorded behavior includes: long walks of three to seven miles with no destination, sitting in diners for ninety minutes nursing a single cup of coffee, parking himself in a public space (a bench, a bleacher, the back of a bar) and watching people. He is not surveilling. He is occupying.

- **Mode C (depowered):** Mid-morning is the steadiest stretch. He is at the construction site or the warehouse job by 0700, has been working for three hours, and is halfway to a lunch he will eat with the crew. The subject becomes legible and stable inside a work shift. The hierarchy is clear, the demands are physical, and no one is asking him to talk about himself. This is, by the file's reading, the closest thing to a regulated daily life he ever achieves.

### 1.3 Afternoon

Across all three modes, the afternoon includes physical exertion. He is the kind of large body that gets noticeably worse without it.

In Mode A/B this takes the form of "training" that isn't really training — there is nothing to train for when one is already invulnerable — but is a physical-discharge ritual. He lifts heavy objects (engine blocks, sections of wall, in safehouse settings whatever is bolted down least). He throws things at walls. He has been observed in three separate junkyard locations across two decades simply walking up to cars and hitting them, methodically, working down a row. The activity has the cadence of a swimmer doing laps. No audience. No vocalization. Approximately forty-five minutes to an hour, then he stops, sits on something, drinks water, and leaves.

In Mode C the physical discharge is the job itself, and the subject has been observed taking on more work than required — staying late, volunteering for the heavy task, eating lunch on the move. Foremen describe him as the best laborer they've ever had and the worst conversationalist. He does not chat during work. He responds when addressed, in two- or three-word answers, and returns to the task.

Afternoons end with the first real meal of the day, between 1700 and 1900. The subject eats large — by witness accounts, three to four times a normal adult intake even depowered, considerably more under Cyttorak. He prefers meat, fried food, anything dense. He eats fast. He does not season anything at the table. He does not finish what he started talking about during the meal; he eats first, talks after. He uses his hands more than is socially typical, including for foods that warrant a fork. Napkin use is post-meal, never during.

### 1.4 Evenings

This is the most predictable surveillance window and the most psychologically loaded.
