He drinks. The drinking begins between 1800 and 2000 and runs until he stops moving for the night. The venue is the discriminator:

- **With the Black Tom figure or equivalent chosen kin:** A bar, often the same bar over weeks or months, often Irish-leaning in décor and clientele. He sits at the bar, not at a table; takes the second-from-end stool if available; orders in rounds, not by drink. He laughs in this setting. He is funny in this setting — dry, profane, deadpan. He listens more than he speaks. He buys when it's his round and never short-changes it. Surveillance recordings of these evenings show a man no one would identify from his bulletins.

- **Alone, in residence:** He drinks at a table or on a couch, with the television on. He does not pour drinks; he opens cans or bottles in a row and finishes them. The cadence is steady, not festive. He does not get visibly drunk in the typical sense — the volume required, given his constitution, is enormous — but he becomes slower, more inward, and eventually still. The terminal posture is leaned back, head against the wall or cushion, eyes open, looking at nothing. The file's working interpretation: this is the only state in which the affect underneath the rage is accessible to him, and even then he does not name it.

- **In a bar alone, in a town he doesn't live in:** Different ritual. He picks a corner with sightlines to both doors. He drinks more slowly. He does not initiate. He is, in this configuration, the most likely to be in a bar fight by 2300 — not because he starts them but because his presence reads as a challenge to the kind of man who needs to issue one, and he has no incentive to defuse.

He does not use recreational drugs. There is no record of this. Alcohol is the entire pharmacology.

### 1.5 The Hours Before Bed

The last ritual of the day is the most consistent one after the helmet placement. Between thirty minutes and two hours before he lies down, regardless of where he is, he goes outside. He stands in open air. He does not smoke (no record of tobacco use); he does not pace; he stands. Recorded duration ranges from eight minutes to over an hour. He looks up — at the sky if it is visible, at the side of a building if it is not. He has been observed talking to himself during this interval, inaudibly, lips barely moving, on perhaps one occasion in five. The file does not know what he says and the subject would not, if asked, be able to report.

He returns inside. He places the helmet. He lies down. The day ends.

---

## 2. HABITS OF PLACE

### 2.1 Where He Lives

The subject does not own real estate in his own name in any documented period. Residences across the file fall into five categories:

1. **Safehouses with the Black Tom figure** — typically rented under aliases, mid-tier urban apartments or small standalone houses, never high-rises (elevator/egress concerns; also, by partner preference, ground-level). Duration: months to a few years.
2. **Hotel and motel rooms** — between operations, while traveling. He prefers low-rise motels with exterior corridors; he avoids hotels with key-card systems where possible because of the unreliability under his hand pressure and because he dislikes hallways with no windows.
3. **Westchester guest suite (Austen-era X-Men tenure)** — a brief, anomalous period of institutional residence. He adapted poorly to communal space and well to the room itself once he had rearranged it.
4. **Construction-site trailers and SRO rooms (depowered periods, Bunn-era and equivalents)** — minimal, clean enough, paid weekly. He has been observed keeping these spaces tidier than any of his powered residences. This is consistent: when he is small, he is orderly; when he is large, he is not.
5. **No address** — periods of travel, of subterranean transit (the original Korea-to-Westchester march and its lesser successors), of crashing on couches. The subject is comfortable being unhoused in a way most adults are not. He does not panic without a bed.

### 2.2 What His Room Looks Like

Surveillance entry photographs across decades show a remarkable consistency. The bed is unmade. There is a chair, usually with clothes on it. There is at least one piece of armor or armor component visible somewhere in the room even in depowered periods — a gauntlet on a shelf, a chest piece in a closet — kept the way other men keep a wedding ring after a divorce. The helmet, if present, is on the floor right of the bed.

There are few personal effects. He does not display photographs. He does not own books. He keeps a small number of items with disproportionate care: a wristwatch from a specific decade he has worn since (cheap, scratched, never replaced even when broken — he gets it repaired); one or two pieces of jewelry given by the Black Tom figure across the years; an item recovered from his mother (the file's working inference based on its appearance in multiple residences across decades and its untouched condition — possibly a hairbrush or a small ceramic). These are not arranged. They sit in drawers, in the pockets of bags, on shelves, but they always travel with him.

He does not put art on walls. He does not own plants. He does not own a pet, ever, in any recorded period — this is notable in a man with documented protective instinct toward small things, and the file's reading is that pets imply a relationship to one's own continuity he does not feel entitled to.

### 2.3 Routes and Geographic Habits

He walks. The subject's preferred mode of transit when not actively transporting himself by Cyttorak-amplified momentum is on foot, regardless of distance. He has been documented walking thirty-plus miles in a day for no operational reason. He uses public transit reluctantly (close quarters, small seats, social demands of being a large man not making other passengers uncomfortable — he cannot, and gives up trying). He drives only when necessary and prefers older, larger vehicles he doesn't have to be careful with.

Routes are habitual once established. In any residence longer than a week he develops a fixed bar, a fixed diner, a fixed route between them, a fixed corner store for beer and cigarettes (he buys cigarettes for partners and acquaintances; he does not smoke himself). He varies the route only under operational threat. The variation is shallow — he uses two alternates, not five.

He sits with his back to walls. He picks corner booths. He notices exits. This is not training; it is the habit of a body that has been hunted and that does not want to be surprised.

---

## 3. HABITS OF TIME

The subject's relationship to clock time is utilitarian and unsentimental. He shows up when he says he will, in most cases on the dot. He does not run late; he does not run early. He does not wear modern devices — no smartphone use is recorded beyond the bare functional minimum, and surveillance has not documented him scrolling. He owns a watch and looks at it. He keeps no calendar visible in any residence; significant dates are remembered, not scheduled.

Anniversaries he marks privately and never with announcement: there is a recurring three-to-four-day withdrawal period in late autumn across multiple years that aligns approximately with the timing of the Korean War cave incident and with the Kurt Marko death, which the file cannot fully disentangle. During this window he drinks more, talks less, and is more likely to leave town. He has never named the dates aloud in any recorded conversation.

He marks the Black Tom figure's birthday with a gift, always, including in years they are estranged. The gift is always practical (a coat, a knife, a bottle); never sentimental.

He does not observe holidays in any sustained way. Christmas surveillance recordings across decades show him working, drinking, or sleeping through it. He has been observed in a diner alone on Christmas Day on at least three separate occasions in three separate cities, eating a full meal, leaving a tip larger than the bill. He does not appear sad in these recordings; he appears to be inside a regular Wednesday.

---

## 4. RITUALS OF THE BODY

The helmet is the single most ritualized object in his life and has been addressed above. Beyond it:

He shaves his head himself, with a straight razor or a single-blade safety razor, in front of a mirror, approximately every three to five days. The duration is fifteen to twenty minutes. He is meticulous about this; it is the only grooming task he performs with care. He does not nick himself.

He bathes by shower, briefly and hot, usually at the end of a workday in Mode C or after physical-discharge sessions in Mode A/B. He does not take baths. He does not use scented products; he uses whatever bar soap is available. He does not own cologne.

He clips his own nails. He cuts his own clothes to fit when needed (sleeves removed, seams let out, hems undone) — the subject possesses a small sewing kit that has traveled with him across multiple residences, a fact disproportionate to its observation frequency but consistent in inventory.

He does not get tattoos in most depictions and does not seek piercings. He has standing scars from the pre-Cyttorak era that have not been added to since.

He does not exercise in any formal sense. The labor and the physical-discharge rituals are sufficient. He does not run for cardiovascular reasons; he walks. He does not stretch.

---

## 5. WHAT A WEEK OF SURVEILLANCE WOULD ACTUALLY RECORD

Compressed to a representative week in Mode B (powered, quiet, in residence with the Black Tom figure, no active operation):

**Monday.** Wakes 0820. Sits on bed edge 0820–0828. Tap water. Helmet on by 0834. Eats leftover pizza standing in kitchen, 0840. Coffee with partner 0900–1015, mostly listening. Walks alone to nearby park 1030, sits on bench 1100–1240 watching dog-walkers and children. Returns. Eats deli sandwiches 1320. Naps on couch with television on (boxing replay) 1410–1530. Lifts engine block in back lot 1545–1640. Showers. First beer 1715. Bar with partner 1900–0145. Outside the bar smoking partner's cigarette he does not light, talking quietly, 0200–0215. Helmet placed 0240. Lies down 0245.

**Tuesday.** Wakes 0800. Eight-minute bed sit. Same opening sequence. Restless midday — partner is away. Walks roughly six miles, route unfamiliar to surveillance, ends at a different bar than the usual. Drinks alone in corner 1500–1830. Returns, eats heavily 1900–1930. Television on, drinks at table 1930–0100. Long outside-stand 0145–0240 (extended; this is a harder evening). Helmet, bed, 0300.

**Wednesday.** Wakes 0735, anomalously early. Coffee with returned partner 0800–0900. Operational discussion begins — a job is being prepped. Subject's contribution: tactical, terse, accepts assigned role. Mid-morning at scouted location, walking the perimeter twice. Lunch at diner with partner 1330. Afternoon: rests, lies on couch, reads nothing, watches television. Evening: bar, partner, shorter than usual (0040 closing). Pre-job sobriety beginning to take hold. Outside-stand 12 minutes. Bed 0125.

**Thursday.** Wakes 0700. Pre-operation discipline visible: no morning beer, more water, longer mirror-stare. Afternoon at scouted location again. Evening early dinner 1800. One drink with partner 1930–2030. Bed 2300. Helmet placement, as always.

**Friday.** Operation. Out of residence 1100, returns 0500 Saturday. The week's rampage news cycle, such as it is, occupies these eighteen hours. The other 150 hours of the week occupy this file.

**Saturday.** Sleeps until 1140 — the only late wake of the week. Aggressive recovery: eats heavily 1230, drinks beginning 1300, partner present, television on, no conversation about the operation in any depth (the subject does not debrief verbally; the partner narrates and he grunts assent or correction). Bar that evening, loud and long.

**Sunday.** Wakes 1010. Slower. Walk alone in the morning. Diner alone, two hours, one plate, three coffees. Returns. Quiet afternoon. Drinks earlier than usual, 1530. Outside-stand at 2200 is the longest of the week — over an hour. He talks to himself for some of it. He goes back inside. Helmet to the floor, right side of the bed. Lies down. The week resets.

---

## 6. WHAT THE ROUTINES TELL THE FILE

Three diagnostic points emerge from the daily-life record and reinforce the larger workup:

**First**, the helmet ritual is older and more stable than any of his ideological or operational commitments. It predates every alliance, survives every reform, and persists in depowered periods when it serves no tactical function. It is the load-bearing ritual of the subject's selfhood. Any plan that requires its removal will fail not for tactical reasons but for psychological ones.

**Second**, the subject is most stably regulated when his day is structured by an external hierarchy that asks nothing of him emotionally and a great deal of him physically. This is not a man who needs solitude; it is a man who needs **occupation**. The Mode C construction-job stability is not despite the depowering; it is partly because of it, the day giving him the regulating structure that his powered modes leave him without. This implies the long-form intervention horizon: he does best in lives that are *busy in the body and quiet in the demand*.

**Third**, the unstructured hours are where the wound surfaces — the morning bed-sit, the evening outside-stand, the long walks with no destination, the diner Christmas. None of these are tactical; none of these are operational; all of them are visible only in surveillance, never in news. The man the file is interested in is in those hours. The Juggernaut is in the other ones. The work of understanding him is the work of staying with the bed-sit until the face resets.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# RELATIONSHIPS I — FAMILY & ORIGIN BONDS

*The subject's family file is small in headcount and enormous in gravitational pull. Four primary figures (Kurt Marko, Sharon Xavier Marko, Charles Xavier, Kurt's biological line via Marko relations), one near-adopted surrogate (Sammy Paré, treated here because the subject filed him under "kin" in everything but legal paper), and a long shadow of the dead. The dead in this file outnumber and outweigh the living. Everyone foundational to this subject is in the ground, and the subject has not finished arguing with any of them.*

---

## 1. KURT MARKO (stepfather; biological father; deceased) — THE ORIGIN INJURY

**Status:** Deceased, c. subject's early adolescence, laboratory fire at Kurt's atomic research facility. Subject was present.

**Biographical baseline.** Kurt Marko was a nuclear physicist of moderate professional standing, colleague of Brian Xavier, who inserted himself into Sharon Xavier's life with practiced opportunism in the months after Brian's death. The marriage was transactional on his side — Sharon's inheritance, Brian's house, a child (Charles) whose intellectual promise Kurt registered as a kind of status acquisition. Cain was Kurt's biological son, conceived earlier in a relationship Kurt had treated as disposable; Cain entered the Xavier household as the unwanted prior chapter that Kurt could not legally close.

**Day-to-day operational record (reconstructed from flashback corpus).** Kurt drank. He drank in the late afternoon, into the evening, and the violence rose with the alcohol on a schedule the household had memorized. He hit Cain — open-handed at first, then closed-fist as Cain grew — on a rotation that the subject's adult behavior suggests followed no rational schedule: bad days at the lab, perceived backtalk, Cain physically resembling the woman Kurt had abandoned, Cain simply being in the wrong room. The beatings were administered out of sight of Sharon when possible and out of sight of Charles always. Kurt's cruelest stroke was institutional, not muscular: in front of Cain he praised Charles. Charles's grades, Charles's manners, Charles's quiet, Charles's *promise*. Cain was the disappointment held up against the prodigy, by the man who hit only one of them.

**Dynamics.** The relationship was constructed entirely around a single asymmetry: Kurt had absolute physical power and used it without contest. There is no recorded evidence of tenderness, no birthday, no shared activity, no instructional moment. The subject's adult inability to imagine a father-figure that is not also a threat-figure is sourced here. Critically, Kurt also feared Charles — Kurt suspected the boy of telepathy long before it was confirmed, and at least one canonical flashback shows Kurt's terror that Charles had *heard* him plotting (the death of Brian Xavier, complicity in the lab fire that produced Charles's father's death — depending on era, Kurt's culpability ranges from passive beneficiary to active murderer). The household's deep secret, audible to Charles and inflicted on Cain, was that the man at its head had killed to be there.

**The fire.** The terminal event is the cleanest behavioral evidence in the file. Kurt, dying in his own laboratory accident, called for help. Cain was within range. Cain did not move — by some accounts watched, by others fled, by none rescued. Kurt's last act was to entrust certain documents/secrets to Charles, not to Cain — the favoritism extended into death and the subject witnessed it. The fact that he did not save the man who beat him is unsurprising; the operationally important datum is that the subject *recorded the moment as a settled score and then immediately discovered that the score was not in fact settled, because the favoritism had outlived the favoritist*.

**Trust/safety profile.** Zero, in life. Posthumously, the subject treats Kurt's memory with a complicated stillness — Kurt is rarely named, rarely cursed aloud, rarely invoked at all. This is not forgiveness; this is the foreclosure of a relationship the subject cannot revisit because the other party is no longer available to lose to. The trauma was sealed at the moment of the fire and has not been opened since.

**Failure mode.** The subject cannot tolerate any adult male in a position of structural authority who also expresses moral judgment. Drill sergeants, prison wardens, team leaders, Asgardians, professors — all draw a charge they have not personally earned. Kurt is the template; every authority figure is its echo.

**Leverage.** Direct invocation of Kurt is the single most destabilizing verbal lever available, and almost nobody has access to it because almost nobody knows the details. Charles knows. Black Tom knows fragments. A skilled interrogator with the file could, by naming Kurt without affect, produce either a freeze response or an immediate physical eruption, with no middle state. The lever should never be pulled casually; the subject's recovery time from the touch is measured in months.

**Identification residue.** The hardest fact in the dossier: the subject *became* Kurt in his adult operating mode. Larger than the room. Drinking. Hitting. Resenting a smaller, gentler male relative. The Juggernaut is, structurally, Kurt Marko at scale, wearing armor instead of a lab coat. The subject has never said this aloud and the file holds no evidence he has ever thought it clearly. He is built on a model he has not examined.

---

## 2. SHARON XAVIER MARKO (stepmother; deceased) — THE ABSENCE THAT DID NOT INTERVENE

**Status:** Deceased, illness, during the subject's adolescence — predeceasing Kurt by a margin that the household never recovered from.

**Biographical baseline.** Sharon Xavier was widowed young, wealthy, gentle, and by every available account already failing when Kurt Marko entered her life. She drank — possibly before Brian's death, certainly after — and Kurt's predation was facilitated by the simple fact that she was not in a condition to refuse him. By the time Cain was brought into the household, Sharon was a thinning presence; by the time Cain was being beaten in adjacent rooms, she was effectively already gone, anesthetized in the way that allowed the household to function around her.

**Dynamics with the subject.** Almost nothing. This is itself the data point. Cain was the second son brought into a house Sharon had stopped fully occupying; the subject has no recorded warm memory of his stepmother, no recorded grievance against her either, no funeral scene, no invocation. She is the *missing maternal column* in the architecture — the figure who, in a non-pathological household, would have intervened against Kurt, named the beatings, removed the child. She did none of these things. The subject does not blame her in any recorded utterance and this is itself diagnostic: he has never permitted himself to be angry at a woman who failed him, because the available template for anger at parents was supplied by Kurt and runs only on the male axis.

**Trust/safety profile.** Untested. He had no relationship rich enough to be betrayed within. The damage is the damage of a deficit, not of a wound.

**Failure mode.** The subject's lifelong inability to seek help from women in caregiving positions — nurses, social workers, female team-handlers, female X-Men in pastoral roles — sources here. He does not register them as *capable of intervention*. They are scenery. The Sammy Paré bond, notably, is with a *child*, not with a maternal surrogate; when the subject reaches across the gender line at all, he reaches downward, never upward.

**Leverage.** Negligible directly. Indirectly, any narrative that frames the subject as someone *no one came for* — the unrescued child — strikes a chord he cannot defend against. Sharon is the unspoken proof of that frame. A patient interlocutor mentioning "your mother" in any context produces a flat affect and a quick subject change; the file should note this as a tell, not a wall.

**Posthumous role.** Sharon's death is the moment Kurt's violence became uncontested. The subject's chronology of the worst beatings clusters in the window between her decline and Kurt's death. She is, in the subject's nervous system, less a person than a *time marker*: the era of survivable childhood ended when she did.

---

## 3. CHARLES XAVIER (stepbrother) — THE PERMANENT TARGET

**Status:** Living (with the canonical asterisks). The only family relationship the subject has had access to as an adult, and therefore the only one that has continued to develop.

**Biographical baseline.** Charles is two years younger, smaller, frailer in childhood, intellectually precocious, telepathic from latency onward, and the recipient — through no choice of his own — of every scrap of paternal approval Kurt Marko was capable of distributing. The subject met him as a six- or seven-year-old being moved into a house already occupied by a smaller, paler, smarter boy who his new father visibly preferred. The relationship was poisoned in the first hour and has never recovered.

**Childhood operational record.** Cain bullied Charles. The bullying was systematic, daily, escalating, and conducted out of adult sight with a discipline that itself indicates the displacement pattern was already organized: the subject knew, even at nine, that what he was doing was forbidden, and chose his moments. He pushed Charles down stairs. He broke Charles's possessions. He humiliated him verbally in front of other children. Critically, Charles — telepathic, even at low resolution — *knew* the beatings Cain was receiving from Kurt, and made the unforgivable mistake of letting Cain perceive that he knew. The pity of the favored child for the unfavored child became, in Cain's interior, the deepest insult the household contained. Charles's gentleness scaled the wound; his attempts at kindness were intolerable, because every kindness from Charles was evidence that Charles could *afford* kindness, and Cain could not.

**Korea.** The shared deployment was Charles's idea — Charles, by then adult and telepathic, had volunteered to shadow his stepbrother into the war, to protect him. The subject experienced this protection as surveillance and indictment. When Cain deserted under fire and found the Cyttorak gem, he was already running from Charles as much as from the North Koreans; the gem was an answer to a question he had been asking since he was seven. *How do I become larger than my brother.*

**The adult pattern.** The first thing the subject did with the powers of a god was walk back across the Pacific to hit his stepbrother. Not to take Xavier's money — substantial. Not to expose Xavier's secrets — many. To hit him. Sixty years of subsequent engagements run on the same fuel. The X-Men are obstacles; the Mansion is a target because Charles built it; Cerebro is a target because Charles uses it; mutants in general are not the subject's quarrel and he has said so. *Charles* is the quarrel.

**Reconciliation attempts (multiple, all by Charles).** Charles has, across decades, offered:
- Hospital visits during the subject's depowered episodes.
- A bed at the mansion (Austen era; accepted, briefly functional).
- Telepathic offers to *remove* the rage — refused, every time, and correctly: the subject understands at some level that the rage is the load-bearing wall.
- Repeated public defenses of the subject to other X-Men, framing him as redeemable.

The subject accepts these only when he is too depowered, too sober, or too tired to refuse them, and reverts on contact with the next provocation. The pattern is not that he doesn't believe Charles — he does — but that *believing Charles requires reorganizing the entire self around a fact (I am loved by the brother I have spent my life punishing) that the architecture cannot support*. Reconciliation would require the demolition of the Juggernaut, and the subject cannot live in the rubble.

**Trust/safety profile.** Inverted and absolute. Charles is the person the subject trusts most in the world to *not actually kill him*, and therefore the person it is safest to attack. This is a paradox the subject lives in without naming. He would not march on Magneto's island; he would die. He marches on Westchester because Westchester will let him. The depth of Charles's restraint is the medium in which the subject's aggression swims.

**Failure mode.** Any third party who praises Charles in the subject's presence has, within seconds, a binary problem. Any third party who *compares* the brothers — favorably or unfavorably to either — has a violence problem. The subject cannot hear Charles's name in an evaluative sentence without the small-body wound activating.

**The helmet.** Worth its own paragraph in this sub-section because the helmet is, functionally, the wall between the brothers' interiors. Charles can read every mind in a city block; he cannot read his brother's. The subject discovered this vulnerability the hard way (early X-Men engagements) and the helmet has been non-negotiable since. Note what the helmet means structurally: the subject has *organized his physical silhouette around the necessity of not being known by his brother*. The most iconic visual element of his costume is a defense against intimacy with the one living person who knows his actual name.

**Leverage.** Charles is the master key. Any operator with credentialed access to Charles — or who can convincingly *imitate* a Charles-channel — can either pacify or detonate the subject, depending on script. The same words mean opposite things from different mouths: *your brother is proud of you* from a stranger is a provocation; from Charles, transmitted with care under conditions of low demand, has, in documented instances, made the subject cry. The lever is dangerous and should not be operated by amateurs.

**Long-term forecast.** The subject will die without completing this relationship. Charles will likely die first (statistically, given respective combat exposure and somatic durability), and the subject's response to that death is the single most important unhedged variable in his entire file. The available models are: (a) collapse — the Juggernaut identity, having lost its target, deflates and the man underneath surfaces in mourning; (b) eruption — the rage, having lost its rationale, generalizes catastrophically; (c) stasis — the subject continues to live as if Charles were alive, because the relationship was never about Charles, only about the wound Charles symbolized. Field assessment: (c) is most likely, with intermittent episodes of (b), and (a) only under sustained, low-demand support from a non-family kin figure (currently only Black Tom qualifies, and Tom's own longevity is not assured).

---

## 4. THE BIOLOGICAL MOTHER (unnamed, abandoned by Kurt; status uncertain) — THE GHOST UPSTREAM

**Status:** Effectively unrecorded in canon; functionally absent from the subject's entire life. Treated here because the *gap* is data.

The subject is the product of a relationship Kurt Marko terminated before commitment. The mother either died, departed, or was paid off — the file does not resolve which, and the subject has never been recorded inquiring. He does not search for her. He does not speak of her. He has never used resources he plainly possesses (and as Black Tom's partner had access to) to locate her or her line.

**Behavioral significance.** The non-search is the datum. The subject has organized his identity around the household he was inserted into, not the one he came from. He does not believe in a prior, gentler maternal alternative; whether one existed or not is irrelevant, because believing in it would require admitting that *he was placed* in the house where he was beaten, which would in turn require grieving the placement, which the architecture does not permit. The biological mother is therefore a sealed room in the subject's interior. He walks past it without looking.

**Leverage.** Potentially enormous and entirely untested. Any operator producing credible evidence of the mother — alive, dead, lineage — would force open a room the subject has spent sixty years not entering. Outcome unpredictable. Recommendation: do not attempt without containment.

---

## 5. SAMMY PARÉ ("the Squid Boy"; deceased) — THE SON HE BRIEFLY HAD

**Status:** Deceased, murdered by a vengeful relative during the subject's mansion tenure. Cause of one of the subject's two recorded breakdowns into genuine, unweaponized grief.

**Biographical baseline.** A young mutant boy resident at the Xavier school during the subject's reform era. Visibly mutated (aquatic morphology), bullied by other students, socially isolated, sharp-tongued in self-defense, parentally rejected at home. The subject identified him immediately and across every diagnostic axis: the smaller body in the room, the favoritism inversion (other children preferred), the paternal rejection, the verbal armor over the somatic wound. Sammy was the subject's childhood with the polarity of the power-asymmetry reversed: the bullied child standing next to the largest man on the property.

**Dynamics.** The relationship was the cleanest prosocial bond in the subject's adult life with the partial exception of Black Tom. The subject was *patient* with Sammy — patience is otherwise foreign to him. He sat with the boy. He listened to school complaints. He provided physical proximity as deterrence (no one bullied Sammy with the Juggernaut in the same hallway). He did not lecture, did not perform fatherhood, did not demand reciprocity. The arrangement worked precisely because Sammy required nothing the subject could not give and offered nothing the subject would have to reject: company without evaluation, recognition without comparison.

**Why it worked, mechanically.** Sammy was not a peer (no rivalry available); not a parent (no authority threat); not female (no Sharon-shaped absence to navigate); not telepathic (no Xavier-shaped interior threat); and — critically — *visibly smaller and visibly more hated*. The subject's protector mode activated with full force and no contamination. For the duration of the relationship, the subject was, in observable behavior, *not the Juggernaut*. He was a large man walking a small mutant boy to class.

**The murder.** Sammy was killed in the subject's effective custody — outside his moment-to-moment supervision but inside the perimeter the subject had implicitly accepted responsibility for. The killing was an attack the subject failed to prevent, and the subject knew, immediately, that failure-to-prevent was the original sin he had been organized around (Kurt at the fire; Charles in the line of paternal favoritism; every bystander he had himself failed to spare across decades of rampages). The grief was real, sustained, and lacked any available target — the killer was outside the subject's reach in ways the narrative would not let him cross.

**Failure mode revealed.** The subject's reaction to Sammy's death was *not* generalized rage. It was withdrawal, alcohol, regression to Juggernaut-as-identity, and eventual departure from the mansion. The first time grief was authentically available to him in adulthood, he could not metabolize it; he absorbed it into the existing architecture and called the architecture back into service. The Juggernaut, in this period, was not weaponized aggression — it was *anesthesia*.

**Posthumous role.** Sammy is the subject's private proof that he is capable of love. He does not invoke this proof aloud — the subject does not narrate himself — but operationally, every subsequent attempt at reform has Sammy somewhere in the substrate. The Bunn-era construction job, the depowered-sobriety chapters, the willingness to be useful to mutant communities without payment: all of it carries Sammy's residue.

**Leverage.** Sammy is the second master key, after Charles, and the only one accessible to operators without telepathic credentials. A clean, non-manipulative invocation of Sammy — by name, with care — opens the subject in a way that nothing else does. The same invocation, cynically deployed, will be detected and produce immediate, terminal violence. The lever requires sincerity to operate; the subject's instrument for distinguishing sincere from cynical invocation, in this single domain, is uncannily accurate.

---

## 6. THE DEAD, COLLECTIVELY — THE FILE'S CENTER OF MASS

The subject's family is, in headcount, a graveyard. Kurt is dead. Sharon is dead. The biological mother is functionally dead. Sammy is dead. Of the family register, only Charles remains, and the relationship with Charles is itself a long argument with the dead — Kurt's favoritism, Sharon's absence, the household that produced both brothers.

The operational consequence is that the subject's interior is populated by figures who cannot be renegotiated with. Every behavior toward the living is mediated by the unfinished business with the dead. He hits Charles to settle a score with Kurt. He fails to seek maternal care because Sharon never modeled it. He fathers Sammy briefly because Sammy is the child Cain was, and then loses Sammy and confirms the architecture's deepest belief: *nothing held is held for long*.

**Final note for the family-relationships file.** The subject's recovery from his condition, if it is possible at all, is not available through the channels normally indicated. He will not, in this lifetime, do effective trauma work in a clinical setting; he will not name Kurt aloud to a professional; he will not grieve Sharon. The only available route is the slow accumulation of *low-demand non-evaluative kinship* in the present — relationships structured like the Sammy bond, durable like the Black Tom bond, supplied by figures who do not want anything and do not compare him to anyone. Charles cannot supply this directly because the comparison is constitutive of the relationship. No one currently in the subject's life supplies it at volume. The file's central prognostic question is whether anyone ever will.


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*UATU FILE FRAGMENT 7-B. Cross-reference Relationships I (Adversaries, Kin-of-Origin, Rivals) for the Xavier, Kurt Marko, and Sharon Marko entries. This module catalogues every individual the subject has, across the longitudinal record, treated as ally, friend, chosen kin, mentor, or protégé — including the marginal cases. Entries are arranged by depth of bond, not by chronology. Each entry maps origin, operational pattern, the specific micro-behaviors the subject exhibits in that person's presence, the failure mode of the bond, and the leverage either party holds.*

---

## 1. BLACK TOM CASSIDY — The Spine of the Subject's Adult Emotional Life

**Origin and first contact.** The bond predates most of the X-Men's awareness of it; the subject and Cassidy were established as already-partnered when first depicted (*X-Men* #101–103, Claremont, 1976). Reconstructed history places the meeting in a holding cell or trans-Atlantic criminal-services network in the early-to-mid 1970s, post-Cain's initial X-Men confrontations, during a period in which the subject was drifting between European underworld jobs. Cassidy — Irish, charming, dispossessed gentry, a man with his own paternal-favoritism wound regarding his cousin Sean (Banshee) — recognized the subject's grievance structure immediately because it mirrored his own. The bond was built on isomorphic pain: *each is the discarded brother of a beloved man.* Neither has ever needed to explain this to the other.

**Operational pattern.** Across roughly forty-five years of intermittent canon, the partnership is the most stable structure in the subject's life. Distinguishing micro-behaviors observed in Cassidy's presence and *nowhere else*:

- *Verbal register softens.* The subject's normal speech is short, blunt, often profane; with Cassidy his sentences lengthen, he tells stories, he sets up jokes for Cassidy to land. He is the straight man.
- *Defers in tactical planning.* In every heist sequence on record (Murderworld, Genosha runs, various banks and museums), Cassidy designs; the subject executes. This is the *only* sustained context in which the subject accepts a subordinate role.
- *Permits physical proximity at rest.* They share apartments, hotel rooms, vacation cottages. The subject — who otherwise sleeps alone, drinks alone, and bristles at touch — is observed sleeping in adjoining rooms with the door open, eating breakfast across small tables, accepting Cassidy's hand on his shoulder without flinching.
- *Mourns publicly.* On every occasion Cassidy has been believed dead or grievously injured, the subject has openly raged and openly grieved — the only person whose loss he externalizes in real time rather than retroactively through alcohol.

**Trust architecture.** Cassidy meets all three of the subject's tolerability conditions: (a) he does not threaten the subject's self-concept (Cassidy is his own kind of unstoppable, in a different modality — plant-based, ranged, indirect — and so does not compete on the strength axis); (b) he accepts the dominance hierarchy without contest in physical matters; (c) he is emotionally undemanding — he never asks the subject to *talk about it*, never asks the subject to reform, never invokes Charles. The bond is sustained by what is *not* required.

**Evolution.** Three distinct phases. Phase one (1976–c.1991): pure criminal partnership, lateral and warm. Phase two (1990s, post-Onslaught, post–subject's various reform attempts): Cassidy is the constant the subject returns to between identity collapses; the partnership becomes asymmetric, with Cassidy occupying a quasi-fraternal stabilizing role. Phase three (post–Fear Itself, through Bunn's *Juggernaut* miniseries 2020 and after): contact thins; Cassidy is on his own arcs, the subject is in and out of the gem. The bond is no longer active-operational but is *referentially live* — both men speak of the other as still present.

**Failure mode.** The bond has fractured under exactly one consistent pressure: when one of them has been forcibly turned against the other by external power (Cassidy bonded with a sentient plant entity, the subject under Onslaught or Kuurth amplification). They never break each other by *choice*. The structural vulnerability is that neither has built any defense against the other's good faith, so coercion of either side weaponizes the bond instantly. After every such episode they reconcile without apology — apology would require articulating the wound, and they protect each other from articulation.

**Leverage.** Cassidy holds the highest non-coercive leverage on the subject of any living person. He can, in a single sentence delivered without heat, end a rampage that telepathy and Asgardian weaponry cannot. He has done so, on record, multiple times. The leverage is *unusable by anyone else* — it depends entirely on Cassidy's specific voice, specific register, and the absence of any request behind the sentence. Cassidy has never, in canon, asked the subject for anything self-serving. This restraint is the entire substrate of the leverage.

---

## 2. SAMMY PARÉ ("The Squid Boy") — The Protégé That Proved the Capacity Existed

**Origin.** *Uncanny X-Men* (Austen run, c. 2003). A teenage mutant with aquatic features — visibly other, visibly bullied, socially humiliated in ways the subject's somatic memory registered before his conscious mind did. They met during the subject's X-Mansion residency. The first interaction on record is the subject driving off a group tormenting Sammy; the second is the subject sitting on a stone wall with the boy and not speaking. This sequence is structurally identical to a successful early-treatment alliance: presence without demand.

**Operational pattern.** With Sammy the subject demonstrated a constellation of behaviors that the prior thirty years of his canon would have ruled impossible:

- *Modulated voice.* Audible softening, slowing of cadence, no profanity.
- *Physical down-scaling.* Sat where he could be looked down at; crouched; leaned. The towering frame was deliberately neutralized.
- *Patience with the boy's awkwardness.* He neither rushed the boy's speech nor mocked it; he absorbed silences.
- *Self-disclosure in primitive form.* The subject told Sammy, in fragments, about being hit as a child — the *only* sustained on-page articulation of the Kurt Marko material to any living person in canon.
- *Anticipatory protection.* He positioned himself between Sammy and crowds without being asked.

**Trust architecture.** Sammy hit the third of the subject's three tolerability categories — *protector mode* — with unusual completeness. Sammy was visibly the smaller body in every room; the symbolic equation was direct. Protecting Sammy was the symbolic undoing of his own childhood. There was no risk of comparison (Sammy admired him without qualification), no demand (Sammy asked nothing), no telepathic vulnerability (Sammy was not a mind-reader).

**Evolution.** Brief by narrative time, intense by emotional charge. The arc moved from wary mutual recognition to functional surrogate-paternal bond within months of in-universe time. The subject was, by any honest read, becoming a *father* in this relationship — and showing every sign that he was capable of it under exactly these conditions.

**Failure mode.** Sammy was murdered. The cause was external. The bond did not fracture; it was severed. The subject's response was catastrophic and informative: he did not rampage immediately. He went still. He drank. He sat with the body. The immediate post-loss behavior was *grief in the depressive register*, not anger — establishing that the rage-default is itself a defense, and that when a loss is large enough to bypass it, what is underneath is sorrow. The eventual reversion to violence was delayed, deliberate, and structurally retributive rather than diffuse.

**Leverage (posthumous).** Sammy's memory operates as a permanent moral anchor in the subject's psyche. Any subsequent appeal to him on behalf of a bullied child or vulnerable young mutant trips the same circuit. Operators wishing to redirect the subject toward prosocial conduct should note: invocation of Sammy is *high-power, single-use per encounter*, and is psychologically expensive to the subject. Repeated invocation produces shutdown, then rage at the invoker.

---

## 3. CHARLES XAVIER (as ally, not adversary) — The Asymptotic Reconciliation

*Cross-reference Relationships I for the adversarial mapping; this entry catalogues only the periods in which the subject and Xavier functioned, however briefly, as allies.*

**Origin of the ally-phase.** Beginning with the post-*X-Men: The End* trajectory and consolidating in the Austen run, Xavier extended an explicit and repeated invitation to the subject to live at the Mansion, train, and be useful. The subject accepted, with reservations he never named.

**Operational pattern during ally-phases.** The most stable observation is what the subject *avoided*: he avoided being alone in rooms with Xavier; avoided meals at the same table; avoided any setting in which Xavier might speak to him in the older-brother register. When in joint operations he obeyed Xavier's tactical instructions with surly compliance, executed competently, and removed himself immediately afterward. He never thanked Xavier and never accepted thanks.

He did, however, demonstrate one consistent micro-behavior found nowhere else: he removed his helmet in Xavier's presence at the Mansion, intermittently. This is the highest-trust gesture in his repertoire — the helmet is his telepathic shield and his somatic identity — and the fact that he ever did it at all is the strongest available evidence that some part of the subject *wants* the reconciliation he cannot otherwise allow.

**Trust architecture.** Conditional, fragile, and always asymmetric. Xavier's good faith is the destabilizing element: it cannot be refused without admitting the original wound, and cannot be accepted without surrendering the identity built on the wound. The subject manages this by accepting in narrow operational registers and refusing in all relational registers.

**Failure mode.** Every ally-phase has terminated on the same trigger: a moment in which Xavier — usually inadvertently — slips into the older-brother register, or in which the subject perceives Xavier doing so. A particular tone, a particular hand-on-shoulder gesture, a moment of being *managed*. The subject's exit is rapid, verbal, and final, and is usually followed within months by a reversion-to-grievance arc.

**Leverage.** Xavier's leverage on the subject is the highest in absolute terms and the lowest in usable terms. He could, with a sentence, devastate the subject. He almost never does, and the restraint is the only reason the relationship persists at all. The subject's leverage on Xavier is comparable and similarly unused; each is the other's nuclear option.

---

## 4. THE X-MEN (as collective ally) — Conditional, Tolerated, Never Trusted

**Origin.** Membership-of-record during the Austen run, intermittent team-ups thereafter (most notably during *World War Hulk*, when the subject sided with the larger anti-Hulk coalition; various *Avengers vs. X-Men* and post-*Krakoa* peripheries).

**Operational pattern.** With the team the subject is professionally cooperative and personally absent. He shows up to the briefings, executes the assignment, and disappears to his room or off-grounds. He has no preferred teammate within the larger roster (excepting Nightcrawler — see below), no rivalries within the team that he sustains past the immediate moment, and no participation in the social rituals that consolidate team bonds (movie nights, mess-hall meals, training-room sparring outside scheduled drills).

The single consistent exception is his behavior toward *new and young* team members, particularly visibly-mutated ones. With these he reverts to *protector mode*, with the same modulation observed with Sammy — slower voice, smaller posture, watchful positioning. The pattern is unmistakable and operationally predictable.

**Failure mode.** The team has failed for him on every occasion in which a member has either (a) addressed him in the *Cain* register rather than the *Juggernaut* register without earning it, or (b) attempted to make him *talk about* anything. He responds to both with immediate withdrawal and, if pursued, with verbal aggression escalating toward physical.

**Leverage.** The team holds collective situational leverage (he will not casually harm them while wearing their uniform) but no individual member except those listed here holds personal leverage. The team's most reliable mechanism for retaining him has been to *not ask him to be retained* — to leave the door open, ask nothing, accept his erratic attendance, and never frame his presence as evidence of his goodness.

---

## 5. KURT WAGNER (NIGHTCRAWLER) — The Unexpected Theological Ear

**Origin.** Recurring incidental contact through X-Men team-ups; consolidated as a quasi-relationship during the X-Mansion residency and subsequent crossovers. Wagner is the single team member with whom the subject has been observed in voluntary one-on-one conversation outside operational necessity.

**Operational pattern.** Brief but telling. The subject has, on multiple occasions, sought Wagner out for short, oblique conversations on questions of guilt, damnation, and whether the gem of Cyttorak constitutes a curse or a deal. The conversations are not framed as confessions; they are framed as bar-room theology. Wagner's response — non-judgmental, devout without proselytizing, willing to sit with the question — is exactly calibrated to the subject's tolerability conditions.

**Trust architecture.** Wagner is visibly other; bears stigmatized physical features; is unconditionally kind; makes no demands. The subject reads him, correctly, as someone who has lived inside the *monster* category and chosen something else. This is the only available model the subject has ever had for the trajectory he himself can intermittently imagine.

**Failure mode.** None recorded. The relationship has never been intense enough to fracture; it functions as a low-grade chaplaincy.

**Leverage.** Modest but unique. Wagner is the only person in canon who can use explicitly moral and religious language to the subject without triggering the comparison-with-Charles circuit. Reserved use, however, is essential — over-deployment would convert Wagner into an authority figure and end the function.

---

## 6. D-MAN, THE THUNDERBOLTS / DARK AVENGERS CYCLE, AND SECONDARY UNDERWORLD ASSOCIATES

**Composition.** Across the longitudinal record the subject has rotated through a series of low-grade criminal and quasi-criminal associations — bar regulars, fence networks, second-tier supervillain teaming arrangements (Frightful Four ad hoc inclusions, Masters of Evil one-offs, Thunderbolts-adjacent appearances). No individual within these networks has risen to the level of personal bond.

**Operational pattern.** Strictly transactional. The subject participates, takes his cut, drinks with the crew, and departs. He is described by such associates (when the file has interview-equivalents) as *reliable on the job, terrible to argue with, decent for the price of a round, do not bring up his family*. The last clause is canonical bar-floor wisdom.

**Trust architecture.** Functional, not personal. These networks meet the *peer* condition only in the narrowest sense; he extends none of the Cassidy-level micro-behaviors to any of them.

**Failure mode.** These bonds have fractured constantly and inconsequentially. The subject has been double-crossed by such associates on multiple occasions, has retaliated proportionately, and has neither carried the grudge past the immediate resolution nor extended the trust further into the network as a result. The underworld is, for him, a public utility.

**Leverage.** None in either direction beyond standard criminal-network reciprocity.

---

## 7. THE CONSTRUCTION CREW (Bunn, *Juggernaut* 2020) — The Quiet Civilian Bond

**Origin.** During the depowered interval of the Bunn miniseries, the subject took work on a Chicago demolition-and-construction crew under a partial alias. The foreman and a small subset of co-workers knew, or came to know, who he was. They kept it.

**Operational pattern.** With this crew the subject demonstrated a register seen nowhere else in his record: *civilian competence and civilian humility*. He worked the shift, took directions from a smaller man (the foreman) without resistance, ate lunch with the crew, paid for his round at the end of the week, and treated the work as work. He was *good at it*. He took satisfaction in physical labor that produced rather than destroyed.

**Trust architecture.** The crew accepted him without ceremony, asked nothing of his history, did not attempt to redeem him, and treated his strength as a tool rather than a spectacle. This is the same composite tolerability profile that defines every successful bond in his life.

**Failure mode.** Terminated by the resumption of supernatural plot pressure; the bond did not fracture, it was *interrupted*. The subject's regret about this interruption is observable in subsequent issues.

**Leverage.** The crew has no operational leverage. The *memory* of the crew, however, functions similarly to the Sammy anchor — proof to the subject that he can do honest work and be tolerated as a person. Operators wishing to support a re-entry attempt should note the Chicago period as a working template.

---

## 8. THE SHELTERED, THE BULLIED, AND THE NAMELESS CHILD — The Recurring Stranger-Protégé

**Pattern.** Across decades and writers, the subject has incidentally intervened on behalf of children and obvious underdogs in public settings — a child being yelled at in a diner, a small mutant being cornered in an alley, a non-combatant caught in a crossfire he himself initiated. The pattern is unsignposted in most arcs and is best read across the full canon rather than in any single issue.

**Operational signature.** Identical to the Sammy and crew-modulation patterns: voice softens, posture lowers, body intervenes. He does not ask the child's name; he does not stay. He resumes whatever he was doing — frequently violent — with the protected party safely out of frame.

**Significance.** This is the single most reliable prosocial micro-behavior in the file. It is so consistent across writers as to constitute a *trait* rather than a *choice*. Operators predicting his behavior in any crowd scene should weight this pattern heavily: collateral risk to identifiably small or visibly-othered bystanders is substantially lower than the gross destruction profile would predict.

---

## 9. CYTTORAK — Patron, Parasite, Surrogate Father

*Catalogued here, against ordinary convention, because the entity functions in the subject's psychic economy as the closest thing he has to a *mentor* — a granting, withdrawing, demanding paternal authority.*

**Origin.** *X-Men* #12; Korean cave; the inscription, the touch, the transformation.

**Operational pattern.** Cyttorak grants power conditional on the subject's continued performance of destruction. The subject's relationship to this contract is the deepest unresolved structure in his life. He resents the conditionality; he depends on the supply; he treats withdrawals as betrayals and reinstatements as homecomings. The dynamic is, structurally, a repetition of the Kurt Marko relationship — a more powerful male authority who gives and withholds, whose approval is contingent on the subject's worst behavior, and whose absence leaves him diminished.

**Trust architecture.** None. The subject does not trust Cyttorak; he is *bonded* to Cyttorak in the way an addict is bonded to a substance and a beaten child is bonded to his father.

**Failure mode.** Every depowering. Each is experienced as an amputation and a paternal abandonment. Each is followed by a reclamation drive that overrides every other commitment, including, on record, every bond catalogued above.

**Leverage.** Total in one direction, none in the other. This is the most dangerous structure in the file and the single greatest predictor of relapse from any prosocial trajectory the subject undertakes. Any intervention plan that does not address the Cyttorak bond directly will fail on a long enough timeline.

---

## 10. MARGINAL AND SINGLE-ARC ALLIES — Brief Catalogue

- **Spider-Man.** Antagonist by default; situational ally in cosmic-threat scenarios. The subject's grudging respect is real — Spider-Man's combination of *small body* and *refusal to stay down* registers as a category the subject does not have a hostility template for. He hits Spider-Man harder than necessary and apologizes (in his own register, by *not* hitting again) more often than recorded.
- **The Hulk.** Not an ally in the relational sense; a *peer* in the somatic sense. The subject's interactions with the Hulk are the only ones in which his bravado is appropriate to his ability. He is calmer around the Hulk than around most of his stated allies. There is no friendship; there is recognition.
- **Various Genoshan, Madripoor, and Eastern-European criminal hosts.** Hospitality networks rather than bonds. The subject is, by underworld standards, a polite houseguest.
- **The Krakoan-era mutant collective (peripheral).** The subject's relationship to organized mutantdom in the Krakoa era is uncharacteristically *quiet*. He is present, he is tolerated, he tolerates. The bond is to the *idea* of belonging rather than to individuals; it is the closest he has come to a civic identity, and it is shallow precisely because it is broad.

---

## SYNTHESIS — THE SHAPE OF THE ALLY MAP

The file shows, against the surface presentation, a man with a *small but real* prosocial roster, sustained by an unusually consistent set of preconditions: the other party must not require articulation of the wound, must not invoke the stepbrother, must not attempt management, must not threaten the identity, and must accept the somatic fact of his body without flinching and without spectacle. Where these conditions are met, the subject is loyal across decades and capable of grief, humor, deference, and protection. Where they are not met, no bond stabilizes regardless of the other party's intent.

The single deepest implication is operational: the subject is not bondless and not unsalvageable. He is *narrowly* bondable. The list of people who have ever fully met his conditions is short — Cassidy, Sammy, the Chicago crew, intermittently Wagner, asymptotically Xavier — but the existence of the list is the entire counter-evidence to the file's grimmer surface readings.

The Juggernaut is the armor the boy built. The people catalogued above are the only ones who have ever, in any sustained way, gotten the boy to look out from inside it.

*— End Module 7-B. See 7-C for Relationships III (Romantic, Sexual, and Pseudo-Familial Surrogates) and 7-D for Relationships IV (Subordinates, Hires, and Coerced Associates).*


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*Dossier section. Cross-reference: Relationships I (Family of Origin), Relationships II (Chosen Kin & Allies). The subject's relational map sorts cleanly into three operative modes — surrogate-target, peer-companion, protector — established in §5 of the Workup. This section catalogues every adversarial relationship of operational significance and every intimate/sexual attachment for which there is canonical or strongly inferrable record. Entries are ordered by depth of file, not chronology.*

---

## I. RIVALS & ENEMIES — THE PERMANENT FIGURES

### 1. CHARLES FRANCIS XAVIER — stepbrother, lifelong adversary, primary surrogate-target

**File depth.** The thickest single relational file in the dossier. Sixty years of recorded contact across approximately every era of the subject's public life.

**Origin.** Kurt Marko married Sharon Xavier after the death of Brian Xavier; Cain (Kurt's son by a previous union) entered the Xavier household at approximately age ten to twelve. Within months the stable pattern was established: Kurt beat Cain in private, praised Charles in public. Charles — already telepathic — registered Cain's beatings empathically, an unforgivable trespass for which Cain has never named the actual grievance but has spent six decades enacting it.

**Dynamic.** The cleanest documented displacement in the subject's psychology. Charles did not hit Cain; Charles was loved by the man who hit Cain. The wound is *comparative*, not *agentive*, and this is precisely what makes it inextinguishable: there is no act of contrition Charles can perform, because Charles's offense is *existence as the favored child*. Every reconciliation attempt founders on this fact. Xavier has, across decades, extended sincere amnesty (post-Onslaught, the Austen recruitment, multiple later overtures); Cain has accepted each one and then violated it, usually under a triggering event — depowering, humiliation by a third party, bar-night drift back into Black Tom's orbit — that returns him to the original injury.

**Evolution.** Three phases.
- *Phase one (Korea through the 1980s):* unbroken hostility, ritualized monthly-grudge contact. Cain travels continents to attack Xavier in person; Xavier defends and contains rather than retaliates, which Cain experiences as further condescension.
- *Phase two (Onslaught through Austen):* genuine softening, the closest the relationship has ever been to functional. Cain lived at the mansion. Xavier addressed him as a brother. The tenure lasted as long as the surrounding conditions held; Sammy Paré's death collapsed it.
- *Phase three (Krakoa era through Bunn's reset and after):* exhausted, intermittent, with longer pauses between conflicts. Both are old. Neither expects resolution.

**Trust / safety.** Asymmetric and inverted from the surface presentation. Xavier *trusts* Cain in the operational sense — he believes Cain will not lie about an intention, and he believes Cain's protective impulses toward children are real. Cain *does not trust* Xavier in any sense, because Xavier's telepathy means Cain cannot verify what is or is not being read off him. The helmet is the architectural expression of this. Xavier is the only person in the world the subject categorically wears armor *against*, including in moments of nominal peace.

**Failure mode.** Any framing — gentle, oblique, or accidental — that places Charles in the moral-superior position. Xavier saying "I forgive you" is more provocative than Xavier throwing a punch.

**Leverage.** For an operator hoping to *contain* the subject through Xavier: none reliable. For an operator hoping to *enrage* the subject through Xavier: trivial. Mention the stepbrother by the wrong name, the wrong honorific, or the wrong tone, and the curve in §5 begins.

---

### 2. CYTTORAK — patron deity, transactional master, ontological landlord

**File depth.** Decades of indirect documentation, intensified in the Aaron, Bunn, and *Sins of Sinister* eras when the relationship was foregrounded as character rather than backdrop.

**Origin.** The Korean cave. A crimson gem; an inscription. A panicked deserter grabbing the first thing offered. Cyttorak is a Crimson Cosmos demon-god of destruction, one of the Octessence; the subject is his *avatar*, not his employee. The covenant is reciprocal but radically unequal: Cyttorak provides power; the subject is expected to *destroy*. Periods of restraint, prosocial behavior, or X-Men membership constitute breach. Cyttorak has, multiple times, withdrawn the gift in response.

**Dynamic.** This is the single most important relationship in the subject's life that he cannot displace, deflect, or punch. Cyttorak is exactly what Kurt Marko was: a larger, judging male power that gives and withholds favor based on performance. The structural identity is almost embarrassing. The subject's compliance with Cyttorak's expectations is therefore overdetermined — not only does he want the power, he wants the *approval* of the giver, in a way he has never quite verbalized.

**Evolution.** Early period (1965 through 1990s): the relationship is implicit, mythic, off-screen. The subject behaves as Cyttorak wishes without knowing he is being audited. Middle period (Aaron's *Original Sin* / "Sacred Invasions" arcs): Cyttorak becomes a speaking presence; the subject is told, baldly, that he has been *insufficiently destructive* and that the avatarship is conditional. Late period (Bunn 2020 onward): the subject lives with the conditionality openly. He knows the gem can leave. He builds his identity around the knowledge that the body he wears is rented.

**Trust / safety.** None. Cyttorak is not trustworthy and the subject knows it. The relationship persists because the alternative is the small body.

**Failure mode.** The subject's brief experiments with restraint (X-Men tenure; Bunn-era sobriety) trigger divine displeasure and depowering. He has learned, the hard way, that virtue costs him his face.

**Leverage.** Catastrophic in both directions. Whoever can speak credibly *for* Cyttorak — false avatars (D'Spayre proxies, the brief usurpations of the gem by other vessels) — can move the subject. Whoever can credibly *threaten* his standing with Cyttorak destabilizes him completely.

---

### 3. THE HULK / BRUCE BANNER — measuring stick, recurring physical adversary

**File depth.** Decades of intermittent but high-visibility contact, beginning *Incredible Hulk* #172 (1973), recurring through Defenders, *World War Hulk*, and beyond.

**Origin.** Two unstoppable bodies in the same Marvel Universe; collision was structural inevitability. The first encounter ended ambiguously. Subsequent encounters have been catalogued by both parties as the unresolved question: *which of us is bigger.*

**Dynamic.** Almost purely somatic. There is no ideological dispute, no grievance, no betrayal. The Hulk is the one opponent against whom the subject's central organizing fantasy — *I will never be the smaller body in the room* — is genuinely in question. This makes the Hulk uniquely interesting to the subject and uniquely dangerous. Bar bragging rights aside, the subject's documented post-fight affect after Hulk encounters is *charged*, almost satisfied, regardless of outcome — the way a man feels after the only conversation that week in which he was taken seriously.

**Evolution.** Early bouts were taunting, dominance-display affairs. Later encounters (*World War Hulk* especially) showed the subject actually outmatched by a Hulk operating at extreme amplification, which produced a rare flash of the Nimrod-style brittleness — the bravado cracked. Most recent encounters are wearier, almost ritualized; both bodies have been doing this a long time.

**Trust / safety.** Operationally: both parties are honest about wanting to hit each other. Neither schemes. This is, paradoxically, the *cleanest* adversarial relationship in the file.

**Failure mode.** When the Hulk wins decisively, the subject is destabilized for weeks. When the subject wins decisively, he becomes briefly insufferable, with downstream costs to Black Tom and others around him.

**Leverage.** Banner the man, not the Hulk, has occasionally reached the subject — calm, scientific, slightly sad address registers with the subject in the same key as Xavier's voice without the comparative wound attached. There is the makings of a friendship there that neither party has ever quite pursued.

---

### 4. THOR ODINSON — divine-tier opponent, hammer-figure

**File depth.** Substantial. Recurring across the *Thor* and *Avengers* titles, decisively centered in *Fear Itself* (2011) when the subject became Kuurth, Breaker of Stone — one of Thor's Worthy adversaries.

**Origin.** Standard pantheon-collision opening; the subject's reputation as a moving wall drew Asgardian attention.

**Dynamic.** Thor occupies a peculiar slot: he is a paternal-coded male authority figure of overwhelming power who has, on multiple occasions, *hit the subject and made it stick*. The subject's relationship to Thor is therefore tinged with something his relationship to most opponents lacks: respect under the hostility. He does not mock Thor as he mocks the X-Men.

**Evolution.** *Fear Itself* is the irreversible event. Receiving the Kuurth hammer placed the subject in a relationship of *fealty* to a corrupting Asgardian power (the Serpent) parallel to but distinct from his Cyttorak avatarship — and the post-event recovery left him with the memory of having leveled Las Vegas without coherent reason. Thor was the figure who finally stopped him. There is, in subsequent encounters, a wary acknowledgment between them.

**Trust / safety.** Limited but real. The subject would not, unprompted, attack Thor on a normal day.

**Failure mode.** Asgardian artifacts, runes, hammers, or anything else mystical-and-amplifying placed within the subject's reach will be picked up. The Korean cave instinct never went away.

**Leverage.** Thor is one of three or four figures in the universe whose direct verbal command the subject would actually consider obeying — not from obedience, but from the recognition that defiance costs more than compliance.

---

### 5. NIMROD — the original brittleness exposure

**File depth.** Concentrated in *Uncanny X-Men* #194 (1985) but doctrinally definitive.

**Origin.** A Sentinel from a possible future, dropped into the present, who fought the Juggernaut and *won*. The subject's response: visible fear, an unprecedented appeal to teamwork with the X-Men, retreat.

**Dynamic.** Not an ongoing relationship — a *diagnostic event*. Nimrod is the data point that established, in canon, that the unstoppability is a story the subject tells himself and that the body underneath remembers being stoppable. Every operator with access to this file should treat Nimrod as the proof-of-concept for the §4 finding that the grandiosity is fragile.

**Failure mode / leverage.** Sufficient demonstrated overpowering — not bluffed, demonstrated — collapses the presentation immediately. The subject does not die well; he panics first.

---

### 6. ONSLAUGHT — the de-bodying event

**File depth.** *Onslaught Saga*, 1996. Single arc, life-defining consequence.

**Origin.** Onslaught (the Xavier-Magneto psychic gestalt) tore the subject's helmet off, reached inside his mind, and extracted the Cyttorak essence directly — leaving Cain Marko as a hollowed, shrunken man inside the empty armor.

**Dynamic.** Not a person; an experience. But the file treats it as a relational entry because the perpetrator was, in part, Xavier — meaning the subject's deepest fear (telepathic intrusion via the stepbrother) was literalized at maximum amplitude. The injury Onslaught did to the subject is the injury the subject has spent his whole life building the helmet to prevent. That it happened *through* Xavier's mind, even an Xavier-gone-wrong, has never been fully metabolized.

**Leverage.** Reference to the extraction event, the empty armor, or the moment of being seen-while-small produces the most reliable shame response in the catalogue. Use with extreme caution; it tends to convert directly to violence.

---

### 7. THE X-MEN AS A COLLECTIVE — long-running adversary class

**File depth.** Continuous from 1965 onward.

**Dynamic.** The X-Men are, in the subject's operational schema, *Xavier's house.* They are the people who stand between him and Charles. He has fought every roster generation. Specific sub-rivalries warrant brief annotation:

- *Wolverine.* Mutual physical respect, bar-tested. Logan has bought the subject drinks and stabbed him in roughly equal measure. Closest thing to a peer-companion the subject has within the X-orbit; the file would not be surprised by future thaw.
- *Colossus.* The other immovable object. Power-comparison rival; the subject treats Piotr with grudging fairness, the way one large man treats another large man.
- *Cyclops.* Authority-coded irritant; cleanest avatar of "Charles's chosen son." The subject's distaste is direct.
- *Storm.* Has commanded the subject's reluctant deference; weather-tier power registers in the same key as Thor.
- *Rogue.* The one X-Man who could, in principle, *take* the gem from him via skin contact. He keeps mental note.

**Failure mode for the X-Men as a class.** Treating the subject as a unitary villain misses the §5 finding that protector-mode is live in him. The X-Men have, on rare occasions, accidentally activated it (a child mutant in danger mid-battle, etc.), with mission-disrupting consequences for both sides.

---

### 8. THE EXEMPLARS / OCTESSENCE RIVALS — pantheon-adjacent

**File depth.** Concentrated in the late-1990s Exemplars arc and intermittent later.

**Origin.** The other seven Octessence-empowered avatars (representing Krakkan, Watoomb, Balthakk, etc.). The subject is, structurally, one of eight.

**Dynamic.** Sibling rivalry at the cosmic tier. The subject is uncomfortable being *one of* anything. Reduces him from singular Juggernaut to *Cyttorak's pick*, which is a comparison wound in the same family as Charles. He has fought several Exemplars and cooperated with none willingly.

---

### 9. SPIDER-MAN — recurring incidental adversary

**File depth.** *Amazing Spider-Man* #229–230 (1982), the legendary "Nothing Can Stop the Juggernaut" two-parter, plus ~dozen subsequent encounters.

**Dynamic.** Asymmetric in physics, weirdly symmetrical in temperament. The subject finds Spider-Man's chatter genuinely annoying in a way that distinguishes him from most opponents — Parker's running mouth scratches at the same shame node that Xavier's tone does, because both communicate a presumed moral high ground from a smaller body. The 1982 encounter, in which Parker drowned the subject in wet concrete, is one of the few documented losses the subject has rationalized rather than processed.

**Leverage.** Almost none. Spider-Man's effective tactics against the subject have all been environmental, not interpersonal.

---

### 10. THE AVENGERS / GENERAL HERO COMMUNITY — diffuse adversary

The subject's relationship with the broader hero population is *transactional*. He has fought most of them at some point. He holds no specific grudges except where individual encounters cross into the surrogate-target schema (Captain America's moral framing irritates him; Iron Man's wealth and condescension irritate him; the Fantastic Four's family unit reads to him as a curated insult he cannot articulate). The Avengers as an institution he treats roughly as he treats the X-Men: Xavier's-house, larger denomination.

---

### 11. D'SPAYRE — psychological predator, rare opponent who saw the file

**File depth.** Limited but qualitatively unique.

**Dynamic.** The fear-demon D'Spayre is the only canonical adversary who attacked the subject *through* the small-body wound directly, rather than physically. The subject's response was disproportionate panic followed by disproportionate rage. The file's takeaway: any operator who reads the subject psychologically rather than somatically is operating from a position of asymmetric advantage. Almost no one bothers.

---

## II. INTIMATE / LOVERS — THE SPARSE FILE

A note on this section's brevity. The subject's intimate-partner record is among the thinnest of any major Marvel figure of his vintage. This is itself a finding. The §3 attachment profile (disorganized, fearful-avoidant under demand, tolerant only of low-demand companionship) predicts exactly this pattern: a man who can hold a sixty-year friendship with Black Tom but cannot hold a romance for a season. What exists in the file is sparse, intermittent, and almost entirely consistent with the same architecture.

---

### 1. THE TAVERN AND BARRACK PATTERN — generalized intimate behavior, decades

**File depth.** Cumulative, low-detail, observed across many writers' background panels.

**Pattern.** The subject's sexual life, where depicted, occurs in the same operational ecology as his drinking: bar pickups, brief encounters, no follow-through. Partners (overwhelmingly women, mostly working-class adult, generally his physical scale or larger-than-average) are chosen for the same criteria that govern his friendships — *low demand, no evaluation, no comparison.* The subject is not predatory in these encounters; the file finds no record of coercion. He is, however, entirely uninterested in continuity.

**Dynamic.** Sex appears to function, for the subject, as another somatic-regulation tool in the same family as alcohol and combat. It discharges; it does not bond. Post-coital affect, where depicted, is flat or slightly melancholic, never tender.

**Failure mode.** Any partner who attempts to extend the encounter into a relationship is met with the avoidance pattern: he leaves town, returns to Tom, or vanishes into a depowering arc. There is no record of him explicitly rejecting a partner with cruelty; he simply ceases to be available.

**Leverage.** Effectively none. Sexual access has not been demonstrated to move the subject's behavior in any documented case.

---

### 2. "SWEET SARAH" / SHORT-DURATION ATTACHMENTS IN THE BUNN-ERA SOLO RUN (2020)

**File depth.** The 2020 *Juggernaut* miniseries (Bunn) is the closest the canon comes to depicting the subject in something resembling a domestic life. Depowered, working construction, attempting sobriety, the subject is shown in brief, hesitant contact with women in his orbit — neighbors, coworkers, the occasional acquaintance — none developing into formal romance.

**Dynamic.** What the Bunn arc establishes is that the subject is *capable* of the early stages of intimate connection when stripped of the Juggernaut presentation. He can have a conversation. He can buy a coffee. The connections do not progress because the underlying architecture has not changed: as soon as the gem returns, the small-body identity reactivates as the *hidden* identity, and intimacy requires showing it.

**Failure mode.** Re-powering. Every time.

---

### 3. SHARON XAVIER — mother-figure (cross-reference Relationships I)

*Not a lover. Listed here because the maternal vacancy structures the lover file.* Sharon was distant, ill, dependent, and died early. The subject's adult women have, with no exceptions worth noting, occupied the *opposite* template — physically robust, emotionally undemanding, present-tense. He has organized his intimate life around being unable to recapitulate his mother's frailty, which means he has also organized it around being unable to be cared for.

---

### 4. BLACK TOM CASSIDY — the relationship the file cannot cleanly classify

**File depth.** See Relationships II for the full peer-companion entry. Listed here because the question of whether the Marko–Cassidy bond contains an intimate or romantic dimension recurs in fan reading and is occasionally gestured at in canon (shared apartments, vacations, the depth of mutual mourning, the tactility of their reunions).

**File position.** The dossier does not make a determination. What can be said with confidence:

- The bond is the deepest sustained attachment of the subject's life.
- It satisfies the §3 criteria for the only relational configuration the subject can tolerate: low-demand, non-evaluative, hierarchy-stable.
- Whether it has at any point included a physical/romantic dimension is not on the record. The subject's behavioral profile would be consistent with either reading.
- Whether or not the relationship is romantic in the conventional sense, it functions as the subject's *primary attachment*. Operationally that is what matters.
