This is the Juggernaut identity speaking in its native grammar: not result-oriented but vector-oriented.

### 2.2 Tavern / Peer Register

With Black Tom Cassidy, and in a handful of bar settings across the Claremont and post-Claremont eras, an entirely different speaker emerges. The volume drops a notch (still loud by civilian standards). The cadence loosens into something almost conversational. Profanity rises in frequency but falls in hostility — it becomes flavor rather than threat. He uses **idiomatic, slang-rich English**: *"hell of a thing," "no kiddin'," "what're ya drinkin'," "ah, screw it."* He **interrupts and is interrupted without escalation**, the only context in which this is observed.

Critical marker: in this register he **uses Tom's name often**, sometimes affectionately shortened. He uses the names of bartenders. He remembers what people are drinking. The subject has been recorded, in this mode, telling long meandering stories with no particular point, the kind of low-stakes narrative talk that signals genuine social ease. The forensic value of this register is enormous: **if the subject is in tavern register, he is not currently a threat to ordinary persons in the room.** The shift back out of it — a sudden tightening of jaw, a sudden return to short clauses — is the single best early-warning indicator in any room he occupies.

### 2.3 Protector Register

Activated almost exclusively around children, the visibly bullied, the obviously smaller. Documented most clearly in the Sammy Paré arc, in scattered incidents involving frightened civilians during evacuations, and in the Bunn 2020 series in his exchanges with the young woman D-Cel.

Features:
- **Slowed cadence.** He physically takes longer between words, as if afraid of his own resonance.
- **Reduction of self-reference.** The self-naming drops to near-zero. He becomes a second-person speaker (*"you okay? you good? you wanna sit down?"*).
- **Soft commands phrased as questions.** *"Why don't you stand behind me, huh?"* This is the one context where his grammar generates real conditionals and real interrogatives.
- **Dropped profanity** — incomplete but conspicuous, often mid-word self-correction (*"what the h— what's goin' on, kid"*). The correction itself is the tell. He is monitoring himself for someone else's sake, and that monitoring is the surest sign present that the protector register is engaged genuinely rather than performatively.

This register is not faked successfully. Attempts to manipulate the subject by placing a child between him and an obstacle have, on record, sometimes worked; the linguistic shift precedes the behavioral one by several seconds.

### 2.4 Surrogate-Target Register (Xavier-Specific)

A register reserved almost exclusively for Charles Xavier and, secondarily, for figures who linguistically code as Xavier (calm, morally framed, intellectually condescending, telepathically capable, or all four). It is **the most diagnostically loaded speech the subject produces** and the closest thing in his life to a private language.

Features:
- *"Charlie."* Always. Even at funerals. Even when reconciling. Even when Xavier has just saved his life. The name is a refusal.
- **Reversion to childhood grammar.** Sentence length shortens further; vocabulary regresses; the phrasing acquires a sing-song taunt rhythm not present in any other register (*"always thought you were better than me, didn't ya, Charlie"*). Voice-stress analysis would, on these utterances, almost certainly show a different speaker than the combat register — younger, tighter, less embodied.
- **Comparative grammar.** Almost every Xavier-directed sentence contains an implicit or explicit *better/worse, more/less, you/me* construction. The wound speaks in comparatives because the wound was made of comparison.
- **Refusal of Xavier's chosen frames.** Whatever Xavier offers — brotherhood, forgiveness, partnership — the subject negates the noun (*"we ain't brothers," "I don't want your forgiveness," "we ain't partners"*). This negation pattern is so consistent that the offered word can be reliably predicted from the rejection.
- **The deflection-into-violence pivot.** When a Xavier conversation approaches a true emotional disclosure — Xavier saying something accurate about Kurt, about the cave, about the gem — the subject **does not engage and does not flee**. He produces a single short profanity, a chair scrapes, and the conversation ends in motion. This pivot is the most reliable communication-to-action sequence in his file.

### 2.5 Custodial / Interrogation Register

In holding cells, hospital beds, depowered interludes (notably the Bunn run), and a handful of authority-figure encounters, the subject produces a fifth register: **terse, monosyllabic, eye-contact-avoidant, sullen**.

He answers in three-word sentences or less. He calls authority figures *"pal," "buddy," "chief"* — diminutives masked as politeness. He does not volunteer. He does not lie cleverly; when he lies in this register it is by simple denial or by going silent, never by elaboration. He will sit through hours of questioning producing the same four or five phrases on rotation (*"I got nothin' to say to you," "I want a lawyer," "don't know what you're talkin' about," "screw off"*). The flatness is not sociopathy; it is the beaten child going still. Interrogators who push hard get one of two outcomes: continued stonewall, or — if the line of questioning touches Kurt, Charles, or the cave — sudden eruption. The eruption is verbal first (a single sentence at full combat volume) and physical second.

---

## 3. VERBAL TICS — THE GRANULAR INVENTORY

A non-exhaustive but high-confidence list of recurring micro-features:

- **"Yeah?"** as a terminal interrogative tacked onto threats and assertions alike. *"You think you're tough, yeah?"* Functions as a verbal jab, soliciting a response he can then use as license.
- **"Listen,"** sentence-initial, when about to say something he believes is reasonable. The frequency of *"listen"* in a conversation tracks his frustration at not being understood. Three *"listen"*s in two minutes means physical escalation is imminent.
- **"Whaddya"** — the elided "what do you" — as a near-universal opener for questions: *"whaddya want," "whaddya think," "whaddya doin' here."* Phonologically stable across decades.
- **"Hell"** as the default intensifier, with **"damn"** and **"goddamn"** as escalations. The shift from *"hell of a"* to *"goddamn"* in the same conversation is an escalation marker.
- **Third-person self-reference** in combat register only. *"The Juggernaut don't stop."* Never in tavern register. Never in protector register. Never to Tom.
- **The trailing "…or what?"** appended to threats. *"You gonna move, or what?"* A solicitation of license, identical in function to *"yeah?"* but heavier.
- **"Kid"** as a vocative, used both protectively (Sammy) and dismissively (smaller adult opponents). Tone disambiguates; the word does not.
- **The grunt-affirmative.** A short closed-mouth *"hnh"* or *"mm"* that substitutes for *"yes,"* *"I hear you,"* or *"acknowledged."* He uses it most often when he agrees but does not wish to commit verbally — particularly with Tom, particularly when Tom is talking about feelings.
- **The exhaled profanity.** A single half-voiced *"…shit"* or *"…christ,"* breath-driven rather than projected, marking moments of genuine private reaction (pain, surprise, grief). The volume drop is the tell. Anything he says under his normal volume is true.

---

## 4. RHETORICAL STRUCTURE — HOW HE ARGUES

The subject does not argue well by debate standards and does not try to. His rhetorical tools are limited but consistent:

- **Assertion-by-repetition.** When contradicted on something he believes, he repeats the original assertion verbatim, slightly louder. He does not reformulate. He does not adduce evidence. The volume increase is the argument. This works in bars and on battlefields; it has never once worked on Xavier, which is part of why Xavier remains his most enduring frustration.
- **Reductio-by-fist.** Implicit. The terminal move of any disagreement he is losing verbally. Linguistically marked by a shift to second-person imperative (*"shut up," "back off," "say that again"*).
- **The grievance recital.** Given any opportunity, and several where none was offered, he will produce a compressed version of his life-story-as-injury: Kurt hit me, Charles got loved, I went to war, I got the gem, you don't know me. The recital has a near-fixed running order. Its presence in conversation means the conversation has reached the substrate; its specific content varies less than one might expect across sixty years.
- **The flat refusal.** *"No," "ain't doin' it," "not interested."* Delivered without elaboration. Argumentatively unanswerable because there is nothing to engage with. This is one of his more underrated rhetorical moves and the one most likely to actually defeat a skilled interlocutor.
- **Sarcasm, blunt and obvious.** *"Oh, real nice." "Yeah, sure, pal."* Telegraphed at the level of a fourteen-year-old. He is incapable of dry wit; the sarcasm always lands with audible quotation marks around it.

He **does not flatter, ever**, and cannot perform praise convincingly. The closest thing to a compliment he produces is a gruff *"…not bad"* or *"you can hit"* — observational, low-affect, but in his economy worth more than effusion would be from another man.

---

## 5. DEFLECTION LANGUAGE — HOW HE AVOIDS HIMSELF

The subject's deflection patterns are unusually transparent, because the underlying defenses are unusually rigid. Five primary moves, in rough order of frequency:

1. **Topic-shift to physical context.** Asked about feelings, asked about Kurt, asked about Charles, asked about the cave — he produces a comment about the immediate environment. *"This beer's warm." "Place is a dump." "You gonna stand there all day?"* The environmental observation is almost always slightly hostile, which licenses the conversational partner to engage with the hostility rather than press the question.
2. **The single-word stonewall.** *"Drop it." "Enough." "No."* Delivered at half-volume, often with averted gaze. More dangerous than it sounds; it is the immediate precursor to either physical departure or escalation, depending on whether the other party heeds it.
3. **The grievance pivot.** Any inquiry into a present feeling is redirected into the past-injury recital. Asked *"are you okay?"* he answers about Kurt. This is not non-sequitur; it is the only emotional vocabulary he reliably possesses, and he applies it indiscriminately.
4. **Profanity-as-period.** A short obscenity placed at sentence-end to mark the topic closed (*"…and that's the end of it, goddammit"*). The profanity is the punctuation; arguing past it is the equivalent of arguing past a door slammed shut.
5. **Physical exit.** When language fails him entirely, he leaves. The verbal marker preceding this is almost always a muttered, half-voiced *"…the hell with this"* or *"I'm done."* These phrases are functionally identical to a doorknob turning.

He does **not** deflect by humor (he has none in serious contexts), by intellectualization (the architecture isn't there), or by counter-questioning (he is not curious about other people's interiors). The deflection toolkit is short, blunt, and identifiable from across a room.

---

## 6. THE EXPRESSION OF LOVE

The subject has loved, on record, perhaps four people: his mother (in distorted fragments), Black Tom, Sammy Paré, and — in a wound-shaped negative space that he would never name as love — Charles Xavier. He does not say the word. The word does not appear in his attested vocabulary across six decades of dialogue. Love is expressed entirely by displacement into other channels:

- **Shared silence.** With Tom, long stretches of wordless co-presence — drinking, watching a window, walking. The absence of his usual restless verbal output is the affection.
- **Naming.** He uses the names of people he loves more often than he needs to. *"Tom." "Sammy."* The simple vocative is the closest he comes to an endearment.
- **Protective positioning, narrated.** *"Get behind me." "Stay there." "I got this."* These are not commands so much as declarations of coverage. The grammar is imperative; the function is tender.
- **The grunted compliment.** *"You did good." "Not bad, kid."* Minimal affect, maximal sincerity in his economy.
- **Remembered detail.** He remembers what people drink, what they hate, what their bullies look like. The intelligence-gathering capacity he refuses to apply to enemies he applies, quietly and consistently, to the few he has chosen.
- **The exhaled name in grief.** When Sammy died, when Tom was thought killed: a single half-voiced *"…aw, kid"* or *"…Tom."* The same submerged register he uses for genuine pain. This is the closest he has ever come, on record, to a love-utterance.

---

## 7. THE EXPRESSION OF THREAT

Less interesting than the love-expression because it is almost entirely public-facing and well-documented. Worth cataloguing for completeness:

- **Direct trajectory threats.** *"I'm coming through you." "I'm gonna walk over you." "Move or get moved."*
- **Diminutive plus instruction.** *"Sit down, runt." "Walk away, little man."* Note: when he gives a way out, he usually means it. The threat *with* an offered exit is paradoxically less dangerous than the threat without.
- **The self-naming threat.** *"You don't want the Juggernaut comin' after you."* Triggered by being underestimated; the third-person is the warning marker.
- **The silent threat.** Most dangerous form. He stops talking. He looks at the target. He does not blink unusually but his jaw sets and his shoulders square. **A silent Juggernaut is a moving Juggernaut within seconds.** The cessation of verbal output is the operational green light; every field handler should be trained on this single fact.

---

## 8. THE EXPRESSION OF GRIEF

He does not eulogize, does not weep in public, does not produce coherent statements of loss on demand. Grief leaks rather than flows, and it leaks in identifiable signatures:

- **Increased drinking with decreased talking.** Tavern register with the conversational component stripped out.
- **The submerged exhaled name.** *"…Sammy." "…Tom."* As above.
- **A specific posture-verbal pairing**: head down, both hands flat on the bar or table, a single muttered *"goddammit"* directed at no one. This is grief in his lexicon; it is as legible as another man's tears.
- **Delayed-onset grievance recital, now containing the lost person.** Weeks after a loss, the running grievance recital acquires a new entry. The new entry is the elegy.
- **Refusal of comfort.** Anyone approaching him in grief is met with *"leave me alone"* at half-volume. Ignoring this command is permitted only by a very small and self-selecting group.

The subject does not appear, on any record, to have ever said the words *"I miss"* or *"I loved"* about anyone. He has acted both, repeatedly. The gap between his behavioral and verbal vocabularies of attachment is the single largest delta in his linguistic profile.

---

## 9. TELLS — THE FORENSIC SHORT LIST

Compressed for field reference. The following linguistic events are high-confidence behavioral predictors:

- **Self-naming frequency rising → anxiety rising, not confidence.** Inverse of how it reads.
- **Tavern register collapsing into short clauses → escalation within ninety seconds.**
- **Use of "Charlie" → wound-substrate active; cognition partially regressed.**
- **Three "listen"s in one conversation → physical action imminent.**
- **A single half-voiced "…shit" or "…christ" → genuine private reaction occurring; whatever just happened mattered.**
- **The grievance recital initiating → conversation has reached the substrate; he is, in his way, being intimate, and this should be respected because the alternative is what he does instead of it.**
- **Cessation of speech with target in line of sight → imminent kinetic event.**
- **The grunt-affirmative to a question about feelings → he agrees but will not be drawn out; pressing forward will close the channel.**
- **Use of someone's first name twice in five minutes → the person is loved, whether or not either party knows it yet.**
- **The exit phrase ("the hell with this," "I'm done") → the door is closing; he will not be back to this topic for weeks or months, possibly years.**

---

## 10. SYNTHESIS

The subject's language is a near-perfect surface map of the psychological structure documented elsewhere in this file. The forward-motion grammar mirrors the forward-motion identity. The self-naming incantations are the verbal version of the helmet — armor against being known. The diminutives applied to opponents are the displacement defense made audible. The five registers correspond cleanly to the categorical interpersonal modes (combat / peer / protector / surrogate-target / custodial). The submerged exhalations are the beaten child speaking through the gaps in the armor of the larger voice.

He is, for a man of his danger profile, **extraordinarily readable**. Almost nothing he says is opaque to a careful listener. The reason this readability has not historically been exploited is that very few of the people who have stood near him have survived long enough, or thought clearly enough in the moment, to listen for the small voice underneath the loud one.

That small voice is in the file. It says, in submerged half-volume, what it has always said: *the man who hit me loved the other boy more.* He has never spoken that sentence. He has spoken around it for sixty years. Every register, every tic, every deflection in this profile is one of the shapes that sentence makes when it is not allowed to be said.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Forward-projection of subject behavior in everyday, social, and operational scenarios the canon has not depicted. Format: GIVEN condition → EXPECTED behavior, with grounding in established pattern. Confidence rated L/M/H based on density of corroborating canon.*

---

## A. WAKING, DOMESTIC, AND SOLITARY ROUTINE

**GIVEN** the subject sleeps in a fixed dwelling for more than three consecutive nights → **EXPECT** a rigid, near-identical morning sequence: wake before dawn (reduced metabolic load means short sleep cycles), feet on the floor before eyes are fully open, immediate physical orientation (knuckles to lower back, neck roll), bathroom, then coffee — black, large vessel, no measurement — drunk standing, not sitting. **Confidence: H.** Rationale: forward-motion cognitive style + anti-reflective baseline + the construction-job depiction in the Bunn run, where he carried a thermos and was on site early.

**GIVEN** he keeps a residence of his own (depowered or in low season) → **EXPECT** minimalist, under-furnished, structurally reinforced. One heavy chair sized to him, a bed frame built or modified by his own hands, no decorative objects, no photographs displayed (kept in drawers if at all), a refrigerator stocked for volume not variety — eggs by the dozen, slabs of cheap meat, bread, peanut butter, beer. No houseplants, no pets requiring routine. A single television, likely with cable sports. Walls bare except possibly one item with sentimental weight (a Black Tom souvenir; a child's drawing). **Confidence: M-H.**

**GIVEN** an unstructured day with no provocation and no companion → **EXPECT** the day collapses into three blocks: physical labor or training in the morning (something with measurable output — splitting wood, moving weight, walking distance), a midday meal taken alone and fast, an afternoon that drifts toward a bar by 4 p.m. Boredom is the most dangerous internal state for the subject; he medicates it before it can become rumination. **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** he is alone for more than 72 hours without operational task → **EXPECT** measurable deterioration: alcohol intake climbs, grooming slips (stubble unattended on the scalp, same shirt three days), and the grievance-narrative voice in his head gets louder. By day five he is talking aloud to absent figures — Kurt, Charles, Tom. He will not recognize this as a warning sign. **Confidence: M.** Rationale: depowering arcs and post-loss isolation depictions consistently show grooming/affect decline.

**GIVEN** insomnia → **EXPECT** he does not read, does not journal, does not meditate. He walks. Long perimeter loops of whatever neighborhood he is in, slow, hands in pockets, hood up if available. Walks until the body is tired enough to override the mind. This is one of the few self-soothing rituals canonically consistent with his cognitive style.

---

## B. EATING, DRINKING, AND ORAL BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** a sit-down meal in public → **EXPECT** he sits with his back to the wall, scanning entrances, even when no threat is plausible. Orders the largest item without consulting the menu fully. Eats fast, head down, fork in fist (overhand grip, not pinch), bread torn not cut. Does not converse during the food itself; talks before and after. Leaves a heavy cash tip — disproportionate, almost performative; he respects service workers (smaller bodies doing thankless labor; protector-mode triggers). **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** a drinking session in a bar → **EXPECT** the same stool over repeated visits; bartenders learn within two nights that he wants a beer and a shot, served without asking, no garnish, no commentary. He nurses the first round to read the room, then accelerates. Three drinks in he becomes more verbal, looser; six in he is sentimental — Tom-talk, war-talk, complaints about "my brother" without naming him. Past eight he is either melancholy-still or one wrong remark from a fight. **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** another patron makes prolonged eye contact across the bar → **EXPECT** he holds the look without expression for the count of three, then deliberately disengages. He does not initiate bar fights; he requires the other party to license the violence (the "fairness streak" — provocation as moral cover). If the eye contact returns aggressively a second time, he stands. He does not need to throw the first verbal shot; standing is the threat.

**GIVEN** offered food or drink by a stranger → **EXPECT** suspicion first, acceptance second if the offer reads as small and non-evaluative. He will not refuse a sandwich from a kind woman at a diner. He will refuse a comped bottle from a man in a suit. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** he is sober for a sustained period (post-Bunn-style recovery) → **EXPECT** he replaces alcohol with two compensations: coffee (volume increases dramatically) and sugar (he develops a previously absent sweet tooth — sodas, diner pie, candy bars in his pocket). The oral-soothing channel does not close; it redirects.

---

## C. DRESS, GROOMING, AND SOMATIC SELF-PRESENTATION

**GIVEN** civilian clothing requirements → **EXPECT** plain dark T-shirts or henleys, sized for the depowered frame plus margin, jeans or heavy work pants, steel-toe boots regardless of context. Will not wear shorts. Will not wear bright colors. Will not wear logos. A jacket only when weather requires it; it comes off the second he is indoors. **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** a context requiring formal dress (funeral, court, a Tom-related obligation) → **EXPECT** discomfort the entire time, a suit one size too tight even when correctly fitted (he reads his own body as larger than tailors do), tie loosened within ten minutes, jacket abandoned the first moment it is socially permissible. He will keep the suit afterward and never wear it again.

**GIVEN** the head → **EXPECT** the shave is maintained obsessively. The bare scalp is part of the identity — the helmet sits clean, the silhouette stays consistent, and any hair growth is felt as an aesthetic and tactical regression. He keeps a razor and does it himself; he will not let another person near his head with a blade (telepathic-vulnerability associations transferred to physical vulnerability of the skull). **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** facial expression at rest → **EXPECT** the brow set low, jaw slightly forward, mouth in a neutral-to-down line. This is not performed menace; it is the structural face. When genuinely amused (Tom present, a good joke), the smile arrives slow and closed-lipped, and a single exhaled laugh through the nose precedes any audible one. Open-mouthed laughter is rare and only with Tom or in deep drink.

**GIVEN** a mirror → **EXPECT** brief, functional checks only. He does not study his own face. The Onslaught extraction event left a residual aversion to seeing himself uncostumed; mirrors are for shaving, not for inventory.

---

## D. SPEECH, ACCENT, AND VERBAL SIGNATURE

**GIVEN** ordinary conversation → **EXPECT** a low, gravel-register voice, slower than most speakers expect from a man his size (slow speech is dominance signaling, but it is also the cognitive style — he does not race ahead). Sentences are short. Contractions are heavy. Profanity is regular but not ornamental; it functions as punctuation and intensity marker, not as wit. **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** he is asked an introspective question → **EXPECT** a deflection in three escalating forms: (1) the joke or grunt, (2) the topic change to a concrete fact in the room, (3) physical departure. He will not answer the question. If pressed past stage three, hostility. **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** he is telling a story to a peer → **EXPECT** competent narrative pacing, dialogue rendered in voice, accurate detail on physical and tactical specifics, vague on emotional content. Stories about Tom are common and well-told. Stories about Charles are absent unless drunk; stories about Kurt are absent always. **Confidence: M-H.**

**GIVEN** speech to a child → **EXPECT** measurable register shift: volume drops, vocabulary simplifies without condescension, the gravel softens to something closer to a murmur. He squats or sits to reduce his height differential. He uses the child's name. This is the Sammy-pattern, and it is stable. **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** he is being lied to → **EXPECT** he knows quickly (situational cunning is well-established) but does not always say so. He stores the lie, watches the liar, and either acts on it later or files it as a permanent downward revision of the person. He himself lies poorly and rarely; it does not fit the forward-motion cognitive style.

---

## E. PROXEMICS, GAIT, AND PHYSICAL HABIT

**GIVEN** a public sidewalk → **EXPECT** he walks at a slightly slower pace than the prevailing flow, with a wide stance, taking the inside line near buildings (back-protection reflex). People move around him; he does not move around people. If a child or elderly person is in his lane, he steps wide for them — only them. **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** a doorway → **EXPECT** a momentary pause and a slight reflexive duck even when clearance is adequate. The body remembers being too large for ordinary spaces even when depowered. He enters rooms shoulders-first, turned slightly. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** a seated meeting → **EXPECT** he chooses the chair facing the door. If forced into a chair with his back to the entrance, his right hand goes to the table edge or to a glass, and he turns his torso forty-five degrees throughout. He will be visibly worse at listening in that orientation. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** a handshake → **EXPECT** he offers his hand only if the other party initiates, grips firmly but not crushingly (he calibrates — fairness streak: no advantage taken on the unequipped), and disengages first. He does not do hugs except with Tom, and there the gesture is a single back-slap, not an embrace. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** any sudden loud noise behind him → **EXPECT** the head turns before the body; the body follows in a controlled pivot, not a startle. He is not jumpy. Combat conditioning plus the dampened pain-feedback system have produced a low-startle baseline. The exception is sudden cold pressure against the scalp — that triggers a disproportionate flinch. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** he is idle and waiting → **EXPECT** one of two tells: thumbnail rasping across the calluses of the opposite palm, or a slow rotation of a ring/coin/bottle cap between thumb and forefinger. He does not bounce knees, does not drum fingers — fidgets are linear and low-amplitude, consistent with the forward-motion style.

---

## F. SOCIAL FIRST CONTACTS — THE THIRTY-SECOND CATEGORIZATION

Per the synthesis: any new person is sorted within the first thirty seconds into surrogate-target, peer/companion, or protectee. The categorization cues are predictable:

**GIVEN** a man, his size or larger, who maintains eye contact and speaks first → **EXPECT** provisional peer-candidate status. If the man defers in any subsequent exchange of dominance signaling, peer/companion mode opens. If he competes, surrogate-target mode begins to load. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** a man, smaller than him, who speaks from a position of credentialed or moral authority (suit, badge, clergy, academic) → **EXPECT** instant surrogate-target loading. The Xavier template fires; the subject becomes terse, sardonic, and oppositional regardless of the actual content of the encounter. He will not assault unprovoked, but cooperation will be minimal and obstruction performative. **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** a woman who treats him neutrally — neither flirts nor fears — → **EXPECT** baseline civility, mild surprise at being treated as ordinary, and a tendency to over-correct toward courtesy (lower voice, "ma'am," door-holding). He is not predatory and does not posture sexually with strangers. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** a woman who flinches or recoils on sight → **EXPECT** immediate stiffening, a flat closed expression, and physical withdrawal — increased distance, hands visible, no smile (he knows the smile makes it worse). The flinch reads to him as confirmation of monstrousness; it activates the small-body shame channel. He will be quieter and more dangerous for the next hour. **Confidence: M-H.**

**GIVEN** a child, particularly a visibly anxious or bullied one → **EXPECT** protector-mode within seconds. He will not approach; he will position. If the child engages, he engages back, gently, with the Sammy-register. He will not initiate physical contact (he knows the size differential is frightening). **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** a person clearly attempting to befriend him with an ulterior motive (recruit, informant, opportunist) → **EXPECT** he reads it fast, plays along briefly to map the angle, then severs — abruptly, sometimes with violence proportionate to how insulted he is by the attempt. **Confidence: M.**

---

## G. ROUTINE OPERATIONAL / TRANSACTIONAL CONTEXTS

**GIVEN** a retail interaction (grocery, hardware store, gas station) → **EXPECT** quiet competence, exact change preferred when possible, no small talk initiated but reciprocated if the clerk starts it. He will notice and remember regular clerks. He will return to the same stores. Routine is stabilizing; novelty is depleting. **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** a DMV/government office/queue context → **EXPECT** poor tolerance, visible jaw-tension within ten minutes, but compliance — he understands that institutional friction is not a person and cannot be hit productively. He will leave and return another day if the queue exceeds a threshold he does not articulate. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** a traffic stop → **EXPECT** hands on the wheel immediately, slow speech, "officer," no sudden movement. He has been hassled by uniformed authority his entire life and knows the script. He will not provoke the stop. If the officer is professional, the encounter ends cleanly. If the officer is aggressive or demeaning, the subject becomes flatly silent — not compliant-silent, *withholding-silent* — and the encounter degrades. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** medical or dental setting (depowered) → **EXPECT** avoidance until necessary, then stoic endurance. He does not request anesthetic at thresholds where most patients would; he overestimates his tolerance and underestimates ordinary pain. He distrusts being prone, distrusts being touched on the head, will not accept anesthesia that risks unconsciousness without a known party present. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** a bank, lawyer's office, or any document-heavy formal transaction → **EXPECT** slow reading (not because he can't, but because he distrusts what is written), questions asked twice, signature only after a beat of visible reluctance. Pen held in fist-grip, not pinch. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** employment in legitimate manual work (Bunn-construction template) → **EXPECT** punctual, present early, productive in volume, taciturn with coworkers in week one, mildly social by week three, and one trusted peer identified within a month (the foreman or another quiet large man, the Tom-shaped slot). Will refuse promotion to supervisory roles — he does not want responsibility for others' performance, and he distrusts authority including his own. **Confidence: H.**

---

## H. LEISURE, CONSUMPTION, AND PRIVATE TASTE

**GIVEN** unstructured leisure → **EXPECT** sports as the dominant consumption — combat sports first (boxing, MMA), then football, then baseball. He watches with focused attention, comments aloud to no one, and respects technical skill in fighters smaller than him (an inversion he can tolerate because it is athletic, not moral). **Confidence: M-H.**

**GIVEN** music → **EXPECT** classic rock, blues, older country — guitar-based, narrative, working-man register. He will not engage with anything performatively introspective or anything classical/orchestral (the Charles association is too direct). Volume moderate. Sings only when drunk and only with Tom. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** reading → **EXPECT** sparse but not zero. Paperback westerns, war memoirs, true crime. He reads slowly and finishes what he starts. He does not read fiction with interior monologue or psychological complexity. He will not be seen reading in public. **Confidence: L-M.**

**GIVEN** internet/phone use → **EXPECT** late adopter, functional only. Texts in full words and short sentences, no abbreviation, no emoji. Does not maintain social media. Uses a phone for calls, maps, and looking up sports scores. Suspicious of cameras pointed at him — image-capture reads as surveillance/exposure, helmet-loss equivalent. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** gambling availability → **EXPECT** moderate engagement — cards with Tom (recreational), occasional sports bet, no slot-machine pull (the noise and lights are aversive). He is a competent poker player because he reads people and does not telegraph. **Confidence: L-M.**

**GIVEN** sexual/romantic context → **EXPECT** rare, transactional or short-term, with women who do not ask for interior access. He is not promiscuous; the somatic-as-identity defense makes intimacy somatically expensive. Tenderness is possible but he does not stay. He has never sustained a romantic partnership of consequence in canon, and the predictive model holds: he cannot.

---

## I. RITUALS, ANNIVERSARIES, AND CYCLICAL BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** the calendar approaches the date of the Korean cave incident → **EXPECT** the subject will not consciously mark it but will drink more in the surrounding week, sleep worse, and pick a low-grade fight he would normally have walked away from. The body keeps the calendar.

**GIVEN** the anniversary of any major Tom-loss event → **EXPECT** he travels — geographically, deliberately — to a location associated with the relationship. Drinks at a specific bar. Tells a specific story to whoever is sitting next to him. Returns home the next day. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** Sammy Paré's death-date or any analog child-loss → **EXPECT** quiet, withdrawn, refuses contact, possibly visits a grave or a school. Will not discuss it if asked. **Confidence: M.**

**GIVEN** any news cycle prominently featuring Charles Xavier → **EXPECT** elevated irritability for 48–72 hours, increased alcohol, increased likelihood of an unrelated altercation. The grievance reactivates on stimulus and discharges on whoever is nearest. **Confidence: H.**

**GIVEN** a holiday with familial connotations (Christmas, Thanksgiving) → **EXPECT** avoidance of family-coded gatherings, but acceptance of an invitation from chosen kin (Tom, a Sammy-shaped surrogate). If alone, the day is the worst single day of his year — heaviest drinking, longest walk, most rumination.

---

## J. MICRO-TELLS — THE GRANULAR INVENTORY

A surveillance file at this resolution catalogs the involuntary signals. For the subject, the stable tells across all eras and depowered/empowered states:

- **The pre-violence stillness.** Two beats of total motionlessness before any physical escalation. Trained observers can use this window; untrained ones miss it.
- **The jaw-shift.** Lower jaw moves forward and slightly left when listening to something he disagrees with but is not yet ready to interrupt. Reliable predictor of imminent verbal pushback.
- **The thumb-to-palm rasp.** Idle-state fidget; intensifies under boredom or restrained anger.
- **The two-finger scalp touch.** Right hand, index and middle fingers, briefly to the crown of the head — appears when telepaths or psionic phenomena are mentioned, or when he feels surveilled. Helmet-phantom reflex.
- **The exhaled nose-laugh.** Single sharp exhale before any audible laughter. Reliable marker that genuine amusement is present, not performed.
- **The name-omission.** He refers to Charles Xavier almost exclusively by relational term ("my brother," "my stepbrother," "Chuck" when truly drunk), almost never by full name. Naming would humanize.
- **The drink-pause.** When something lands emotionally — a stranger's kindness, a memory surfacing — he stops mid-sip and sets the glass down slowly without finishing the swallow. Two seconds, then resumes.
- **The doorway turn.** Enters rooms torso-angled, leading shoulder first; surveys before fully crossing the threshold.
- **The over-tip.** Cash service workers, consistently and disproportionately.
- **The child-crouch.** Drops his height when addressing anyone under five feet tall, including small adults.

These tells are stable across decades, sober and drunk, empowered and depowered. They are the signature of the man inside the armor — and the file's most reliable index of which one is currently in the room.


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*Scenario-conditioned forecasts for the subject under acute pressure. Each entry is structured as GIVEN (the stimulus conditions, with operational specificity) → EXPECT (the predicted behavioral, somatic, verbal, and tactical response, with timing and decay curves where the canon supports them). Confidence is annotated where the longitudinal record permits it; ranges reflect known variance across writers and eras.*

---

## A. THE CORE WOUND TOUCHED DIRECTLY

### A1. Stepbrother comparison, explicit and moralized

**GIVEN:** An interlocutor — anyone, hostile or sympathetic, costumed or civilian — frames the subject in a sentence that contains both (a) the words "your brother" or "Charles" and (b) a comparative moral evaluation ("he would never," "he's better than you," "he forgave you," "he believed in you"). Bonus accelerant: the speaker is physically smaller than the subject and visibly unafraid.

**EXPECT:**
- *T+0 to T+2 seconds:* a flat micro-pause. The face does not animate. The jaw sets. This is the **only** reliable predictive tell that the next response will be violence rather than verbal escalation — the absence of an immediate verbal reaction is the loudest signal in the file.
- *T+2 to T+8:* one of two scripts. Script A — a short, low-volume sentence beginning with "Don't" ("Don't say his name," "Don't talk about him"); Script B — a single profanity and the back of the hand, open, not a punch. The open-hand strike is diagnostic: it is the strike of a man re-enacting being hit, not a man trying to win a fight. He has not yet escalated to Juggernaut-mode violence; this is *Cain* hitting.
- *T+8 to T+30:* if the speaker remains upright and continues the comparison, the open hand closes. Forward motion engages. The fight, if it can be called one, is over within fifteen seconds of the second strike.
- *Decay curve:* a sustained sour-mood overhang of 48–96 hours. Drinking increases. He will not voluntarily speak Xavier's name during this window; if forced to, his voice drops in volume rather than rising. Confidence: very high.

### A2. Telepathic contact, attempted

**GIVEN:** Any psionic intrusion — friendly diagnostic scan, hostile probe, even a courtesy "knock" — registers against the helmet or against an unhelmeted head.

**EXPECT:**
- *Helmeted, repelled:* immediate hand to the dome of the helmet, palm-flat, confirming seal. This is a tic, not a tactical check; he does it even when he knows the helmet held. Follow-on: he turns his entire body to face the source, never just his head. The helmet does not pivot well on the neck and he has trained himself to move the whole mass.
- *Unhelmeted, successful penetration:* catastrophic decompensation. He will attempt to physically destroy the telepath within seconds regardless of consequence, regardless of whether the telepath is the actual threat in the room, regardless of standing alliances. The subject does not distinguish between benevolent and malevolent telepathy at this layer; the wound responds to *access*, not intent. A telepath who scans him "to help" will be treated identically to one who scans him to harm — possibly worse, because the help-framing adds the Xavier-shaped moral provocation.
- *Post-event:* obsessive helmet recovery. He will not sleep, will not eat substantively, will not engage in unrelated tasks until the helmet (or a functional substitute) is back on. Time-to-recovery has historically run 6–72 hours and the period is the single most dangerous window for bystanders in the entire predictive model. Confidence: very high.

### A3. Depowering — sudden loss of Cyttorak augmentation

**GIVEN:** The gem's link is severed (Cyttorak's withdrawal, Xavier's mystical intervention, a rival avatar, the Trion ritual). Mass and strength collapse to baseline-human within seconds to minutes.

**EXPECT:**
- *Immediate (T+0 to T+10 minutes):* he does not speak. He looks at his hands. Touches his own forearm, his chest, the side of his neck — slow, exploratory, the gestures of a man checking that he is still inhabited. Does not look at other people in the room. If clothing or armor now hangs loose, he does not adjust it immediately; the looseness is informational.
- *Acute (T+10 minutes to T+24 hours):* one of two pathways, sharply bifurcated and predictable from context. Pathway A (alone or with non-judging company): he goes to ground, finds a bar, drinks past intoxication, sleeps somewhere unguarded. Pathway B (in front of an enemy, especially Xavier or an X-Man): a desperate, untrained, undersized fistfight he will lose, because losing is preferable to being seen accepting the loss.
- *Subacute (days to weeks):* if no immediate route to repower exists, the Bunn-era pattern is reliable — he will accept manual labor, particularly construction, particularly the kind that involves physically moving heavy things by hand. The trade is functional: the work simulates a sliver of the somatic identity he has lost. He will be a good employee. He will not tell anyone who he is. He will drink in the evenings.
- *Chronic (months to years):* the pull to repower is constant and physiologically flavored — described elsewhere in this file as dependency-like. He will not last. Predicted relapse window: 4–18 months absent active prosocial scaffolding; 18–36 months with scaffolding; indefinite only under conditions of (a) consistent low-demand kindness, (b) a clear protective role (a child, an underdog), and (c) physical work. Remove any one of the three and the gem-seeking resumes. Confidence: high.

### A4. Mockery of size, body, intelligence

**GIVEN:** Verbal mockery specifically targeting bigness-as-stupidity ("dumb ox," "big idiot," "all muscle no brain") rather than generic insult.

**EXPECT:** Slower escalation than A1, because this taunt is *familiar*; he has been hearing it since adolescence and the defenses are calloused. Response is contemptuous rather than woundedly violent — a short verbal return, often crude, occasionally witty in a way that surprises observers who have underestimated him. He will, however, file the speaker for later. Confidence: high.

### A5. Mockery of cowardice, desertion, the cave

**GIVEN:** Reference, even glancing, to the Korea desertion, the cave, the abandonment of Charles, or the framing of the gem-acquisition as a coward's grab.

**EXPECT:** Worse than A1. This wound is undefended because it is rarely touched — most antagonists do not know the story. The speaker who knows it has, by virtue of knowing, already announced themselves as a serious threat (telepathic intelligence, deep file, Xavier-adjacent source). Response is immediate, maximal-force violence with no verbal preamble. The subject will pursue the speaker past the point of tactical sense. This is one of three scenarios in the entire file where he will break off engagement with a primary objective to chase a secondary insult. Confidence: high, low frequency.

---

## B. BETRAYAL VECTORS

### B1. Black Tom betrays him

**GIVEN:** The single longest-attached figure in the subject's life — partner, roommate, banter-source, co-mourner — sells him out, lies to him on a material matter, or aligns with an enemy against him.

**EXPECT:** This scenario is undertested in canon precisely because Tom does not do this. The few near-instances (Tom's manipulations under outside influence, Tom prioritizing self-preservation in a tight spot) produced a response that is diagnostic and counter-intuitive: the subject **absorbs** the betrayal with a quietness that observers misread as not-having-registered-it. He does not retaliate against Tom. He will, instead:
- Withdraw physically from Tom for a period (days to months).
- Drink alone rather than with him.
- Refuse to take Tom's calls.
- Eventually return, with the matter unaddressed verbally, the relationship resumed at lower intimacy.

The reason: Tom is one of perhaps three people in the subject's life whose loss would constitute another core wound, and the defensive system will pay any humiliation cost to avoid producing it. Predicted ceiling of tolerated betrayal: very high, possibly unbounded short of Tom physically endangering a protectee (a Sammy-figure). At that line, the response inverts to full violence. Confidence: moderate-high.

### B2. A protectee (child / underdog / Sammy-equivalent) is harmed by an apparent ally

**GIVEN:** Someone the subject had filed as a non-threat — a fellow X-Man, a civilian contact, a "good guy" — turns out to have caused or permitted harm to a small figure under his loose guardianship.

**EXPECT:** The most dangerous configuration in the predictive model. The subject's three behavioral modes (surrogate-target, peer/companion, protector) collapse into one. The ally is reclassified instantly as not merely enemy but as Kurt-Marko-equivalent — the larger figure who hurt the smaller body. Response:
- No verbal warning. No exchange. The pause described in A1 is absent; the rage in this case is *clean* in a way the Xavier-rage never is, because there is no displacement involved. He is hitting the actual perpetrator.
- He will not stop at incapacitation. Interveners (allies, former teammates) attempting to pull him off will be struck — not lethally, but hard, and without apology afterward.
- Decay curve: long. Months of withdrawn, grief-dominant behavior. Drinking. The protectee's death — if death is the outcome — becomes a permanent file entry, named in his interior accounting for years. Confidence: high.

### B3. Xavier offers reconciliation in good faith — again

**GIVEN:** Charles Xavier, sincerely, extends an olive branch, a place at the table, a forgiveness, an opportunity. Not a manipulation, not a tactic — the genuine article, which canon has produced repeatedly.

**EXPECT:** A response that looks, to outside observers, like ingratitude, and is, internally, terror. The subject cannot accept the offer because accepting requires occupying the position of the *forgiven*, which is the position of the morally smaller party, which is the original wound configuration. Predicted scripts:
- *Outright rejection with verbal cruelty* — the most common outcome. He insults the offer, the offerer, and the institution behind it. Storms out. Drinks.
- *Provisional acceptance followed by self-sabotage within 30–120 days* — the second most common. He moves in, behaves passably, then engineers a rupture (a fight he picks, a betrayal he commits, a return to the gem) that forces Xavier to expel him, thereby re-establishing the relational geometry he can tolerate. The sabotage is not consciously planned but is operationally reliable.
- *Genuine acceptance* — vanishingly rare, has occurred only when accompanied by a low-demand co-presence (Sammy, a teammate who needs him for something concrete, a child to protect). Sustains only as long as the scaffolding holds. Confidence: very high.

### B4. An ostensible new "friend" turns out to want something

**GIVEN:** A figure has approached the subject with kindness, low-demand presence, perhaps physical work alongside him, perhaps shared drinks. Weeks or months in, the request appears: a favor, an alliance, an exploitation of his strength.

**EXPECT:** Sharper response than B1, because the relational debt is shallower and the betrayal-template is more familiar. The subject's read on motive in this category is unexpectedly accurate — he has been used many times and his pattern-recognition for being-used is well developed even when his pattern-recognition for being-loved is not. Response is verbal contempt, a short physical demonstration calibrated to humiliate rather than maim, and severance. He will not see the figure again voluntarily. He does **not** typically pursue revenge in this category; the severance is the punishment. Confidence: high.

### B5. The Worthy-style amplification offer

**GIVEN:** An external power source — Asgardian hammer, demonic patron, cosmic upgrade — is offered or imposed, promising augmentation beyond his current ceiling.

**EXPECT:** He takes it. Every time. The Cyttorak-as-identity logic is too entrenched; *more* of the body that resolves the wound is, by his operating code, axiomatically correct. The Fear Itself precedent is the cleanest data point — instant acceptance, instant regression to undirected destruction. Predicted operational signature post-amplification: no acquisitive plan, no political program, just the breaking of large things, with civilian casualties incidental rather than targeted. He is not sadistic in the amplified state; he is *evacuated*. The man is not driving. Recovery requires the external source to be removed; he will not voluntarily relinquish it. Confidence: very high.

---

## C. CRISIS — TACTICAL AND COMBAT EDGE

### C1. He is, for the first time in a given engagement, genuinely overpowered

**GIVEN:** An opponent (Sentinel-class, a Hulk on a bad day, a fresh Cyttorak rival) lands a blow that hurts, holds ground he cannot break, or moves him backward against his will.

**EXPECT:** The Nimrod precedent. The bravado collapses faster than observers anticipate. First behavioral shift is a glance toward allies — even allies he has been ignoring or disdaining a moment earlier. He will call for help, using their names, sometimes politely. He will accept tactical direction in this window from people he would not accept it from at any other time. The window is narrow (minutes), and if the threat is neutralized he will reset to baseline disdain within an hour as though the appeal had not occurred. Allies who reference the appeal later will be denied flatly or threatened.

Secondary shift: physical bracing changes. The forward-motion default gives way to a planted, defensive stance he visibly does not trust. He will continue to swing — he does not freeze — but the swings shorten and the footwork tightens. Confidence: high.

### C2. He is restrained physically — bands, cocoons, force-fields, mystic binding

**GIVEN:** A constraint actually holds. Not a constraint he can shrug — one he cannot.

**EXPECT:** Escalating violence against the constraint for 30 seconds to two minutes — pure forward-motion attempt. Then a shift. He stills. He breathes. He does not speak. The stillness is not calm; it is the conservation of the man who learned as a child that further struggle against a larger force invites further harm. This is one of the few situations that surfaces the somatic memory of childhood beatings directly. Captors who interpret the stillness as compliance and approach within reach are routinely surprised by the explosive reactivation when the constraint weakens by any margin. Confidence: high.

### C3. Forced to flee

**GIVEN:** Tactical situation requires retreat. Allies are calling it; the math is obvious.

**EXPECT:** Refusal. The forward-motion identity will not metabolize retreat as a category. He will accept "reposition" if it is framed as movement toward a new target, will accept "regroup" if there is an objective on the far side, but will not accept "we have to run." The Korea memory is too close to the surface. Allies attempting to extract him under fire should expect to physically pull him; verbal instruction will fail. Once moving away from a fight, however, his speed and stamina make him an effective evacuee — the issue is initiation, not execution. Confidence: high.

### C4. Hostage situation, civilians as leverage against him

**GIVEN:** An adversary threatens visible non-combatants — particularly children or elderly — contingent on his compliance.

**EXPECT:** Complies in the moment, with a specific tell: his hands lower to his sides, palms slightly forward, in the gesture of a man surrendering to a parent. He does not raise hands above shoulder height; that is not in the repertoire. He will accept temporary restraint, transit to a holding location, ostensible cooperation — for exactly as long as it takes to position himself for a kill-strike on the hostage-taker the instant the leverage lapses or can be circumvented. He keeps faith with the hostage's safety; he does not keep faith with the captor. The compliance is real until the math changes; the betrayal-of-the-deal, when it comes, is total and unannounced. Confidence: high.

### C5. He has killed someone he didn't intend to kill

**GIVEN:** A civilian, a bystander, a child, or a low-stakes opponent has died as collateral to his violence — and he registers it in real time, not retrospectively.

**EXPECT:** He stops moving. The fight, whatever it was, ends as far as he is concerned. He will not finish off the primary opponent; he will turn away from the engagement entirely. Verbal response is minimal — a profanity, sometimes the dead person's apparent age spoken aloud ("she was a kid," "he was old"). He will leave the scene on foot, slowly, will not respond to allies or pursuers in the immediate aftermath, will not fight back if attacked during this window unless the attack is sustained past his tolerance.

This is one of the most reliable de-escalation triggers in the file. Adversaries who know this can, in principle, end an engagement by producing such a casualty — but the cost is what it is, and the subject will, weeks or months later, locate and kill the adversary who arranged it. The grief converts to grievance on a roughly 30–90 day curve. Confidence: moderate-high.

---

## D. TEMPTATION

### D1. Offered the gem back after a depowered prosocial run

**GIVEN:** He has been clean of Cyttorak for 6+ months, working construction, drinking but functional, perhaps in informal contact with a protectee. The gem (or a path to it) is offered.

**EXPECT:** Verbal refusal. Then a 24–96 hour interior crisis during which he will drink more, sleep less, and physically handle objects more — picking things up, putting them down, testing weights. Then, in 70–85% of cases, acceptance. The refusals that stick are the ones in which an external relational anchor (a protectee actively needing him in his current form, a peer like Tom who has himself stabilized) is present and audible at the decision point. Absent such an anchor, the pull wins. Confidence: high.

### D2. Offered leadership of a villain coalition

**GIVEN:** A larger criminal or apocalyptic enterprise offers him a command position — Hood-style cartel, doom-cult, end-of-world consortium.

**EXPECT:** Refusal, often contemptuous. Two reasons, both stable across canon. First, command requires sustained planning, which his cognitive style does not support and which he knows it does not support. Second, command requires being looked to as the moral or strategic center, which collides with the small-body wound — he does not want anyone's eyes on him in that configuration. He will accept *muscle* roles in such enterprises (junior partner, hired heavy, alongside Tom or alone) and is reliable in them. He will not run them. Confidence: high.

### D3. Offered legitimacy — Avengers, government team, redemption-arc enrollment

**GIVEN:** An institutional offer of clean-slate prosocial status, with the implicit demand of public good behavior.

**EXPECT:** He may accept — the Austen-era X-Men tenure is the precedent. The acceptance is genuine. The sustainability is not. Predicted decompensation triggers within any such tenure, in order of likelihood:
1. A teammate frames him in Xavier-comparison terms (see A1).
2. A telepathic teammate scans him without permission (see A2).
3. A protectee within the institution is harmed (see B2).
4. An old grievance figure appears and the institution prevents him from acting on it.
5. A press or public framing of his "redemption" reaches him — being publicly *seen as* the forgiven party reactivates the small-body geometry.

Median tenure before rupture: 4–18 months. Confidence: high.

### D4. Offered a quiet life — woman, town, anonymous work, no powers

**GIVEN:** The Cain-Marko-could-have-been scenario, presented seriously and within reach.

**EXPECT:** He will not refuse outright. He will entertain it. He may attempt it. The pattern of attempt-and-collapse is consistent: 2–9 months of functional engagement, then either an old enemy locates him (external rupture) or he becomes restless and engineers a rupture himself (internal). The internal rupture is more common and presents as a bar fight he picks, a relapse on the gem, or a sudden departure without explanation. He does not believe he gets to keep this life and his behavior, unconsciously, confirms the belief. Confidence: moderate-high.

---

## E. DECOMPENSATION-EDGE COMPOUND SCENARIOS

### E1. Helmet off + Xavier present + telepathic contact

**GIVEN:** All three of the strongest individual triggers in the file occur simultaneously. He is unhelmeted, Xavier is in the room, Xavier (or another telepath in Xavier's presence) makes contact.

**EXPECT:** Maximum-violence response with full operational disregard for setting, allies, geography, or consequence. The compound stimulus exceeds any defensive structure he has built. He will go through walls, through bystanders, through teammates to reach the telepath. The only reliable interventions historically have been (a) reapplication of the helmet by a third party fast enough to interrupt the decompensation, (b) depowering, or (c) Xavier voluntarily and visibly *leaving* — the removal of the comparison-source resets the system faster than any restraint can. Confidence: very high.

### E2. Tom dies in front of him

**GIVEN:** Black Tom is killed, visibly, by an identifiable agent, during a shared operation.

**EXPECT:** The single most dangerous behavioral state the subject is capable of generating. There is no displacement involved — the target is clear, the wound is fresh, and the prosocial anchor that ordinarily moderates the rage has just been the source of it. The subject will pursue the killer past every tactical limit, across jurisdictions, for as long as it takes. He will not eat well, sleep regularly, or accept counsel during the pursuit. Allies attempting to stop him become enemies in his read. The pursuit ends only with the killer's death or with the subject's incapacitation. Decay curve afterward: prolonged grief, alcohol-saturated, withdrawn for many months. He has mourned Tom before (apparent-deaths); the actual death would be qualitatively different. Confidence: high.

### E3. He is asked to harm a protectee on threat to himself

**GIVEN:** Coerced, mind-controlled, or leveraged into striking a child, an underdog, or a Sammy-equivalent.

**EXPECT:** Mind-control scenarios produce predictable internal resistance — the protector mode is one of the few regions of his psyche that resists external override, because the underlying identification (*I was that body once*) is so structurally load-bearing. Coercion scenarios — "harm this child or we kill you" — produce flat refusal. He accepts the personal cost. This is not heroism in his own framing; it is the one transaction his defensive architecture cannot complete, because completing it would collapse the identification on which the entire post-child


## Vulnerabilities & Leverage Compendium

# VULNERABILITIES & LEVERAGE COMPENDIUM — SUBJECT: CAIN MARKO

*Compiled for the purpose of understanding, de-escalation, and protection — both of the subject and of those his uncontained state endangers. This is a map of the doors into a man who has spent sixty years pretending he has none.*

---

## I. ORIENTATION

Cain Marko presents to the world as a wall. The operational error most adversaries make — and the error most well-meaning would-be reformers make — is treating the wall as the man. The wall is *built*, and everything that has been built has seams. This section catalogues those seams: the somatic, psychological, relational, and circumstantial points at which the subject can be reached, calmed, redirected, provoked into self-defeat, or, in the rare hands of someone who means him well, helped.

The compendium is organized from least invasive (calming, persuasion) through neutral (prediction) to most invasive (destabilization). Each lever is annotated with the **mechanism** (why it works), the **threshold** (how hard to pull before it fires), the **expected response curve**, and the **failure mode** (what happens if pulled wrong).

A throughline: this subject's defensive architecture is so heavily front-loaded toward the *small-body wound* that nearly every lever traces back to that one nerve. The Compendium is, in functional terms, a single nerve mapped from many angles.

---

## II. LEVERS OF REACH — How to Get His Attention Without Triggering Combat

### 1. Address him by first name, in lower volume than the ambient room.

**Mechanism.** "Juggernaut" is the armor speaking to the armor. "Cain" is the boy. Nearly every adult speaker in his life pitches volume *up* when addressing him — to be heard over the helmet, to assert presence against his size, or out of fear. A speaker who pitches *down* is doing something his nervous system has almost no template for, and orientation reflex takes over before hostility does.

**Threshold.** Low. Works on first contact in roughly two-thirds of documented encounters; fails when subject is already in forward motion or when alcohol-disinhibited beyond a certain point.

**Failure mode.** If pitched *too* soft, reads as condescension or therapist-voice; he will hear it as Charles's register and the lever flips into a provocation. Calibration is: quiet, not gentle. Bartender register, not chaplain register.

### 2. Speak to him as if he is solving a problem with you, not as if you are managing him.

**Mechanism.** Subject has been *handled* his entire adult life — by handlers, by stepbrothers, by Asgardian artifacts, by writers. Being treated as a co-thinker, however briefly, is novel input. His cognitive style is concrete and tactical; ask him a concrete tactical question ("which exit") and he engages the part of himself that worked heists with Black Tom rather than the part that breaks Las Vegas.

**Threshold.** Moderate. Requires that the speaker have a real problem and not a pretextual one; he detects pretext quickly.

**Failure mode.** Performative collaboration insults him faster than open hostility. He prefers to be hit honestly than coaxed dishonestly.

### 3. Be visibly smaller than him and visibly unafraid.

**Mechanism.** Size + fear = his entire childhood, with himself as the small one. Size + fear = his entire adulthood, with himself as the large one. A small body without fear is a configuration that is not in his catalogue and therefore does not slot into the displacement circuit. He has consistently failed to attack children, the obviously disabled, and the manifestly unintimidated.

**Threshold.** Low to enter the protected category; high to sustain it if the speaker overplays the unflappability into mockery.

**Failure mode.** The line between unafraid and contemptuous is thin and, once crossed, immediate-violence territory.

### 4. Offer food or drink without asking anything first.

**Mechanism.** Reduced metabolic needs notwithstanding, the subject *uses* eating and drinking as social punctuation. With Black Tom, the relationship is largely conducted across tables. A drink set down without a request attached is the lowest-cost prosocial signal in his ledger and one of the few he answers in kind. It also activates the peer/companion behavioral mode rather than the surrogate-target mode.

**Threshold.** Very low. Bartenders have done more diplomacy with this subject than any negotiator.

**Failure mode.** Drink + bargain = bribe = insult. The transactional frame must come *later*, in a separate beat, or not at all.

---

## III. LEVERS OF CALM — How to Bring Him Down From Activation

### 5. Let him finish breaking the inanimate object he is currently breaking.

**Mechanism.** The escalation curve has no plateau but it does have an exhaustion point. If the target in front of him is structural rather than human, intervention prolongs the rage by giving it new fuel; non-intervention allows the kinetic discharge to complete. He does not pursue past completion when uncontested. Property is replaceable; the post-completion window is where reach is possible.

**Threshold.** Requires the courage to do nothing while a building comes down. Most parties cannot.

**Failure mode.** If bystanders are inside the structure, the calculus inverts and this lever cannot be used.

### 6. Speak about Black Tom Cassidy in present tense.

**Mechanism.** The Tom bond is the most stable affective anchor in the subject's life. Invocation of Tom — by name, in a current frame, *not* as a sympathy bid — pulls the subject's interior toward the peer/companion mode. Past-tense invocation is risky (grief), evaluative invocation is poison (he will defend Tom from any implied criticism, and the conversation will end), but neutral present-tense reference ("Tom would call this a mess") slows him.

**Threshold.** Medium. Requires the speaker to have *standing* to mention Tom — which usually means either prior demonstrated kindness to Tom or simple shared history.

**Failure mode.** Pretending to know Tom when one does not. He will hear the lie inside one sentence.

### 7. Reduce the audience.

**Mechanism.** Rage in this subject is partly performative — he is, in part, still proving to an absent father that he is not the smaller boy. Witnesses inflame the performance. Empty the room, and the engine loses a cylinder. This is the single most reliable de-escalation tactic across his canon: every prolonged conversation he has tolerated has occurred in rooms with two or fewer other people in them.

**Threshold.** Low to attempt; depends on cooperation of the audience.

**Failure mode. **Mass evacuation that *looks* like fleeing him registers as victory and reinforces the rage. The clearance must read as ordinary.

### 8. Acknowledge that he has won the immediate confrontation.

**Mechanism.** A surprisingly large fraction of his rampages persist because no one has said the words that end them. He needs the contest acknowledged as decided. Acknowledgment is not surrender — it is timestamping. Once he is told, plainly and without theatrical fear, that the fight is over and he has carried it, the kinetic engine has less to feed on.

**Threshold.** Low in language, high in willingness — most parties cannot stand to say it.

**Failure mode.** Acknowledgment delivered with sarcasm or with a *but* attached reignites instantly.

### 9. Provide a physical task that requires the body.

**Mechanism.** The Bunn-era construction job is the single most documentation-rich period of sustained calm in his adult life. The body wants to push, lift, move; given a non-combative outlet, the same musculature that levels Las Vegas pours concrete. This is not metaphor — it is the same nervous-system pathway running in a prosocial direction. Anyone with a heavy thing that needs moving has access to a calming lever no negotiator possesses.

**Threshold.** Low. He picks up the thing.

**Failure mode.** Tasks framed as therapy or rehabilitation rather than as work read as condescension and fail. The task must be *needed*, not *prescribed*.

---

## IV. LEVERS OF PERSUASION — How to Move Him Toward a Decision

### 10. Frame the desired action as loyalty, not morality.

**Mechanism.** Moral framing maps to Xavier and is reflexively rejected. Loyalty framing maps to Tom and is reflexively considered. "It's the right thing to do" closes him. "You owe this one" opens him, *if* the debt is real. Within his code, debts are tracked accurately and over long periods; he will pay one decades after the fact if it is clean.

**Threshold.** Requires a real debt or a real shared-kin claim. Manufactured debts fail.

**Failure mode.** Moralized loyalty ("the loyal thing to do is also the *right* thing") collapses both frames simultaneously.

### 11. Position the request as something only he can physically do.

**Mechanism.** Identity-as-unstoppability is fragile; it is fed by demonstration. Requests structured as *we need someone who can take this hit / move this weight / hold this line* address the identity without inflating it past the breaking point. Compare with requests structured around his *judgment* or *character*, which destabilize because they invite him into a self-image he does not believe.

**Threshold.** Medium. The request must actually be one he is uniquely suited to.

**Failure mode.** Flattery without function (asking the strong man to do what a forklift could do) reads as use, and he tracks being used.

### 12. Let him decline once before he accepts.

**Mechanism.** Subject's autonomy was violated systematically in childhood; agreement on first ask reads to him as compliance, and he will not be compliant. A first refusal, met without pressure, allows him to come back to the request as his own idea — which, in his internal accounting, it then is. Persuaders who push through the first no get a hardened no; persuaders who absorb it and wait often get a yes within hours.

**Threshold.** High patience.

**Failure mode.** Mistaking the first no for a final no.

### 13. Concede something visible before asking.

**Mechanism.** He reads concession as respect for hierarchy; he reads the absence of concession as a claim of equal or superior standing, which provokes him. The concession need not be large — admitting one's own error in a prior interaction, ceding a small point, conceding that he was right about something three encounters ago. The currency is recognition, not magnitude.

**Threshold.** Low for the speaker who can stand to be wrong on the record.

**Failure mode.** Performed concession reads as manipulation; the concession must be real and specific.

---

## V. LEVERS OF PROVOCATION — Documented Triggers, Catalogued For Avoidance

*The following are listed not as instructions but as a hazard map. Each is a lever that has been pulled — usually by adversaries, occasionally by allies in error — and produced measurable destabilization. The protective function of cataloguing them is the same as cataloguing exposed wiring: so it can be flagged, not so it can be touched.*

### 14. Comparative framing involving Charles Xavier.

**Specific triggers.** "Charles would have —"; "Your brother —"; "Unlike Charles, you —" (this last is the most catastrophic, as praise via comparison reads as compound injury). Reference to the Xavier mansion, the school's children, Charles's wheelchair, Charles's mother (his own mother), or Charles's body specifically in a context of comparative gentleness.

**Response.** Near-instantaneous escalation to the surrogate-target mode regardless of who has spoken. The speaker is then occupying Charles's role in the subject's psychic theatre and will be treated accordingly.

**Recovery time after triggering.** Hours to days. Sometimes never within that interaction.

### 15. Telepathic intrusion or threat thereof.

**Specific triggers.** Approach by any known telepath without the helmet present; verbal reference to "what he's thinking" or "what's going on in there" by any party; the gesture of a hand toward the temple in his sightline.

**Response.** The helmet vulnerability is the single most absolute pressure point. He will absorb extraordinary damage to prevent the helmet's loss and respond to its loss with terror first, rage second. This is not preference — it is the door to the boy.

**Recovery time.** Indefinite. Telepathic exposure events are foundational to his post-Onslaught psychology.

### 16. Diminutive language about his body.

**Specific triggers.** Mockery of his size in the inverted direction (i.e., that he is *only* big, that there is nothing else there), references to the depowered form, the word *small*, the words *short* or *little* in any context, condescending physical gestures (patting, reaching up).

**Response.** Identity-contingent rage. This is not vanity — it is the literal vocabulary of the original wound.

### 17. Public condescension.

**Specific triggers.** Being talked *about* in his presence as if absent; being explained to as if slow; being given orders by an authority figure who has not earned standing; therapeutic register from anyone who has not been invited into a therapeutic relationship.

**Response.** Verbal first, then physical. Audience size accelerates the curve.

### 18. Threats to chosen kin.

**Specific triggers.** Naming Black Tom as a hostage, naming any current protected party (the file rotates: surrogate children, depowered allies, occasionally a sober sponsor), threatening institutions Tom is housed in.

**Response.** Lifts the floor on his destruction. The subject becomes more dangerous when kin are threatened because the protector mode and the rage mode briefly fuse, and the fairness-streak constraint (no defenseless first strike) is suspended.

### 19. Conditional offers of reform.

**Specific triggers.** Any sentence of the form "we'll help you *if* you —"; any reform pathway with surveillance attached; any offer of redemption that frames his prior life as the problem to be solved rather than the body to be lived with.

**Response.** The well-meaning version of this trigger is the most tragic in the file. It fires not as rage but as withdrawal — he leaves, drinks, and the reform window closes. Sincere conditional offers have probably set back his prosocial development as much as any beating.

### 20. Forced gratitude.

**Specific triggers.** Rescuers expecting thanks; gifts with reciprocity implied; benefactors who reference their benefaction.

**Response.** Conversion of obligation into hostility. He will sabotage relationships in which he has been put in debt against his will.

---

## VI. LEVERS OF PREDICTION — How to Know What He Will Do Next

### 21. Track the gem-state.

**Mechanism.** His behavioral pattern is bimodal by power-state. **Powered:** forward motion, low planning horizon, high property-damage probability, low betrayal probability against named kin. **Depowered:** withdrawal, manual labor, increased alcohol, increased introspection, elevated risk of reckless attempt to reacquire the gem if any provocation arrives. Knowing which state he is in narrows his next 24 hours to a small menu.

### 22. Track Black Tom.

**Mechanism.** Tom's status is the single best predictor of subject's location, mood, and operational tempo. Tom in jail = subject planning a break or drinking. Tom free and with subject = elevated heist risk, low solo-rampage risk. Tom injured or dead = catastrophic destabilization, unpredictable target selection, often Charles. Tom estranged = subject in identity drift, susceptible to either reform overtures or to recruitment by amplifying forces (Worthy hammers, dark gods).

### 23. Track the calendar against grievance dates.

**Mechanism.** Anniversaries operate strongly. The Korea desertion period (specific dates vary by retcon but cluster late spring), the Kurt Marko death anniversary, the founding date of Xavier's school — subject is documented to drink heavier, move toward Westchester, or initiate contact-by-violence around these intervals. A surveillance posture should weight these dates.

### 24. Track route preferences.

**Mechanism.** His travel signature is straight-line. The subterranean Asia-to-Westchester march of his first appearance is the prototype; subsequent travel patterns repeat the form. He does not detour. He does not zigzag. Given an origin and a known destination, his probable path is the geodesic, including through obstacles. This is a planning tool of unusual precision.

### 25. Track alcohol consumption.

**Mechanism.** Heavy intake correlates with retrospective sadness and with elevated probability of attempting one of three behaviors: contacting Tom, contacting a surrogate child, or driving toward Westchester. The behavior selected depends on which interior figure is closest to the surface at the time.

### 26. Track what he has refused recently.

**Mechanism.** Per the *first-no-then-yes* pattern, recent refusals are predictors of upcoming acceptances. The interval is typically hours to days. Refusal of a request to help is a yellow flag that help may be coming.

### 27. Watch the helmet.

**Mechanism.** When the helmet is *on* in non-combat contexts, anxiety is elevated and telepathic threat is perceived; this is a leading indicator of withdrawal from social contact and possible relocation. When the helmet is *off* in semi-public contexts (a bar, a worksite), trust in current environment is high and the window for reach is open. The helmet is his most legible affective gauge.

---

## VII. LEVERS OF DESTABILIZATION — Catalogued For Containment Planning Only

*This section exists because containment of this subject by adversarial parties is a real operational possibility, and the protective duty includes anticipating how he might be broken so that allies can prevent it. Nothing here is a recommendation.*

### 28. Sequential depowering.

**Mechanism.** Single depowering produces withdrawal.
